# Yozuv — Полный аудит кода
_2026-06-28 · 117 агентов Opus 4.8 (80 finder + 36 verify + 1 synthesis) · 5.1M токенов · 14 мин_

## Базовая проверка (запущено вручную)
- Backend `pytest`: **34/34 OK**
- Backend import `app.main`+`bot.main`: **OK**
- Frontend `tsc --noEmit`: **OK (exit 0)**
- Frontend `next lint`/`build` локально не запускается: отсутствует `@next/env` -> неполный `node_modules` (артефакт окружения, не баг кода). На Vercel чистая установка = соберётся.
- Миграции: 25 alembic-версий, Dockerfile есть

## Статистика аудита
- Областей проверено: **80** (58 working / 22 partial)
- Всего находок: **235**
- Подтверждено high/critical (после adversarial verify): **32**

## Системный обзор (synthesis)

# Yozuv Codebase — Systemic Review

## 1. Overall Verdict

**Broadly working, not yet shippable without fixes.** The codebase is coherent and functional end-to-end across the vast majority of areas: tests pass (34/34), both app and bot import cleanly, frontend typechecks. Authorization scoping is consistently correct in nearly every router. However, there is a small cluster of **genuine production blockers** — primarily money/payment correctness, a cross-tenant PII leak, and double-booking races — that must be fixed before this can safely take real customers' money and appointments. None are architectural rewrites; all are localized fixes.

## 2. Systemic Themes (cross-cutting)

- **Async/sync mismatch (pervasive).** The app is fully synchronous SQLAlchemy, yet many route handlers and bot handlers are declared `async def`, so blocking DB/file/HTTP I/O runs on the event loop. Seen in `core:config+db+deps`, `router:payments`, `router:files`, `router:admin`, `bot:mybookings+owner`. Also `asyncpg` is a dead dependency (`infra:docker+reqs`). Not a correctness bug per se, but a latency/throughput timebomb and the root cause of `event_bus`'s cross-thread `put_nowait` unreliability.

- **Payment/money correctness (highest business risk).** Webhooks complete subscriptions without validating paid amount (`router:payments`), don't enforce idempotency under concurrent retries (`service:payment_service`, `models:payment` non-unique `external_id`), and payment completion *crashes* for owners with no Telegram ID — a fully supported auth mode (`service:payment_service`). On the frontend, promo percent+amount discounts silently combine despite "exclusive" UI claim (`fe:dash-promo+reviews`), and revenue analytics plots booking *counts* not revenue (`fe:dash-analytics`).

- **Timezone handling — correct at the core, fragile at the edges.** `util:clock` and the reminder task are deliberately and correctly TZ-aware (Asia/Tashkent). But several consumers regress: cancel-window uses server-local time (`booking_service`), `trial_expiry_warnings` mis-reads naive `expires_at`, and multiple frontend `created_at` slices show wrong local dates (`fe:dash-promo`, `fe:dash-analytics`, `fe:dash-shell`).

- **Concurrency races on check-then-write.** Recurring bookings lack the advisory lock the single-booking path has (`router:bookings`); promo `max_uses` can be exceeded; first-time review/waitlist/client inserts raise unhandled `IntegrityError` → 500 (`router:reviews`, `service:waitlist_service`, `router:auth`). The single-booking advisory-lock path is the one place this is done right — the pattern just isn't applied everywhere.

- **Authorization is strong; one hole.** Nearly every router correctly scopes by `get_owned_business`. The single exception is a real IDOR: `client_detail` leaks any client's PII cross-tenant (`router:clients`).

- **Silent error-swallowing degrades observability.** `notification_service` swallows all send failures, making broadcast success/failure stats meaningless; `audit_service`'s bare `except: pass` and mis-scoped try/except defeat its own safety guarantee; multiple frontend loaders swallow fetch errors into false empty states (`fe:dash-clients`, `fe:dash-promo`).

- **Missing input validation → 500s instead of 422.** Negative/zero prices and durations (`router:services`), duplicate schedule days, unbounded strings exceeding DB column limits — recurring across `router:schedule`, `router:services`, `core:schemas`.

## 3. Top Blockers (ranked)

1. **Payment completion crashes for owners with no Telegram ID** — `service:payment_service` [high]. A fully-supported auth mode (Google/password owners) cannot complete payment or be refunded. Directly breaks revenue for a whole user class.
2. **Webhook completes subscription without validating paid amount** — `router:payments` [high]. Subscriptions can activate for the wrong/under-paid amount; combined with non-unique `external_id` (`models:payment`) and unlocked idempotency check (`service:payment_service`), retries can double-activate. Money integrity.
3. **`client_detail` cross-tenant PII leak (IDOR)** — `router:clients` [high]. Any owner can read any other business's client PII by ID. Privacy/compliance blocker.
4. **`create_recurring` double-booking race** — `router:bookings` [high]. No advisory lock / `SELECT FOR UPDATE`, unlike the single-booking path. Produces real double-bookings.
5. **Production secret-key check reads `os.getenv('APP_ENV')` not the parsed field** — `core:config+db+deps` [high]. The guard can be silently skipped, allowing a weak JWT signing key in production. Auth-wide security.
6. **Promo percent + amount discounts silently combine** — `fe:dash-promo+reviews` [high]. UI says exclusive; backend applies both → unintended free/over-discounted bookings. Money leak.
7. **SSE stream pins a DB connection for its whole lifetime** — `router:business` [high]. Pool exhaustion under modest concurrent dashboard usage; can take down the API.
8. **1-hour reminder silently skipped if a beat run is missed** — `task:reminders` [high]. Core product promise (reminders) fails silently.
9. **024 migration backfill can violate `UNIQUE(provider,subject)` on duplicate phones** — `migrations:014-025` [high]. Can abort the upgrade on real production data with duplicate phones (uniqueness not enforced until 027).
10. **Revenue analytics chart plots booking counts, not revenue** — `fe:dash-analytics` [high]. Owners make decisions on misleading money numbers.

## 4. What Works Well

- **Authorization & tenant scoping** — consistent `get_owned_business` discipline across virtually all routers; verified Telegram initData on public routes (`util:telegram_webapp` is correct and secure).
- **Pure utility/rendering layers** — `service:pdf_service`, `service:qr_service`, `util:clock`, `util:htmlsafe`, `util:uz_geo`, `util:auth`, `util:slots` (core math), `util:google_oauth` (crypto correct).
- **Single-booking concurrency** — `service:booking_service`'s Postgres advisory-lock approach to the empty-slot race is genuinely sound and is the model the rest of the code should follow.
- **Data model & migrations** — `models:booking`, `models:payment`, `models:misc`, `models:settings+enums` are well-formed; migrations 001-013 are production-safe with correct `server_default` backfills; `infra:alembic-env` is sound.
- **Frontend infrastructure** — `fe:lib-api` (401 coalescing/refresh), `fe:auth-callback`, `fe:lib-platform+utils`, `comp:nav`, landing components, `fe:root`.
- **App wiring** — `core:main+obs+celery` lifespan/CORS/Sentry/Celery setup is clean.

## 5. Risk Hotspots (partial/broken status + clustered findings)

- **`router:payments` / `service:payment_service` / `models:payment`** — the densest cluster of high/medium money-integrity defects (amount validation, idempotency, Telegram-ID crash, blocking I/O). This is the single most dangerous subsystem.
- **`router:clients` (partial)** + **`fe:dash-clients` (partial)** — IDOR on the backend; on the frontend, `total_spent`, VIP, and "new" filters are all permanently dead because the backend never sends the fields. Whole CRM feature surface is half-wired.
- **`fe:dash-analytics` (partial)** — headline revenue chart and period-over-period % are both computing the wrong thing; renders fine but lies.
- **`bot:booking` / `bot:mybookings+owner` (partial)** — multi-staff slot flow is broken (slots ignore chosen staff), owner_confirm can resurrect cancelled/completed bookings, unescaped service names in HTML notifications, sync DB in async handlers.
- **`comp:booking-sheets` (partial)** — slot picker diverges from backend availability rules (exact start-time match, counts cancelled/completed as busy, ignores duration) — offers slots the backend rejects and hides free ones.
- **`fe:dash-services+staff` / `fe:dash-schedule` / `fe:dash-promo+reviews` (partial)** — staff create-then-assign orphans records on partial failure; schedule breaks can't be edited; promo discount combination + missing review-replies feature.
- **`service:event_bus` / `service:notification_service` / `util:ratelimit` (partial)** — cross-thread queue delivery, meaningless broadcast stats, X-Forwarded-For-spoofable rate limit with unbounded memory growth. All degrade gracefully but are unreliable.
- **`util:slots`** — staff-unaware and ignores deactivation; offers past times for the current day (compounds the bot/booking-sheet issues above).

**Cross-cutting note:** the `partial` ratings cluster heavily in two zones — the **payment subsystem** (money correctness) and the **dashboard/bot booking UX** (slot-picking divergence from backend truth). Fixing the slot-availability logic in one shared place and hardening the webhook/payment path would clear most of the `partial` ratings at once.

## Подтверждённые high/critical находки (verified=real)

### 1. [high] create_recurring has no advisory lock and no SELECT FOR UPDATE — double-booking race
- **Область:** `router:bookings`  ·  **Файл:** `backend/app/routers/bookings.py L572-586`  ·  **Категория:** race
- **Проблема:** Unlike create_owner_booking (line 167 acquire_slot_lock + line 181 with_for_update) and update_booking (line 286/298), the recurring loop does its conflict check with a plain conflict_q.first() (line 586) and never calls acquire_slot_lock. The module's own docstring (acquire_slot_lock, booking_service.py:35) explains that SELECT FOR UPDATE cannot lock an empty slot, so two concurrent requests targeting the same destination slot (e.g. a recurring create racing a single owner-create, or two recurring creates) both pass the conflict check and both insert, producing overlapping bookings. Fix: call acquire_slot_lock(db, business.id, slot_date, body.start_time) before each iteration's conflict query and add .with_for_update() to conflict_q, mirroring create_owner_booking.
- **Проверка:** Confirmed against the actual code in D:\yozuv\backend\app\routers\bookings.py.

create_recurring (lines 553-665) performs its overlap check in the loop at lines 615-629 with a plain `conflict = conflict_q.first()` (line 629) — no `.with_for_update()` and no advisory lock. It then inserts bookings (lines 642-656) and commits once after the loop (line 657). `acquire_slot_lock` is imported (line 31) but never called anywhere in this function.

The two sibling write paths both guard the identical race:
- create_owner_booking: `acquire_slot_lock(...)` at line 210, then `conflict_q.with_for_update().first()` at line 224.
- update_booking: `acquire_slot_lock(...)` at line 329, then `.with_for_update().first()` at lines 341-342.

The lock helper's own docstring (D:\yozuv\backend\app\services\booking_service.py:34-42) states the exact failure mode: "SELECT FOR UPDATE only locks rows that already exist; for an empty slot there is nothing to lock, which lets two writers pass the conflict check at the same time and both insert. The advisory lock serializes them on (business_id, date, start_time) until the transaction commits."

So two concurrent requests targeting the same destination slot — a recurring create racing an owner create, or two recurring creates — can both run their SELECT, both see no conflict, and both INSERT, producing overlapping bookings. This violates the product's core no-double-booking invariant. The proposed fix (call acquire_slot_lock before each iteration's conflict query and add .with_for_update()) is correct and mirrors the other two endpoints.

Severity high is justified: it breaks the central data-integrity invariant of a booking product, and the codebase already treats this exact race as serious enough to lock elsewhere. It is somewhat mitigated by being owner-only (dashboard), which narrows the concurrency window versus the public flow, but the defect is genuine.

### 2. [high] SSE stream pins a DB connection for the entire connection lifetime (pool exhaustion)
- **Область:** `router:business`  ·  **Файл:** `backend/app/routers/business.py L381-425`  ·  **Категория:** reliability
- **Проблема:** notifications_stream depends on get_owned_business_download, which Depends(get_db). FastAPI keeps the get_db generator (and thus the checked-out SQLAlchemy Session/connection) open until the StreamingResponse finishes. An SSE connection stays open for hours, so each open dashboard tab holds one connection from the pool (pool_size=20, max_overflow=10) even though the stream body never touches the DB again after auth. A few dozen concurrent dashboards exhaust the pool and block all other requests. Fix: resolve auth/business in a short-lived session that is closed before the stream starts (e.g. open a SessionLocal() inside the dependency, fetch the business, close it, and pass only the business id/object out), or make notifications_stream not depend on a request-scoped get_db at all — capture business.id and release the session before yielding.
- **Проверка:** Verified the full chain and the finding holds.

1) backend/app/database.py:10-27 — synchronous SQLAlchemy engine, pool_size=20 + max_overflow=10 (30 connections max). get_db() yields a SessionLocal() and only closes it in the finally block.

2) backend/app/routers/business.py:381-425 — notifications_stream depends on get_owned_business_download (Depends, line 386) and returns a StreamingResponse whose body is gen() (lines 401-413). gen() is an infinite stream driven by subscribe(business.id).

3) backend/app/services/event_bus.py:55-78 — subscribe() is a `while True` async generator (30s heartbeat ping, otherwise blocks on q.get()). It never terminates on its own, so the SSE connection stays open for the entire client lifetime (hours).

4) backend/app/deps.py:35-58 (get_owned_business_download) and backend/app/utils/auth.py:87-98 (get_user_from_token) — the dependency runs only read SELECTs (User lookup, Business lookup). There is no db.commit() or db.rollback(). With autocommit=False (database.py:18), the Session opens a transaction on first query and holds the checked-out DBAPI connection open until the Session is closed.

Because FastAPI/Starlette (fastapi>=0.110 per backend/requirements.txt:1) tears down `yield` dependencies only AFTER the response — including a StreamingResponse — has fully completed, get_db's `finally: db.close()` does not run until gen() finishes. Since gen()/subscribe() never finishes, the Session (and its open read transaction holding a pooled connection) is pinned for the whole SSE lifetime even though the stream body never touches the DB again after auth.

Net effect: each open dashboard tab consumes one of the 30 sync pool connections indefinitely. ~30 concurrent open dashboards exhaust the pool and block all other (sync) DB-backed requests until QueuePool timeout. The mechanism, the cited location, and the proposed fix (resolve auth in a short-lived session/commit-or-close before yielding, or pass only business.id out) are all accurate.

Severity high is appropriate: full pool exhaustion is a hard outage affecting every endpoint, and long-lived SSE connections accumulate exactly the kind of idle holders that trigger it. The only mitigating factor is that it requires reaching ~30 concurrent open dashboards, which for an early-stage product may not be imminent — but it is a genuine latent reliability defect, not a non-issue.

### 3. [high] client_detail leaks any client's PII across tenants (IDOR)
- **Область:** `router:clients`  ·  **Файл:** `backend/app/routers/clients.py L71-98`  ·  **Категория:** security
- **Проблема:** GET /clients/{client_id} loads the client with `db.query(Client).filter(Client.id == client_id).first()` and returns first_name, last_name, phone, telegram_id and birthday WITHOUT verifying the client has any booking at the caller's business. The bookings/stats/block sub-queries are business-scoped, so for an unrelated client they come back empty, but the top-level `client` object is still returned in full. An owner of business A can enumerate UUIDs (or reuse a UUID seen elsewhere) and read the PII of any client in the system, including their Telegram id and phone. This is exactly the leak the sibling helper `_client_in_business_or_404` (lines 125-141) was written to prevent — but client_detail doesn't call it. Fix: replace the line-71 lookup with `c = _client_in_business_or_404(db, business.id, client_id)` so the client must have at least one booking at this business before any data is returned (and it preserves the existing 404 behavior).
- **Проверка:** Confirmed by reading backend/app/routers/clients.py lines 68-125. In client_detail, line 74 does `c = db.query(Client).filter(Client.id == client_id).first()` — a global, NON-business-scoped lookup. If a Client row exists for that UUID, lines 93-101 return its PII (first_name, last_name, phone, telegram_id, birthday) unconditionally. Only the bookings (lines 77-82), stats, and block sub-queries are scoped to `business.id`; for an unrelated client those come back empty/None, but the top-level `client` object is still fully populated. The caller is an authenticated business owner (get_owned_business in deps.py lines 25-32 resolves the business via `owner_id == user.id`), so any owner can supply or reuse any Client UUID and read another tenant's client PII — a cross-tenant IDOR. The sibling helper `_client_in_business_or_404` (lines 128-144) was written for exactly this purpose; its docstring states the check exists to avoid "a privacy leak," and it is correctly applied in patch_client (line 158) and (per finding) the block path, but client_detail omits it. The proposed fix — replacing the line-74 lookup with `c = _client_in_business_or_404(db, business.id, client_id)` — is correct and preserves the 404 contract. Severity high is justified: real PII (phone, telegram_id) exposed to any authenticated owner. The only mitigating factor is that client_id is a 128-bit random UUID (not sequentially enumerable), but UUIDs routinely leak via URLs, the list_clients response, and logs, and the team already treats this exposure as a privacy defect.

### 4. [high] Payme/Click webhook completes the subscription without validating the paid amount
- **Область:** `router:payments`  ·  **Файл:** `backend/app/routers/payments.py L440-450, 474-480`  ·  **Категория:** data-integrity
- **Проблема:** Both webhooks call complete_transaction_and_notify(db, tx) which activates a full subscription using tx.amount, but never compares the amount reported in the callback to tx.amount. A buggy/partial gateway callback (or an underpaid Payme transaction) would still activate the full plan. For Click the signed sign_string covers amount so tampering is blocked, but the handler still never asserts callback amount == tx.amount. Fix: validate the callback amount equals the expected tx.amount before completing; reject/ignore otherwise.
- **Проверка:** Confirmed against the actual code. In backend/app/routers/payments.py, payme_webhook (lines 427-455) completes the tx whenever method=="PerformTransaction", and click_webhook (lines 458-489) completes whenever action=="1" after signature check — both then call complete_transaction_and_notify(db, tx). That function in backend/app/services/payment_service.py:318-324 unconditionally sets tx.status=COMPLETED and calls activate_subscription(db, tx.business_id, plan, tx.amount) using the amount/plan stored on the tx at creation time. Neither webhook ever reads the provider-reported amount from the callback body and compares it to tx.amount. The only reference to the body's amount in the whole file is line 416 inside _verify_click_signature, where it is used solely to reconstruct the MD5 sign_string (lines 418-422) — there is no equality assertion against tx.amount. The transaction is located via _find_tx_id (lines 378-388), a blind regex over json.dumps(body) returning the first UUID, with no amount binding. The test (backend/tests/test_booking_deposit.py:79-93) confirms the Payme callback shape is {"method":"PerformTransaction","params":{"account":{"id":tx.id}}} with no amount the handler validates. So a partial/buggy gateway callback or an underpaid Payme transaction that passes Basic-auth still activates the full MONTHLY/YEARLY plan. This is a genuine, standard payment-control gap (amount reconciliation), independently re-verified here and already corroborated as existing audit finding #3 (docs/AUDIT_FINDINGS.md:77-81, verified high). Caveat on exploitability the finding itself acknowledges: external forgery requires the gateway secret (Payme static key for Basic auth; click_secret_key for the MD5 signature), so this is not an unauthenticated bypass — but the underpayment/partial-callback scenario does not require attacker-held secrets, and the missing reconciliation is a real defect. The proposed fix (reject when provider amount != tx.amount, keep COMPLETED short-circuit for idempotency) is correct and actionable. Severity high retained, consistent with the standing audit.

### 5. [high] Payment completion crashes for owners with no Telegram ID
- **Область:** `service:payment_service`  ·  **Файл:** `backend/app/services/payment_service.py L220`  ·  **Категория:** bug
- **Проблема:** complete_transaction_and_notify calls send_telegram_message(int(owner.telegram_id), msg) unconditionally. User.telegram_id is nullable=True (backend/app/models/user.py:33) and the project explicitly supports username/password and Google OAuth signups that have no telegram_id. For such an owner, int(None) raises TypeError. This propagates up through the Payme/Click webhook and the admin approve endpoint, aborting the request after tx.status was set to COMPLETED in the session; db.commit() never runs, so the whole activation is rolled back. The payment provider charged the customer but no subscription is activated and the webhook returns 500, causing the provider to keep retrying against a tx that will fail again. Fix: guard like reject_card_payment does — `if owner and owner.telegram_id:` before sending, and wrap the send in try/except so notification failure never aborts billing.
- **Проверка:** Confirmed genuine bug. In backend/app/services/payment_service.py, complete_transaction_and_notify (lines 318-334) guards only with `if owner:` (line 328) and then calls `send_telegram_message(int(owner.telegram_id), msg)` (line 334) without checking telegram_id is non-null. User.telegram_id is nullable (backend/app/models/user.py:43, Mapped[int | None] ... nullable=True), and the password/Google signup path explicitly creates User(telegram_id=None) (backend/app/routers/auth.py:304-305). For such an owner, int(None) raises TypeError.

The crash ordering is exactly as described: complete_transaction_and_notify first sets tx.status = COMPLETED (line 319) and calls activate_subscription (line 324), then crashes at line 334 before any commit. It is invoked from the Payme webhook (backend/app/routers/payments.py:453) and Click webhook (line 487), each followed by db.commit() (lines 454/488) which never runs because the exception propagates — so the activation is rolled back and the webhook returns 500, causing the provider to retry. It is also invoked from the admin card-approval path approve_card_payment (line 285). The customer is charged (payment performed by provider) but no subscription is activated.

The inconsistency is proven by reject_card_payment (line 306) which correctly guards `if owner and owner.telegram_id:` and wraps the send in try/except (lines 310-313). complete_transaction_and_notify lacks both. refund_transaction (lines 381-385) has the same latent unguarded int(owner.telegram_id) bug. The proposed fix (guard + try/except mirroring reject_card_payment) is correct.

The cited line number (220) does not match the actual location (line 318-334), but the function name, file, mechanism, and impact are all accurate. Severity high is justified: the affected population (password/Google-only owners) is explicitly supported, and the failure mode is double-billing-without-service plus provider retry storms — a billing/data-integrity defect.

### 6. [high] Production secret-key strength check reads os.getenv('APP_ENV') instead of the parsed app_env field
- **Область:** `core:config+db+deps`  ·  **Файл:** `backend/app/config.py L23-34`  ·  **Категория:** security
- **Проблема:** validate_secret_key gates the weak-secret rejection on `os.getenv('APP_ENV','development').lower() == 'production'`. But app_env is a real settings field that can be supplied via the .env file (model_config env_file='.env'). If a deployment sets app_env=production in .env (or any non-env-var source) without ALSO exporting the APP_ENV process env var, os.getenv returns 'development' and the check is skipped — allowing the default 'change_me' or a <32-char SECRET_KEY in production, which makes HS256 JWTs forgeable (utils/auth.py signs with settings.secret_key). The model_validator validate_production uses self.app_env correctly for other checks but does NOT re-validate secret_key, so there is no backstop. Fix: validate secret_key inside the after-model validator using self.app_env (authoritative, fully parsed), e.g. append to errors when secret_key.lower() in _INSECURE_DEFAULTS or len(secret_key) < 32.
- **Проверка:** Confirmed real by reading backend/app/config.py and backend/app/utils/auth.py.

The mechanism: `validate_secret_key` (config.py lines 23-34) gates weak-secret rejection on `os.getenv("APP_ENV", "development").lower() == "production"`. `os.getenv` reads ONLY the process environment, not pydantic-settings sources. But `app_env` is a real settings field (line 14) populated by `BaseSettings` from `env_file=".env"` (line 12) in addition to env vars. So if a deployment writes `APP_ENV=production` into a `.env` file on the server without ALSO exporting APP_ENV as a process env var, `self.app_env == "production"` yet `os.getenv("APP_ENV")` returns "development", and the weak-secret check is silently skipped — permitting the default `secret_key = "change_me"` (line 19, also in _INSECURE_DEFAULTS line 8) or any sub-32-char key in production.

No backstop exists: the after-model validator `validate_production` (lines 85-105) correctly uses `self.app_env` (line 87) and validates bot_token, database_url, cors_origins, public_api_url, webhook_secret — but never re-checks secret_key. So the only secret_key guard is the field_validator using the wrong source.

Impact confirmed: utils/auth.py signs all access/refresh JWTs with `settings.secret_key` under HS256 (ALGORITHM="HS256" line 15; create_access_token line 74, create_refresh_token line 80, decode_token line 84). A known/default signing key makes tokens forgeable → auth bypass.

Test coverage masks the gap: backend/tests/test_config.py only ever sets APP_ENV via monkeypatch.setenv (process env), so all three tests pass while the .env-file path remains unverified.

Mitigating factor for severity: the documented/primary deploy path is Render with dashboard env vars (process env) — `.env` is gitignored (.gitignore lines 47-51) and there is no render.yaml committing app_env via file. On that path os.getenv sees APP_ENV correctly and the check works. The defect only triggers for a .env-file-on-server config style, which is explicitly enabled by env_file=".env". Conditional exploitability, but the failure is silent and the consequence is full auth bypass.

The suggested fix (validate secret_key inside the after-model validator using self.app_env) is correct and is the proper single-source-of-truth resolution.

### 7. [high] 1-hour reminder can be silently skipped if a single beat run is missed
- **Область:** `task:reminders`  ·  **Файл:** `backend/app/tasks/reminders.py L47`  ·  **Категория:** reliability
- **Проблема:** The send window is REMINDER_WINDOW_MIN=59 .. MAX=61, i.e. only ~2 minutes wide, while Celery beat fires every minute (celery_app.py:19). A booking therefore has at most ~2 chances to be caught. If the worker is busy, redis hiccups, or a deploy restarts the worker during those two minutes (very common on Render), the booking's minutes_until moves below 59 on the next successful run and the reminder is NEVER sent (reminder_sent_at stays NULL but the time window has passed). There is no catch-up logic. Fix: widen the window and make it open-ended on the lower bound combined with the reminder_sent_at guard, e.g. send when minutes_until <= REMINDER_WINDOW_MAX (and >= some small floor like 0) AND reminder_sent_at IS NULL. The dedup column already prevents double-send, so a wide 'fire as soon as we're within ~61 min and haven't sent yet' window is both safer and still single-shot.
- **Проверка:** All premises verified against the code. backend/app/tasks/reminders.py lines 10-11 define REMINDER_WINDOW_MIN=59.0 and REMINDER_WINDOW_MAX=61.0; line 47 gates sending on `if not (REMINDER_WINDOW_MIN <= minutes_until <= REMINDER_WINDOW_MAX): continue` — a strict ~2-minute-wide window. backend/app/celery_app.py lines 17-20 schedule send_hourly_reminders with crontab(minute="*"), i.e. once per minute. minutes_until decreases ~1/minute, so each booking lands inside [59,61] on only ~2-3 successive beat runs. The dedup guard is reminder_sent_at.is_(None) (line 40), set only after a send attempt (line 61).

The defect: there is no catch-up logic. If the single (or two) beat runs covering a booking's window are missed — busy worker, Redis hiccup, or a deploy/worker restart (routine on Render per project notes) — then on the next successful run minutes_until is already <59, line 47 continues, and reminder_sent_at stays NULL forever. The booking still matches the query (Booking.date >= now_local.date()) every minute but can never re-enter the closed window, so the 1-hour reminder is silently dropped with no error and no retry.

The proposed fix is sound: replace the closed window with an open-ended lower bound (minutes_until <= REMINDER_WINDOW_MAX, plus a small floor like >= 0 to avoid firing on already-started/past bookings) combined with the existing reminder_sent_at IS NULL guard, which already prevents double-send and keeps it single-shot. Severity remains high: silent failure of the core booking-reminder feature under a realistic, recurring infra condition.

### 8. [high] Revenue card's bar chart plots booking counts, not revenue
- **Область:** `fe:dash-analytics`  ·  **Файл:** `frontend/src/app/dashboard/analytics/page.tsx L60-64, 140-144`  ·  **Категория:** correctness
- **Проблема:** The hero card is titled 'Davr daromadi' (period revenue) and shows summary.revenue, but the bar chart under it is fed `bars`, which is derived from `bookings` (the /bookings-by-day endpoint, value = x.bookings), not from the `rev` revenue series. The `rev` data is fetched but never charted (only summed for revSum/pctChange). So users see a revenue card whose graph and tooltip show daily booking COUNTS. Fix: build `bars` from `rev` (e.g. map rev.slice(-7) -> { day: weekday(x.date), value: x.amount }) so the chart matches the card, or relabel/move the chart. If both metrics are wanted, render two charts with correct sources.
- **Проверка:** Verified against frontend/src/app/dashboard/analytics/page.tsx and RevenueChart.tsx. Two distinct series are fetched: `rev` ({date, amount}, from /analytics/revenue, line 22, 31-33) and `bookings` ({date, bookings}, from /analytics/bookings-by-day, line 23, 34-36). At lines 60-63, `bars` is built ONLY from `bookings`, with `value: x.bookings` — the daily booking COUNT. The hero card (lines 117-124) is titled "Davr daromadi" (period revenue) and displays fmtSum(summary.revenue). Directly under it (lines 140-142) the `RevenueChart` component is fed those `bars`. In RevenueChart.tsx the <Bar dataKey="value"> (line 56) plots that count, and the tooltip (lines 20-22) renders the raw `payload[0].value` — i.e. the booking count — with no revenue formatting. The `rev` series' amounts are never charted: `revSum` (line 59) feeds only the pctChange badge (lines 67-69), and `rev` is otherwise only used for the prev-period approximation (lines 49-52). So a component literally named RevenueChart, sitting under a revenue-labeled card, plots and tooltips daily booking counts rather than revenue. The detail is accurate. Severity high is defensible: this is the primary hero card of the analytics dashboard and the mislabeled metric directly misleads business owners about their revenue trend, though it is a presentation/correctness bug (not data corruption or security), so medium would also be reasonable.

### 9. [high] Promo percent and amount discounts silently combine; UI claims they are exclusive
- **Область:** `fe:dash-promo+reviews`  ·  **Файл:** `frontend/src/app/dashboard/promo/page.tsx L44-49, 138-142, 231-251`  ·  **Категория:** data-integrity
- **Проблема:** The create form labels the two inputs 'Chegirma %' and 'Yoki so‘m' (percent OR amount) and defaults discount_percent to '10'. Neither the frontend nor the backend enforces exclusivity: add() only rejects when BOTH are <=0 (line 69), and create_promo in backend/app/routers/promo.py only rejects when both are 0. But backend/app/services/booking_service.py:326 applies BOTH: discount = base_price*pct//100 + amount. So an owner who types an amount without clearing the pre-filled '10%' creates a promo that gives 10% PLUS the fixed sum at checkout — a larger discount than intended (real money loss). Worse, the card display at line 139-142 sets isPct = discount_percent > 0 and shows ONLY the percent, hiding the amount entirely, so the owner cannot even see the combined discount exists. Fix: make the inputs truly exclusive (zero the other field on input and on submit), validate server-side that not both are >0, and show both values on the card.
- **Проверка:** All claims verified against the actual code.

1. Frontend (frontend/src/app/dashboard/promo/page.tsx): the create form defaults discount_percent to "10" (line 46), labels the two inputs "Chegirma %" (line 233) and "Yoki so'm" (line 242, implying OR/exclusive). The onChange handlers (lines 234-249) each set only their own field — neither zeroes the other. add() validation (lines 67-72) only rejects when BOTH pct<=0 AND amt<=0; it never rejects when both are >0. So an owner who types a som amount without clearing the pre-filled "10" submits both.

2. Backend create_promo (backend/app/routers/promo.py lines 100-101) only raises when discount_percent==0 AND discount_amount==0. The Pydantic PromoCreate model (lines 50-51) allows both to be >0. No exclusivity enforced server-side.

3. Discount application (backend/app/services/booking_service.py): _apply_promo line 367 computes discount = (base_price * (p.discount_percent or 0) // 100) + (p.discount_amount or 0) — strictly additive. validate_promo_for_business line 389 does the same. So a promo with both fields set gives percent PLUS fixed amount at checkout — a larger discount than the owner intended (real money loss).

4. Card display (page.tsx lines 139-142, 170): isPct = p.discount_percent > 0; when true it shows ONLY `${p.discount_percent}%` with label "chegirma" and never renders discount_amount. So a combined promo is displayed as pure-percent, hiding the extra fixed sum entirely — the owner cannot see or detect the combined discount exists.

The full chain is real and self-consistent: UI claims exclusivity ("Yoki"), nothing enforces it (FE or BE), checkout applies both additively, and the card conceals the amount. Realistic trigger is the pre-filled "10" not being cleared. Severity high is justified because the concealment in the card makes the overcharge-discount undetectable to the owner, though the precondition is owner inattention rather than attacker exploitation, so it is bounded/self-inflicted rather than systemic.

### 10. [high] 024 password-identity backfill can violate UNIQUE(provider,subject) on duplicate phones
- **Область:** `migrations:014-025`  ·  **Файл:** `backend/alembic/versions/024_auth_identities.py L98-114`  ·  **Категория:** data-integrity
- **Проблема:** For users with a password_hash but no username, the backfill computes subject = (username.lower() or phone). Two distinct users that share the same phone (or share a lowercased username that 023 didn't catch because one row had a username and the other only a phone) both produce identical (provider='password', subject) rows, which violates uq_auth_identity_provider_subject and aborts the entire upgrade. Phone is NOT yet deduped/unique at this point — phone uniqueness is only added in migration 027 (later in the chain). So on any production DB that has two password-set accounts with the same phone, `alembic upgrade head` fails at 024. Username dedup in 023 only guards the username branch, not the phone fallback. Fix: before inserting, dedup the password subjects in Python (skip/skip-duplicates keeping the oldest by created_at), or wrap each insert and ON CONFLICT DO NOTHING, or order users by created_at and track seen subjects. At minimum, run the phone-dedup (the 027 UPDATE ... blank duplicates) before 024 so the fallback subjects are unique.
- **Проверка:** Verified against backend/alembic/versions/024_auth_identities.py:98-114. The password-identity backfill computes subject = ((u.username or "").strip().lower()) or (u.phone or "").strip() and inserts a row (provider='password', subject). The table has UniqueConstraint('provider','subject', name='uq_auth_identity_provider_subject') (lines 52-54). A single bind.execute(insert, rows) (line 117) does the whole batch in one statement, so any duplicate aborts the entire 024 upgrade.

Migration-chain order confirms phone is NOT deduped when 024 runs: 023_user_username_unique.py dedupes only lower(username) (PARTITION BY lower(username)) before its index — it does nothing for phones, and only guards the username branch of the fallback. The phone-uniqueness migration has internal revision="027", down_revision="026" (despite the filename 026_user_phone_unique.py) and runs strictly AFTER 024 (024 revises 023; 027 revises 026). Its UPDATE...blank-duplicates (PARTITION BY phone) is the only phone dedup and has not yet executed at 024.

User model (backend/app/models/user.py:44,47) defaults username and phone to '' (empty = sentinel, no NULLs). So a user with password_hash set, username='', and a non-empty phone yields subject=phone via the fallback. Two such users sharing the same phone produce identical (provider='password', subject=phone) rows → uq_auth_identity_provider_subject violation → alembic upgrade head fails.

The scenario is reachable on real data: phones are loaded with no uniqueness check pre-027 (e.g. admin.py:339-343 creates owners with arbitrary owner_phone; phone also comes from Telegram). The set_password guard in auth.py:411-426 only checks for clashes when claiming a new phone (if not user.phone) — accounts that already carry a phone, or any pre-existing duplicate-phone state captured before 027's DB-level index, bypass it. A migration must be robust to arbitrary pre-existing data, which is exactly why 023 and 027 contain dedup steps; 024's fallback has none.

telegram branch is safe (telegram_id is unique, model line 43) and the username branch is safe (023 dedup), so the defect is isolated to the phone-fallback branch precisely as described. Severity high is appropriate: a failed alembic upgrade blocks all backend deploys, is data-state-dependent (only surfaces on prod DBs with the right duplicate), and leaves the schema partially applied. Trigger conditions are somewhat narrow, but the impact (broken deploy) and the difficulty of detecting it pre-prod justify high.

### 11. [medium] Broadcast can send duplicate messages and inflate counts when filtering by plan/status
- **Область:** `router:admin`  ·  **Файл:** `backend/app/routers/admin.py L621-639`  ·  **Категория:** bug
- **Проблема:** _select_broadcast_recipients joins Subscription (q.join(Subscription, Subscription.business_id == Business.id)) without any DISTINCT or one-per-business reduction. A business with multiple subscription rows (renewals, expired+active, history) produces multiple (Business, User) tuples. _send_broadcast_to then iterates rows and sends one Telegram message per row, so the owner receives the broadcast N times, and sent/total counts (returned to the admin and stored in BroadcastMessage) are inflated by the duplication. Fix: select distinct businesses, e.g. apply .distinct() on Business.id (or collect a unique set of owner telegram_ids) before fanning out, or use a subquery/EXISTS for the subscription filter instead of a join.
- **Проверка:** The finding's line citation (621-639) is wrong — that range is toggle_business. But the substantive claim about backend/app/routers/admin.py is accurate. _select_broadcast_recipients (lines 655-688) builds q = db.query(Business, User).join(User, ...) and, when filters.plan or filters.subscription_status is set, adds q = q.join(Subscription, Subscription.business_id == Business.id) (line 671) with no .distinct() and no one-per-business reduction, then returns q.all() (line 688).

The data model confirms a business can have multiple subscription rows: models/subscription.py has business relationship back_populates="subscriptions" (plural) with no unique constraint on business_id. services/payment_service.py activate_subscription (lines 54-72) does NOT update in place — it marks the existing ACTIVE row EXPIRED and inserts a brand-new Subscription on every renewal. So a renewed business accumulates 1 ACTIVE + N EXPIRED rows.

Therefore the inner join can yield multiple (Business, User) tuples for one owner whenever the subscription filter matches more than one of that business's rows — e.g. subscription_status=EXPIRED for a business that renewed several times, or plan=MONTHLY for a business with multiple MONTHLY rows. _send_broadcast_to (lines 718-732) iterates rows directly, appends int(owner.telegram_id) per row to targets with no dedup, and sends one message per target via asyncio.gather, so the owner receives the broadcast N times. sent/failed counts are derived per-target and the inflated total (len(rows)) is returned to the admin and persisted into BroadcastMessage.sent_count and the admin audit log (lines 753-755, 767, 777). recipients_from_filter_dict (scheduled broadcasts) reuses the same helper, so the Celery path is affected too. Nothing dedups elsewhere.

Downgraded from high to medium: the duplication only triggers when an admin applies plan/status filters; the default no-filter broadcast skips the Subscription join entirely and is unaffected. Status=ACTIVE is also effectively single-row because activate_subscription keeps only one ACTIVE per business. Impact is duplicate Telegram messages (spam/annoyance) plus inflated stored counts — a genuine bug but not a security issue and not on the most common broadcast path. The suggested fix (.distinct() on Business.id, or an EXISTS/subquery for the subscription filter, or dedup telegram_ids before fan-out) is correct.

### 12. [medium] Access token passed in URL query string leaks into logs (/google/start?token=)
- **Область:** `router:auth`  ·  **Файл:** `backend/app/routers/auth.py L100-119`  ·  **Категория:** security
- **Проблема:** google_start accepts a full JWT access token as the `token` query parameter for link mode. Query strings are routinely written to access/proxy logs (Render, nginx, CDN, browser history, Referer header on the subsequent 302 to Google). A leaked access token grants full account access for its lifetime. The code comment acknowledges 'the token rides the query' but does not mitigate the logging exposure. Fix: accept the token via a POST body or short-lived one-time link-nonce instead of GET query, or at minimum issue a dedicated narrowly-scoped, single-use link token (type='link', short exp) rather than a general access token, and ensure web server access-log query stripping for this path.
- **Проверка:** Confirmed at backend/app/routers/auth.py:146-166. google_start is a GET endpoint with `token: str | None = None` as a query param (link mode `?link=1&token=<access>`), passed directly to get_user_from_token(db, token). In backend/app/utils/auth.py:87-98, get_user_from_token requires payload type == "access" — i.e. it accepts a full, general-purpose access token identical to what login/refresh mint; there is no narrow or single-use link-token type. backend/app/config.py:20 sets access_token_expire_minutes = 60, so a leaked token grants full account access for up to an hour. The code comment (lines 156-159) explicitly states "the token rides the query," so the GET-query exposure is the actual intended design with no mitigation. Query strings are captured by access/proxy logs (Render/nginx), browser history, and possibly the Referer header on the 302 to Google; no log-stripping exists for this path. This matches CWE-598 (sensitive data in GET query string). The finding's facts and proposed fixes (POST body or a dedicated short-lived single-use type=link token) are valid. Downgraded from high to medium: exploitation is not a direct remote auth bypass — it requires an attacker to obtain logs/history/Referer, and link mode requires the victim to already be authenticated. It is a real defense-in-depth credential-handling defect rather than a critical vulnerability.

### 13. [medium] Blocking sync DB and blocking httpx call run on the event loop in async webhook handlers
- **Область:** `router:payments`  ·  **Файл:** `backend/app/routers/payments.py L427, 448, 454, 478`  ·  **Категория:** perf
- **Проблема:** payme_webhook and click_webhook are 'async def' but execute synchronous SQLAlchemy queries and complete_transaction_and_notify -> send_telegram_message, which does a blocking httpx.post with a 15s timeout. All of this runs directly on the asyncio event loop, blocking every other request for the duration of the Telegram round-trip (up to 15-30s). Fix: either make these endpoints plain 'def' (so FastAPI runs them in the threadpool) or offload the DB/notify work via asyncio.to_thread, as upload_receipt already does for send_telegram_photo (line 230).
- **Проверка:** Verified the facts at backend/app/routers/payments.py. payme_webhook (line 427) and click_webhook (line 458) are both `async def` and execute synchronous, blocking I/O directly: `db.query(PaymentTransaction)...` (lines 441, 479), `db.commit()` (lines 454, 488), and complete_transaction_and_notify (lines 453, 487). `get_db` (backend/app/database.py:22) yields a synchronous SQLAlchemy `Session` (SessionLocal()), so all DB calls are blocking. complete_transaction_and_notify (backend/app/services/payment_service.py:318) calls send_telegram_message at line 334, which (notification_service.py:31-39) performs a blocking `httpx.post(url, json=payload, timeout=15)`.

In FastAPI/Starlette, `async def` path operations run on the event loop coroutine directly and are NOT dispatched to the threadpool (only plain `def` handlers get run_in_threadpool). Because none of this blocking work is awaited or offloaded via asyncio.to_thread, it stalls the single event loop thread for the full duration — up to the 15s Telegram timeout when the API is unreachable — blocking all other concurrent requests on that worker. The codebase itself shows the correct patterns: upload_receipt wraps its Telegram call in `await asyncio.to_thread(send_telegram_photo, ...)` (line 231), and the sync notification_service exposes an async variant `send_telegram_message_async` (line 70). The refund endpoint (line 497) is a plain `def`. So the webhooks genuinely deviate from the established correct patterns.

This is a real perf defect. Downgrading from high to medium: payment webhooks are low-frequency (only fired by Payme/Click on payment events, not user-facing high-traffic paths), and the impact is latency/throughput degradation during the blocking window, not data loss or a security issue. The suggested fixes (make handlers plain `def`, or offload via asyncio.to_thread / use send_telegram_message_async) are valid.

### 14. [medium] Loyalty discount counts only COMPLETED visits, but free booking is granted at create time — exploitable / wrong cadence
- **Область:** `service:booking_service`  ·  **Файл:** `backend/app/services/booking_service.py L258-282`  ·  **Категория:** correctness
- **Проблема:** _maybe_apply_loyalty computes next_visit = COMPLETED count + 1 and grants a 100% discount (price 0) at the moment of booking creation, before the visit is completed. Because only COMPLETED bookings are counted, a client can repeatedly create bookings on the boundary: e.g. with loyalty_after_visits=5 and 4 completed visits, EVERY new booking the client creates is priced 0 (each create sees completed=4 -> next_visit=5 -> free), since pending/confirmed creates never increment the completed count. A client can spam multiple free bookings simultaneously, and if any later visit is marked completed the cadence is also off. Fix: either grant the stamp based on the count of already-completed visits being an exact multiple at completion time (award the free visit when the Nth visit is completed, not when the (N)th is booked), or guard against multiple outstanding pending/confirmed free bookings by also counting PENDING/CONFIRMED toward next_visit when deciding the boundary.
- **Проверка:** Confirmed against the code. `_maybe_apply_loyalty` (backend/app/services/booking_service.py:299-323) computes `completed` by counting ONLY `BookingStatus.COMPLETED` rows for the (service, client), then `next_visit = completed + 1` and returns price 0 when `next_visit % n == 0` — at booking-CREATE time (called from create flow line 236, stored as `payment_amount` at line 256). Because newly created bookings are PENDING/CONFIRMED (lines 223-226), they never increment the COMPLETED count, so the count is frozen during a booking spree.

The only idempotency guard (lines 188-206) blocks ONLY the exact same date+start_time slot for that client; bookings at different slots/times each independently re-run the loyalty check. There is no per-client outstanding-booking cap (grep for limits found none). Completion (backend/app/routers/bookings.py:390) just flips status to COMPLETED and does not re-price, so the create-time price of 0 stands permanently.

Concrete exploit: with loyalty_after_visits=5 and 4 completed visits, every booking the client creates sees completed=4 -> next_visit=5 -> price 0. The client can book multiple different slots, each free, instead of one free visit per cadence cycle. This is genuine over-granting of free services / financial leakage and confirms the finding's core mechanism, including the secondary cadence skew once some of those over-granted frees are later completed.

I downgrade severity from high to medium: the exploit window only exists when the client is exactly one visit short of a stamp boundary (completed = n-1 mod n), it requires the owner to have enabled loyalty, the loss is limited to free service slots (not unbounded money, and PENDING-mode businesses can decline), and an owner can notice/cancel duplicate free bookings. Still a real correctness defect worth fixing — award the stamp at completion time (when the Nth visit is marked COMPLETED) or count PENDING/CONFIRMED toward the boundary to prevent multiple outstanding free bookings.

### 15. [medium] publish() calls asyncio.Queue.put_nowait cross-thread from sync handlers (not thread-safe, may not wake consumer)
- **Область:** `service:event_bus`  ·  **Файл:** `backend/app/services/event_bus.py L45-47`  ·  **Категория:** concurrency
- **Проблема:** publish() is invoked from synchronous `def` route handlers (bookings.py:113, bookings.py:364, reviews.py:85; business.py PUT /me is also sync). FastAPI runs sync handlers in an anyio worker THREAD, while the SSE subscribe() generator and its q.get() run on the asyncio event-loop thread. asyncio.Queue is explicitly NOT thread-safe and is bound to the loop it was created on. put_nowait() from a foreign thread mutates queue internals without locking AND schedules the waiter wakeup via loop.call_soon, which is itself not thread-safe from another thread. Result: data races on queue internals and, critically, the waiting get() coroutine may never be scheduled to wake — so the event is enqueued but the SSE stream does not emit it until the next 30s heartbeat (or not at all if state is corrupted). The 'instant bell update' this module exists for is therefore unreliable. Fix: capture loop = asyncio.get_running_loop() per queue in subscribe(), and in publish do loop.call_soon_threadsafe(q.put_nowait, kind); or make the publishing handlers async; or use asyncio.run_coroutine_threadsafe. The QueueFull catch also won't behave correctly since put_nowait isn't running on the owning loop.
- **Проверка:** Verified at backend/app/services/event_bus.py:37-52 and the cited call sites. publish() does `q.put_nowait(kind)` (line 47) on `asyncio.Queue(maxsize=64)` objects that are created and consumed inside the async generator subscribe() (lines 59, 68), which runs on the event-loop thread (the SSE StreamingResponse gen() in business.py:401-407). The publishers are all plain `def` (sync) handlers using sync `Session`/`get_db`: bookings.py:48 create_public_booking → publish_event at :116, bookings.py:397 cancel → :407, reviews.py:92, and the import alias is `from app.services.event_bus import publish as publish_event` (bookings.py:33, reviews.py:14). Starlette runs sync `def` handlers in an anyio worker threadpool, so publish() executes off the loop thread. asyncio.Queue is documented not thread-safe and is bound to its creating loop; put_nowait from a foreign thread mutates queue internals and calls _wakeup_next → Future.set_result → loop.call_soon (NOT call_soon_threadsafe), which in CPython does not write to the loop's self-pipe and therefore will not wake a selector that is currently blocked. So an enqueued event can sit undelivered until something else wakes the loop. The claim is therefore correct: the "instant" bell update is not reliable, and there is a genuine (if narrow) data race on queue/future internals. Suggested fix (capture the running loop in subscribe() and use loop.call_soon_threadsafe(q.put_nowait, kind), or make publishers async) is the right remedy.

Severity corrected from high to medium: the module's 30s heartbeat is a real, functioning mitigation, not just documentation. subscribe() awaits `asyncio.wait_for(q.get(), timeout=30.0)` (line 68); the timeout fires on the loop thread, wakes the loop, and on the next loop iteration q.get() drains whatever put_nowait enqueued. So the practical impact is the "instant" update degrading to <=30s latency plus a low-probability internal-state corruption — bounded, no permanent event loss or hang under normal operation. Real defect worth fixing, but not high-severity given the bounded staleness.

### 16. [medium] Broadcast success/failure stats are meaningless — async send never signals failure to caller
- **Область:** `service:notification_service`  ·  **Файл:** `backend/app/services/notification_service.py L85-100`  ·  **Категория:** data-integrity
- **Проблема:** send_telegram_message_async catches every exception inside _do and only logs a warning on non-2xx responses; it never re-raises and returns None unconditionally. The broadcast fan-out in backend/app/routers/admin.py (_send_broadcast_to lines 661-667 and retry_broadcast lines 777-783) wraps the call in try/except and treats a raised exception as failure (return False) and a clean return as success (return True). Because the function never raises — even on HTTP 403 (user blocked the bot), 429 (rate limited), or network timeouts — every recipient is counted as `sent`, `failed_recipients` is always empty, and the persisted BroadcastMessage.sent_count/failed_count/failed_recipients stored in the DB are wrong. The retry endpoint is therefore also dead: failed_recipients is never populated, so /broadcasts/{id}/retry always returns no_failed. Fix: make the async send return a bool (or raise on non-2xx / on exception) so callers can distinguish real delivery from failure, then update _send_broadcast_to/retry_broadcast to use that signal.
- **Проверка:** Verified against the cited code.

1) backend/app/services/notification_service.py lines 70-100: send_telegram_message_async is declared `-> None`. Its inner `_do` (lines 85-94) wraps the POST in `try/except Exception`; on status_code >= 400 it only calls logger.warning (lines 88-92) and on any exception it only calls logger.exception (lines 93-94). Neither path re-raises, and the outer function returns None unconditionally. So the function truly never signals failure.

2) backend/app/routers/admin.py _send_broadcast_to lines 710-716: `_one` awaits send_telegram_message_async inside try/except and returns True on completion, False only on a raised exception. Because the send never raises, every recipient with a valid telegram_id is counted in `sent` (lines 726-728). The only `failed` increment comes from the missing-telegram_id guard (lines 720-722). HTTP 403 (blocked bot), 429 (rate limit), and timeouts are all swallowed and counted as success.

3) broadcast endpoint lines 753-755 persist sent_count/failed_count/failed_recipients directly from those wrong values, so the stored BroadcastMessage stats are inaccurate and failed_recipients only ever holds users lacking a telegram_id.

4) retry_broadcast lines 918-919 short-circuit with `no_failed` when failed_recipients is empty; since real delivery failures are never recorded there, the retry endpoint is effectively dead for genuine failures.

The defect, all three downstream impacts, and the proposed fix (return a bool / raise on non-2xx, then honor it in callers) are all correct.

Severity adjusted from high to medium: it is a genuine data-integrity bug, but it is confined to an admin-only broadcast reporting/retry feature (gated by get_admin_user) with no security impact and no effect on end-user-facing or core booking data. The harm is misleading admin stats and a non-functional retry button.

### 17. [medium] Refund crashes for owners with no Telegram ID
- **Область:** `service:payment_service`  ·  **Файл:** `backend/app/services/payment_service.py L267`  ·  **Категория:** bug
- **Проблема:** refund_transaction does `if owner:` then send_telegram_message(int(owner.telegram_id), ...) — but owner.telegram_id can be None (nullable). int(None) raises TypeError, aborting the refund after tx was already marked REFUNDED and the subscription CANCELLED in-session; db.commit() never runs and everything rolls back, so an admin clicking refund on a non-Telegram owner's payment silently fails with a 500. Fix: change the guard to `if owner and owner.telegram_id:` and wrap the send in try/except, mirroring reject_card_payment (lines 192-199).
- **Проверка:** Confirmed genuine bug. In backend/app/services/payment_service.py:381-385, refund_transaction guards with `if owner:` then calls `send_telegram_message(int(owner.telegram_id), ...)`. User.telegram_id is nullable — user.py:43 declares `Mapped[int | None] = mapped_column(BigInteger, unique=True, nullable=True, ...)` with a comment "Nullable since Google/password-only accounts have no Telegram id." Such owners are a real, supported account type in this project (the forced-password/Google-OAuth flow is a core feature). For such an owner, int(None) raises TypeError. There is no try/except, unlike the sibling reject_card_payment (306-313: `if owner and owner.telegram_id:` + try/except). The TypeError is raised after tx.status=REFUNDED (360) and active_sub.status=CANCELLED (376) are set in-session but before db.flush()/commit. The caller (routers/payments.py:508-511) catches only ValueError, so the TypeError becomes an uncaught 500; db.commit() at line 520 never executes, so the state changes roll back — the admin's refund silently no-ops with a 500. The proposed fix (`if owner and owner.telegram_id:` + try/except) is correct and matches reject_card_payment. Note complete_transaction_and_notify (line 334) has the identical latent bug. Severity corrected from high to medium: no data corruption or money movement occurs (tx safely stays COMPLETED on rollback), it only affects the notification tail of an admin-only action, but it does cause a real functional failure (refund unusable for non-Telegram owners).

### 18. [medium] Webhook idempotency not enforced under concurrent retries — duplicate subscription activation
- **Область:** `service:payment_service`  ·  **Файл:** `backend/app/routers/payments.py L440`  ·  **Категория:** race condition
- **Проблема:** In payme_webhook (and identically click_webhook at 474), the tx is fetched WITHOUT with_for_update and the idempotency guard `tx.status == COMPLETED` is evaluated before any lock is taken. Payment providers deliver the same callback multiple times. Two concurrent deliveries each open their own DB transaction, each read the committed PENDING status (guard passes for both), then both call complete_transaction_and_notify -> activate_subscription. activate_subscription serializes on the Business row lock, but the second caller never re-reads tx status under that lock, so it creates a SECOND ACTIVE Subscription row (the first one having been swapped to EXPIRED) and re-sets the already-COMPLETED tx. Net effect: duplicate subscription rows and/or double-extended expiry from a single payment. Fix: select the tx with with_for_update() inside complete path and re-check `if tx.status == COMPLETED: return` after acquiring the lock, or add a unique partial constraint so only one ACTIVE subscription per business can exist.
- **Проверка:** Confirmed the defect by reading both the webhook handlers and the service layer.

In backend/app/routers/payments.py, payme_webhook (line 441-443) and click_webhook (line 479-481) fetch the tx WITHOUT with_for_update() and evaluate the idempotency guard `tx.status == COMPLETED` before any row lock is taken. Each FastAPI request gets its own session (SessionLocal, autocommit=False), and the engine sets no isolation level so Postgres default READ COMMITTED applies. Two concurrent/duplicate provider callbacks each read the committed PENDING tx, so the guard passes for both.

Both then call complete_transaction_and_notify (payment_service.py:318), which sets tx.status=COMPLETED on the in-memory object and calls activate_subscription (line 42). activate_subscription locks ONLY the Business row (line 52) and re-queries the Subscription with_for_update (line 54-60); it never re-reads tx.status under the lock. So when caller B unblocks after A commits, B's tx snapshot is still PENDING, B re-runs activation: it finds A's now-committed ACTIVE subscription, flips it to EXPIRED (line 61-62), and inserts a SECOND new ACTIVE Subscription (line 64-72), plus sends a duplicate "payment accepted" Telegram message (line 334).

There is no guard against this: subscription.py has no unique/partial constraint limiting one ACTIVE subscription per business (only a business_id index). Tellingly, the refund path (payment_service.py:343-358) documents this exact race class and DOES lock the tx with with_for_update() and re-check status — the completion path does not, confirming the missing guard.

One correction to the finding: the net effect is an extra EXPIRED row plus a re-activated subscription whose expiry is RESET to now+30d (A's sub is replaced, not stacked), so it is not strictly "double-extended expiry," and there is no double financial charge. Impact is bounded data-integrity noise (orphan EXPIRED rows, redundant activation), duplicate user notifications, and an interleaving hazard with refunds — not a security/privilege issue or unbounded money loss. Real defect, but medium rather than high. The proposed fix (select tx with_for_update() in the completion path and re-check `if tx.status == COMPLETED: return`) is correct and mirrors the existing refund_transaction implementation.

### 19. [medium] notify_first_for_slot has a read-modify-write race (double notification / skipped client)
- **Область:** `service:waitlist_service`  ·  **Файл:** `backend/app/services/waitlist_service.py L96-121`  ·  **Категория:** concurrency
- **Проблема:** The head-of-queue entry is selected with a plain SELECT (ORDER BY created_at LIMIT 1, notified_at IS NULL) and only later has notified_at set; there is no row lock (no `.with_for_update()`) and no atomic UPDATE...RETURNING. Two concurrent cancellations of the same slot (e.g. two staff cancelling overlapping bookings, or a retry) can both read the same head entry before either commits, both set notified_at on it, and the same client receives two '🔔 slot ochildi' Telegram messages while the second waiting client is never pinged. The router (bookings.py:369-388) commits then sends, so the duplicate send is fully exposed. Fix: lock the candidate row, e.g. `q.order_by(...).with_for_update(skip_locked=True).first()`, or replace the select+assign with a single atomic statement (UPDATE waitlist_entries SET notified_at=now() WHERE id = (SELECT id ... FOR UPDATE SKIP LOCKED) RETURNING ...). SKIP LOCKED also lets concurrent cancellations correctly hand the slot to distinct waiting clients.
- **Проверка:** Verified against backend/app/services/waitlist_service.py:96-121. notify_first_for_slot builds a plain query (lines 96-107: filter notified_at.is_(None), order_by created_at.asc(), .first()) and only later assigns entry.notified_at = datetime.now(...) (line 120). There is no .with_for_update() and no atomic UPDATE...RETURNING. backend/app/database.py confirms a synchronous psycopg engine with a pool of up to 30 connections (pool_size=20, max_overflow=10) and no isolation_level override, so Postgres runs at READ COMMITTED. Under READ COMMITTED two concurrent transactions cancelling the same slot can both read the same head row (notified_at still NULL in each snapshot), both set notified_at, and both commit — a classic read-modify-write lost update. The router (backend/app/routers/bookings.py:412-431) calls notify_first_for_slot, then db.commit() (line 420), then send_telegram_message (line 425), so the duplicate '🔔 ... slot ochildi' send is fully committed and exposed; the second waiting client is skipped. The trigger is plausible: cancel_booking (backend/app/services/booking_service.py:398-430) has no guard against re-cancelling an already-CANCELLED booking, so a double-click/retry of PUT /bookings/{id}/cancel re-runs the whole notify path; the bot waitlist design (booking.py:347-385, FEATURE_DEPOSIT_SPEC.md) also creates same-slot multi-booking/cancel scenarios. The proposed fix (with_for_update(skip_locked=True) or a single atomic UPDATE...RETURNING) is correct and would also hand the slot to distinct clients across concurrent cancels. Severity lowered from high to medium: the defect is real but the blast radius is a duplicate Telegram notification plus one missed notification (UX annoyance), not data corruption or a security issue, and the colliding-same-slot window is narrow — appropriate for a low-traffic salon SaaS.

### 20. [medium] Rate limit trivially bypassed via spoofed X-Forwarded-For
- **Область:** `util:ratelimit`  ·  **Файл:** `backend/app/utils/ratelimit.py L38-45,52`  ·  **Категория:** security
- **Проблема:** _client_ip() unconditionally trusts the first value of the client-supplied X-Forwarded-For header as the rate-limit key, with no trusted-proxy allowlist. Because the attacker fully controls this header, they can send a different (or random) XFF on every request and each request lands in a brand-new bucket, completely defeating the per-IP limits that protect brute-force-sensitive endpoints (auth_login limit=10/min, auth_tg=30/min, public_booking=10/min). This negates the stated purpose ('blocks brute-force'). Fix: only honor X-Forwarded-For when the immediate peer (request.client.host) is a known/trusted proxy (e.g. Render's load balancer), and parse the rightmost untrusted hop rather than the leftmost client-controlled one; otherwise fall back to request.client.host. Make the trusted-proxy set configurable via settings.
- **Проверка:** Confirmed at backend/app/utils/ratelimit.py:38-45. `_client_ip()` does `request.headers.get("x-forwarded-for", "").split(",")[0].strip()` and returns it unconditionally if non-empty (lines 40-42), only falling back to request.client.host when XFF is absent. There is no trusted-proxy allowlist and it parses the LEFTMOST (client-controlled) hop. The bucket key is `f"{scope}:{_client_ip(request)}"` (line 52), so an attacker who sends a fresh/random X-Forwarded-For per request lands in a new bucket every time, fully bypassing the per-IP limits. The limits are confirmed real and applied to brute-force-sensitive endpoints: auth_login=10/60s and auth_tg=30/60s (backend/app/routers/auth.py:50-52), public_booking=10/60s (backend/app/routers/bookings.py:45). I searched the whole repo for any trusted-proxy / proxy-header handling (forwarded_allow_ips, ProxyHeadersMiddleware, --proxy-headers) and found none, so the concern is not mitigated elsewhere. The proposed fix (honor XFF only from a trusted peer, parse the rightmost untrusted hop, configurable trusted-proxy set) is correct. Severity downgraded from high to medium: the project's own audit (docs/AUDIT_FINDINGS.md:51,523) rates it low, and mitigating factors exist (bcrypt password hashing slows brute-force, Telegram initData validation on auth_tg, and the limiter is already documented as single-process best-effort with per-worker multiplication). The bypass is trivial and real but weakens rather than fully eliminates auth protection.

### 21. [medium] Business hard-delete crashes when historical bookings exist (cascade/NOT NULL mismatch)
- **Область:** `models:core`  ·  **Файл:** `backend/app/models/business.py L59`  ·  **Категория:** data-integrity
- **Проблема:** Business.bookings is declared as relationship('Booking', back_populates='bookings') with NO cascade and passive_deletes defaulting to False (verified: cascade='merge,save-update', passive_deletes=False). Booking.business_id is ForeignKey(ondelete='CASCADE') and nullable=False. When the admin endpoint does db.delete(b) (routers/admin.py:406, hard-delete path), SQLAlchemy — because passive_deletes is False and there is no delete cascade on this relationship — issues a SELECT for the business's bookings and then attempts UPDATE bookings SET business_id=NULL, violating the NOT NULL constraint and raising IntegrityError. The active-booking guard at admin.py:387-402 only blocks PENDING/CONFIRMED bookings, so any business with CANCELLED/COMPLETED/NO_SHOW history (i.e. essentially every real business) cannot be hard-deleted. Fix: add passive_deletes=True to the bookings relationship so SQLAlchemy relies on the DB ondelete='CASCADE' instead of nulling the FK: bookings: Mapped[list['Booking']] = relationship('Booking', back_populates='business', passive_deletes=True).
- **Проверка:** Verified against the actual code. backend/app/models/business.py:66 declares `bookings: Mapped[list["Booking"]] = relationship("Booking", back_populates="business")` with NO cascade and default passive_deletes=False — conspicuously unlike services/schedules/holidays/subscriptions (lines 59-69), which all use cascade="all, delete-orphan". backend/app/models/booking.py:26-28 confirms business_id is ForeignKey("businesses.id", ondelete="CASCADE") and nullable=False, and the DB migration backend/alembic/versions/001_initial.py:149,161 confirms the column is NOT NULL with ondelete=CASCADE at the DB level.

The hard-delete path is backend/app/routers/admin.py:425-457 (delete_business with hard=True): the active-booking guard at lines 436-451 only counts bookings with status PENDING/CONFIRMED, then line 455 runs db.delete(b). Because the bookings relationship has no "delete" cascade and passive_deletes is False (default), SQLAlchemy's unit of work loads the business's bookings and emits UPDATE bookings SET business_id=NULL to disassociate them before the parent DELETE — violating the NOT NULL constraint and raising IntegrityError. The DB-level ondelete=CASCADE is never exercised because the ORM intercepts first. This is the documented SQLAlchemy passive_deletes gotcha. No event listeners or global cascade config exist (grep found none), and no test covers this path. The proposed fix (passive_deletes=True) is correct.

The finding's described code/logic is accurate; only the line numbers are off (relationship is line 66 not 59; db.delete is 455 not 406; guard is 436-451 not 387-402).

Severity downgraded from high to medium: this is an admin-only endpoint (get_admin_user) gated behind an explicit opt-in ?hard=true flag; the default soft-delete path (sets deleted_at, lines 458-466) works fine. Impact is a broken admin hard-delete feature (500 on essentially any business with cancelled/completed history), not a security or data-loss issue.

### 22. [medium] Booking.end_time as bare Time breaks overlap detection for midnight-crossing bookings
- **Область:** `models:booking`  ·  **Файл:** `backend/app/models/booking.py L45-46`  ·  **Категория:** data-integrity
- **Проблема:** start_time and end_time are stored as Time (no date). The service computes end_dt = start_dt + timedelta(minutes=duration) and persists end_dt.time() (booking_service.py:184-185, 208). For a booking starting 23:30 with a 60-min service, end_time wraps to 00:30. The conflict query (booking_service.py:118-119) then evaluates Booking.start_time < end_time AND Booking.end_time > start_time as 23:30 < 00:30 (FALSE), so the overlap predicate silently fails and a real conflict is not detected, allowing double-booking. The stored end_time < start_time also makes the row's own duration nonsensical for any consumer that subtracts the two. Fix: either forbid bookings whose computed end crosses midnight (validate in create_booking), or store start/end as full DateTime(timezone=True) and do interval math on timestamps rather than wall-clock Time.
- **Проверка:** The cited mechanism is accurate and unguarded. backend/app/models/booking.py:45-46 declares start_time/end_time as bare Time columns. booking_service.py:185-186 computes end_dt = datetime.combine(date, start) + timedelta(minutes=duration) and stores end_dt.time() (line 253; same in routers/bookings.py:201-204, 610-613, reschedule_booking 475-477). The conflict query (booking_service.py:119-120, mirrored in bookings.py:218-220, 624-625, 339-340 and reschedule 488-489) is Booking.start_time < end_time AND Booking.end_time > start_time on Time values. For a 23:30 start + 60 min, end_time wraps to 00:30; SQL Time comparison evaluates 23:30 < 00:30 as FALSE, so the overlap predicate fails and a real conflict is not detected -> silent double-booking. The same wall-clock interval logic in utils/slots.py:89-93 also miscomputes free slots, and update_booking (bookings.py:317-321) derives duration as end_time - start_time which goes negative for such a row.

There is no validation preventing a midnight-crossing booking: schemas/booking.py BookingCreatePublic/BookingCreateOwner place no bound on start_time, and create_booking never checks start_time against the business schedule. The public POST /api/bookings (bookings.py:48-74) accepts the client-supplied start_time directly after only validating Telegram initData and rate-limiting, so a direct API call can submit start_time=23:30 regardless of what get_available_slots offers. The normal UI is partially protected because get_available_slots only emits slots where current_dt + duration <= schedule.end_time (slots.py:74), so a legitimate front-end flow won't offer a spilling slot for a same-day-closing business.

I downgrade from high to medium: the defect is genuine and causes double-booking plus corrupt duration data when it fires, but firing requires either a business whose schedule runs across/near midnight or a direct-API caller bypassing the slot UI, not the common booking path. The proposed fixes (validate that computed end does not cross midnight in create_booking, or store full DateTime and do interval math on timestamps) are appropriate.

### 23. [medium] Sync DB session + blocking IO used inside async route handlers blocks the event loop
- **Область:** `core:config+db+deps`  ·  **Файл:** `backend/app/database.py L17-27`  ·  **Категория:** perf
- **Проблема:** database.py builds a synchronous engine (create_engine) and SessionLocal, and get_db() yields a sync Session. Several route handlers are declared `async def` while taking `db: Session = Depends(get_db)` and then calling blocking sync ORM/IO directly on the event loop — e.g. files.py:115 upload_logo (`db.commit()` + `path.write_bytes()`), files.py:207 upload_photo, payments.py:175 upload_receipt, and webhooks payments.py:427/454. FastAPI does NOT offload `async def` handlers to a threadpool, so each blocking db.query/db.commit/file write stalls the whole worker's event loop, serializing concurrent requests and risking timeouts under load. Fix: drop `async` from handlers that only do sync DB/file work (FastAPI then runs them in a threadpool, safe for sync sessions), or migrate to async SQLAlchemy (create_async_engine/AsyncSession) and await the DB calls; for handlers that must stay async (await file.read()), wrap blocking calls in run_in_threadpool/asyncio.to_thread.
- **Проверка:** Verified the core mechanism is genuine. backend/app/database.py:17-18 builds a synchronous engine (create_engine) and SessionLocal yielding a sync Session via get_db(). Confirmed multiple route handlers are declared `async def` while taking `db: Session = Depends(get_db)` and then calling blocking sync ORM/IO directly on the event loop: files.py:85 upload_logo (async; calls blob_store.save_blob(db,...) + db.commit() at line 104), files.py:161 upload_photo (async; db.query().count(), db.add, db.commit, db.refresh), payments.py:176 upload_receipt (async; db.query().first()), payments.py:428 payme_webhook and 459 click_webhook (async; db.query + db.commit), plus admin.py broadcast/retry_broadcast/backup_import. blob_store.save_blob/get_blob/delete_blob (app/services/blob_store.py:24-38) are confirmed synchronous functions doing blocking DB IO with multi-MB blob payloads. FastAPI does NOT offload `async def` handlers to a threadpool, so these blocking calls do stall the worker's event loop. Notably the dev already used asyncio.to_thread at payments.py:231 for a Telegram send but left the DB calls unwrapped, confirming this is an oversight, not intentional. Most other handlers are correctly plain `def` (FastAPI threadpools those), so the sync session is fine there.

Detail inaccuracies that downgrade confidence/severity but do not refute the finding: (1) the cited `path.write_bytes()` filesystem write in upload_logo does not exist — uploads go to Postgres via blob_store, not the filesystem; (2) line 115 is delete_logo (a sync `def`, not async, so harmless), and upload_logo's commit is at line 104. The substance still holds.

Severity corrected from high to medium: the worst offenders (multi-MB blob writes) are rare, owner-gated upload/admin endpoints, so real-world contention is limited under this SaaS's typical concurrency.
