The externally-triggered payment webhooks are the most exposed but do only light DB work (single query + commit), so their event-loop stall is brief. Real defect, moderate practical impact.

### 24. [medium] DB dump is not a consistent snapshot (READ COMMITTED across many statements)
- **Область:** `task:backup`  ·  **Файл:** `backend/app/tasks/backup.py L61-70`  ·  **Категория:** data-integrity
- **Проблема:** _build_dump() reads each table with a separate db.execute(select(table)) statement on a default-isolation (READ COMMITTED) Postgres session. Under READ COMMITTED, every statement sees a fresh snapshot, so tables read later can include rows that reference rows that did not exist when an earlier table was read (and vice-versa). The nightly task runs at 02:30 Tashkent, but any concurrent write (a booking, a client signup, a webhook) during the dump can yield a referentially-inconsistent backup that fails or silently corrupts on restore. For a tool whose entire purpose is restore safety this is a real defect. Fix: wrap the reads in a single REPEATABLE READ (or SERIALIZABLE) transaction, e.g. db.connection(execution_options={'isolation_level': 'REPEATABLE READ'}) before the first select, or use a SET TRANSACTION ISOLATION LEVEL REPEATABLE READ at the start so all selects share one consistent snapshot. (Same issue exists in admin.backup_export at admin.py:817-819, which shares this code shape.)
- **Проверка:** The technical claim is correct. backend/app/database.py:17-18 creates the engine and SessionLocal with no isolation_level, so sessions run at PostgreSQL's default READ COMMITTED. In backend/app/tasks/backup.py:67 the dump comprehension issues a separate `db.execute(select(table))` per table (`for table in Base.metadata.sorted_tables`). Under READ COMMITTED, each statement takes a fresh snapshot even within the same transaction (only REPEATABLE READ/SERIALIZABLE freeze the snapshot for the whole transaction). So concurrent writes between statements can yield a cross-table referentially-inconsistent dump. The same code shape is confirmed in admin.py:966-968 (backup_export) and again at admin.py:1042-1043 (pre-import auto-snapshot). The fix proposed (open the connection/transaction at REPEATABLE READ before the first select) is the standard correct remedy.

I lower severity from high to medium for two reasons: (1) the "silently corrupts on restore" claim is overstated — the import (admin.py:1055-1086) deletes in reverse FK order and re-inserts in FK order inside one transaction, so a dump with a dangling FK reference would raise on insert and roll back atomically (a loud, safe failure), not silent corruption; the genuinely silent failure mode is narrower (logically inconsistent but FK-valid combinations). (2) The exposure window is small — the task runs nightly at 02:30 local during low traffic. Still a real data-integrity defect because consistency is the entire purpose of a backup tool and a backup can be unusable exactly when needed; the fix is trivial and applies to all three call sites.

### 25. [medium] owner_confirm can resurrect a cancelled/no-show/completed booking
- **Область:** `bot:mybookings+owner`  ·  **Файл:** `backend/bot/handlers/owner.py L39-43`  ·  **Категория:** data-integrity
- **Проблема:** owner_confirm only short-circuits when status is already CONFIRMED. For any other status (CANCELLED, NO_SHOW, COMPLETED) it sets status=CONFIRMED and notifies the client. An owner pressing an old 'confirm' button on a booking the client already cancelled (cxl:) or that was auto-flipped to NO_SHOW will flip it back to CONFIRMED and send '✅ Yozilishingiz tasdiqlandi!' for a slot that no longer exists. Fix: only allow the transition from PENDING (e.g. `if booking.status != BookingStatus.PENDING: cb.answer('...'); return`).
- **Проверка:** Confirmed by reading backend/bot/handlers/owner.py:39-43, which short-circuits ONLY when booking.status == BookingStatus.CONFIRMED. For any other status it unconditionally executes booking.status = BookingStatus.CONFIRMED; db.commit() (lines 42-43) and then sends the client "✅ Yozilishingiz tasdiqlandi!" (lines 65-72). The owner's confirm button is reachable in a stale state: it is created when the booking is first made (bot/keyboards/inline.py:135 and app/routers/bookings.py:107 emit callback_data own_confirm:{id}) and remains pressable in the owner's Telegram chat until that specific message is edited (owner.py:58). Meanwhile the booking can change status through messages that do NOT edit the owner's confirm message: (a) the client cancels via cxl: which routes through cancel_booking and sets CANCELLED (bot/handlers/my_bookings.py:359-378), and (b) the nightly Celery task flag_no_shows flips past PENDING/CONFIRMED bookings to NO_SHOW (app/tasks/reminders.py:74-101). In either case, an owner later pressing the still-live confirm button resurrects the booking to CONFIRMED and sends a false "your booking is confirmed" message for a slot that no longer exists — a genuine data-integrity bug. The proposed fix (reject the transition unless status == PENDING) is correct. Severity lowered from high to medium: triggering requires a stale/out-of-order button press rather than occurring on a normal happy path, and a single press is consumed by the edit_text on line 58, so impact is real but not high-frequency or security-critical.

### 26. [medium] Cancel-window timezone uses server-local time, not Asia/Tashkent
- **Область:** `bot:mybookings+owner`  ·  **Файл:** `backend/app/services/booking_service.py L384`  ·  **Категория:** timezone
- **Проблема:** cancel_booking (reached from my_bookings.py:370 with by_client=True) computes `now_local = datetime.now(tz.utc).astimezone().replace(tzinfo=None)`. `.astimezone()` converts to the *server* timezone. The whole point of app/utils/clock.py is that Render runs in UTC while the business is Asia/Tashkent (UTC+5). So on the real host now_local is effectively UTC, and the `slot_dt - now_local < window_hours` late-cancel test is off by 5 hours — clients can be wrongly flagged (or wrongly not flagged) for late cancellation right at the boundary. Fix: use `local_now().replace(tzinfo=None)` from app.utils.clock instead of `.astimezone()`.
- **Проверка:** Confirmed at backend/app/services/booking_service.py:425: `now_local = datetime.now(_tz.utc).astimezone().replace(tzinfo=None)`. `.astimezone()` with no argument converts to the HOST/system timezone, not Asia/Tashkent. Per backend/app/utils/clock.py's own docstring, Render hosts the backend in UTC, so on the real host now_local is UTC = Tashkent wall-clock minus 5 hours.

The comparison operand slot_dt (line 422 `datetime.combine(b.date, b.start_time)`) is naive Tashkent wall-clock time: bookings store date/start_time exactly as the user picked them (lines 495-496 set `b.date = new_date`/`b.start_time = new_start` with no UTC conversion; creation similarly stores the chosen slot). So slot_dt is in Tashkent local wall-clock.

Comparing a Tashkent-local slot against a UTC "now" makes `slot_dt - now_local` about 5 hours larger than reality, so the `< timedelta(hours=window_hours)` late-cancel test is off by ~5h and mis-flags `b.late_cancel` near the window boundary. The inline comment ("slot_dt is local and the window is wall-clock hours; using utcnow() here would shift by TZ_OFFSET") shows the author intended a Tashkent wall-clock now but used the wrong call. The repo already exposes `local_now()` in app.utils.clock (used in routers/bookings.py, business.py, analytics.py, utils/slots.py) for exactly this; the suggested fix `local_now().replace(tzinfo=None)` is correct.

Caller path verified: backend/bot/handlers/my_bookings.py:373 calls the service with by_client=True, reaching the flagged branch.

Downgraded from high to medium: the only effect is an incorrect `late_cancel` boolean (a soft policy/analytics signal) and only within the ~5h boundary band — no security, money-movement, or data-corruption impact.

### 27. [medium] Any dashboard fetch error redirects established users to onboarding
- **Область:** `fe:dash-shell`  ·  **Файл:** `frontend/src/app/dashboard/page.tsx L139-141`  ·  **Категория:** reliability
- **Проблема:** load() is the initial bundle fetch, and its .catch() unconditionally does router.replace('/dashboard/onboarding'). apiFetch already handles 401 (refresh, then redirect to /auth/login on failure), so any error reaching this catch is a non-auth error: a transient network failure, a 500, a 502 from Render cold-start, a JSON parse error, etc. An established business owner who hits a momentary backend hiccup is bounced into the onboarding flow instead of seeing a retry/error state. Fix: distinguish 'business not found / not onboarded' (e.g. a 404 or a specific error) from generic failures — only redirect to onboarding for the not-onboarded case, and show an error/retry UI otherwise.
- **Проверка:** Confirmed by reading the code. frontend/src/app/dashboard/page.tsx:139-141 does `load().then(() => setReady(true)).catch(() => router.replace("/dashboard/onboarding"))` — the catch is unconditional and redirects to onboarding on ANY thrown error.

apiFetch (frontend/src/lib/api.ts:75-126) confirms the finding's reasoning about error sources: on a persistent 401 it clears tokens, sets `window.location.href = "/auth/login"` and throws "Session expired" (lines 84-95). For every other non-2xx response it throws a generic `Error(detailMessage || text || statusText)` (lines 98-123), and a network failure throws too. There is no error typing/status-code carried on the thrown Error, so the page's catch cannot tell apart a transient failure from a real "not onboarded" state.

Crucially, the legitimate not-onboarded case is a 404: backend deps `get_owned_business` (backend/app/deps.py:29-31) raises `HTTPException(404, "Business not found")`, which apiFetch surfaces as a plain Error. So a 500 (bug), a 502 (Render cold-start — a documented recurring issue for this deploy topology), or a fetch network error are all indistinguishable from that 404 in the current catch, and all bounce an established business owner into the onboarding flow instead of showing a retry/error UI. The proposed fix (only redirect to onboarding for the 404/not-onboarded case, show error/retry otherwise) is correct.

Downgraded severity from high to medium: it is a genuine reliability/UX defect, but it is recoverable (the user is not logged out, no data is lost or corrupted; a reload or re-navigation restores the dashboard once the backend responds). It is confusing and likely to fire on Render cold-start 502s, which keeps it well above low.

### 28. [medium] Week view ignores the selected week — lists ALL bookings across all dates
- **Область:** `fe:dash-bookings`  ·  **Файл:** `frontend/src/app/dashboard/bookings/page.tsx L99-104`  ·  **Категория:** correctness
- **Проблема:** In `visible`, the date filter is applied only when `view === "day"` (`if (view === "day") base = base.filter(r => r.date === selectedISO)`). In week view no date scoping is applied at all, so the list shows every booking in `rows` (up to limit=200) regardless of which week the week-strip is showing. The header/strip imply the user navigated to a specific week, but the week list shows unrelated past/future bookings, and the '%n ta yozilish' counter is also wrong for the week. Fix: in week view, filter to the displayed week, e.g. compute the set of ISO dates from `weekDays` and `base = base.filter(r => weekISOs.has(r.date))` (or filter by r.date being within weekDays[0]..weekDays[6]).
- **Проверка:** Confirmed at frontend/src/app/dashboard/bookings/page.tsx lines 99-104. The `visible` useMemo applies the date filter ONLY in day view: `if (view === "day") base = base.filter((r) => r.date === selectedISO);`. There is no equivalent scoping for week view, so `base` stays equal to all `rows`, which are fetched with `/api/business/me/bookings?limit=200` (line 71) across every date. The week-view branch (lines 272-298) renders `visible.map(...)` directly, so it lists every booking regardless of the week shown by `weekDays`. Consequences are real and user-facing: (1) the week list shows unrelated past/future bookings; (2) the "ta yozilish" counter at line 215 (`visible.length`) is wrong for the week; (3) the prev/next week arrows (lines 132-141, 186-195) mutate `selected` -> `weekDays`/`selectedISO`, but since week view ignores `selectedISO`, navigating weeks does nothing to the list (no-op); (4) the empty state "Yozilish yo'q" (lines 274-280) will essentially never appear in week view if any booking exists anywhere. The proposed fix (filter to ISO dates derived from `weekDays`) is correct. Severity downgraded from high to medium: this is a clear correctness defect breaking the week feature, but each card still displays its own `b.date` (line 285) so data isn't mislabeled, and there is no security or data-integrity impact.

### 29. [medium] total_spent never returned by backend -> every client shows blank '— so'm'
- **Область:** `fe:dash-clients`  ·  **Файл:** `frontend/src/app/dashboard/clients/page.tsx L177`  ·  **Категория:** data-integrity
- **Проблема:** The card renders fmtSum(r.total_spent) with a 'so‘m' label, but the list endpoint backend/app/routers/clients.py:51-62 only returns id, telegram_id, first_name, last_name, phone, visits, last_visit — it never selects/sums any amount. So r.total_spent is always undefined; fmtSum(undefined) returns '—' (utils.ts:2). Every client therefore shows '— so‘m', and the ClientSheet revenue tile (ClientSheet.tsx:68,137) always shows 0. The Row type marks total_spent optional which hides the gap at compile time. Fix: have list_clients aggregate paid/total amount (e.g. SUM over bookings/payments) and include total_spent in the response, or remove the misleading money display until the data exists.
- **Проверка:** Verified all cited code. frontend/src/app/dashboard/clients/page.tsx:222 renders fmtSum(r.total_spent) with a "so'm" label (line 224). The list endpoint backend/app/routers/clients.py:54-65 returns a dict containing only id, telegram_id, first_name, last_name, phone, visits, last_visit — no total_spent key, and the query (lines 32-53) only computes count(Booking.id) and max(Booking.date), never summing any amount. fmtSum in frontend/src/components/yz/utils.ts:1-4 returns "—" when its arg is null/undefined (n == null), so every card shows "— so'm". The ClientSheet path is also affected: page.tsx:197 passes total_spent: r.total_spent (undefined) into the sheet, ClientSheet.tsx:68 does const spent = client.total_spent ?? 0, and the tile at ClientSheet.tsx:137 renders fmtSum based on spent, so it always shows 0; the client_detail endpoint (clients.py:93-125) likewise never returns total_spent. The Row type (page.tsx:51) marks total_spent optional, masking the gap at compile time. The data to fix it exists (Booking.payment_amount, Service.price, Payment.amount) but is not aggregated. The defect is genuine and user-visible across all clients. I lowered severity from high to medium: it is purely a cosmetic/data-display defect with no security, crash, or data-integrity (corruption) consequence — figures simply render blank or 0, degrading gracefully.

### 30. [medium] Staff create-then-assign partial failure orphans a record and duplicates on retry
- **Область:** `fe:dash-services+staff`  ·  **Файл:** `frontend/src/app/dashboard/staff/page.tsx L234-278`  ·  **Категория:** data-integrity
- **Проблема:** save() does two sequential HTTP calls for a new staff member: POST /staff (creates the row, returns id), then PUT /staff/{id}/services. If the second call fails (e.g. AssignServicesBody validation returns 400 'One or more service ids are invalid', or a transient network error), the catch only shows a toast and does NOT call onSaved(); the sheet stays open with initial still null. The staff row already exists in the DB but the list is never reloaded, so it is invisible. When the owner presses Saqlash again, initial?.id is still undefined, so a SECOND POST /staff runs, creating a duplicate staff member. Fix: after a successful create, store the returned id in state (or mutate initial) so a retry updates instead of re-creating; alternatively reload on any outcome, or make the backend create+assign atomic in a single endpoint.
- **Проверка:** Verified against frontend/src/app/dashboard/staff/page.tsx and backend/app/routers/staff.py. save() (page.tsx lines 234-278) does POST /api/business/me/staff then PUT /api/business/me/staff/{id}/services. On the create path the new id is stored only in a local `let id` variable (line 262) and never written to component state or to `initial`. The parent renders the sheet with initial={editing} (line 186), which is null during create and is never updated by the child, so there is no path to feed the created id back. The second call can genuinely fail: backend assign_services raises HTTPException(400, "One or more service ids are invalid") at staff.py line 192-193 when a service id no longer belongs to the business (e.g. deleted between load and save), and any transient network error also throws — apiFetch (lib/api.ts lines 98-123) turns every non-2xx/network failure into a thrown Error. The catch (page.tsx line 273-274) only shows a toast and never calls onSaved(); onSaved()->load() runs only on success (line 272). Result: the staff row created by the POST exists in the DB but the list is not reloaded (stays invisible), and pressing Saqlash again re-enters the create branch because initial?.id is still undefined (line 241), issuing a SECOND POST and creating a duplicate. All four claims in the finding hold. Downgraded from high to medium: the impact is duplicate/orphaned staff records causing owner confusion and clutter, not data loss, security exposure, or corruption of existing bookings, and it requires a partial-failure window plus a user retry. The fix is as described — persist created.id into state/initial so a retry updates instead of recreating, or reload the list on any outcome, or make create+assign a single atomic endpoint.

### 31. [medium] Period-over-period % change compares a series to its own first half (wrong logic)
- **Область:** `fe:dash-analytics`  ·  **Файл:** `frontend/src/app/dashboard/analytics/page.tsx L49-55, 59, 67-69`  ·  **Категория:** correctness
- **Проблема:** prevSummary.revenue is the sum of the FIRST HALF of the `rev` series (r.slice(0, half)), and revSum is the sum of the WHOLE series. pctChange = (revSum - firstHalf) / firstHalf. Because revSum already contains firstHalf, this is not current-period vs previous-period; it measures (whole / first-half) which is always >= ~100% growth whenever the second half is non-zero and structurally inflated. The correct comparison would be secondHalf vs firstHalf: prev = sum(first half), current = sum(second half). Additionally the headline number shown is summary.revenue (summary endpoint) while pctChange is computed from revSum (revenue endpoint) — two different data sources, so the badge can contradict the displayed total. Fix: derive both halves from the same series and compute (secondHalf - firstHalf)/firstHalf, or fetch a real previous-period figure from the backend.
- **Проверка:** Verified against frontend/src/app/dashboard/analytics/page.tsx. Line 50-51: `half = Math.floor(r.length/2)` then `prev = r.slice(0, half).reduce(...)` — prevSummary.revenue is the FIRST HALF of the rev series. Line 59: `revSum = rev.reduce(...)` is the sum of the WHOLE series. Line 67-68: `pctChange = round(((revSum - prevSummary.revenue) / prevSummary.revenue) * 100)`.

Because revSum = firstHalf + secondHalf, the expression (revSum - firstHalf)/firstHalf algebraically equals secondHalf/firstHalf, NOT the intended period-over-period growth (secondHalf - firstHalf)/firstHalf. The result is inflated by a constant +100 percentage points: equal halves (true 0% growth) render as "+100% o'tgan davrga". Whenever the second half is non-empty and the first half is non-zero, the badge is >= ~100% and structurally biased positive. The math defect in the finding is exactly correct.

The secondary observation is also accurate: the headline number is summary.revenue (line 121-123, fetched from /analytics/summary?period=... at line 40-42), while pctChange is computed from revSum/prevSummary derived from /analytics/revenue?days=... (line 31-33). Two different endpoints feed the displayed total vs the change badge, so they can disagree.

This is a real correctness bug in a user-facing analytics metric. It is not a security or data-integrity issue and is display-only (a vanity growth badge), so I correct severity from high to medium. The cited lines and logic are accurate, so this is not a false positive.

### 32. [medium] pollStatus interval leaks and can run concurrently; setState after unmount
- **Область:** `fe:dash-profile+settings+security`  ·  **Файл:** `frontend/src/app/dashboard/settings/page.tsx L119-140, 111`  ·  **Категория:** reliability
- **Проблема:** pollStatus() creates a setInterval (every 4s, up to 10 min) but stores neither the interval id nor the timeout id in a ref/state, and there is no useEffect cleanup. (1) Leak/unmount: if the user navigates away from Settings before the tx completes, the interval keeps firing for up to 10 minutes calling setStatus/setSub on an unmounted component (React warning + wasted polling). (2) Concurrency: uploadReceipt() calls pollStatus(info.transaction_id) every time the user clicks 'Chekni yuborish'; a second upload (e.g. after a transient error, or re-uploading) starts a SECOND interval while the first is still running, so two pollers hit the API in parallel and race on setStatus. Fix: keep the interval id in a useRef, clearInterval before starting a new poll, and clear it in a useEffect(() => () => clearInterval(ref.current), []) cleanup on unmount.
- **Проверка:** Verified against frontend/src/app/dashboard/settings/page.tsx lines 119-140. pollStatus() creates setInterval (line 120, every 4s) and a setTimeout safety clear (line 139, 10 min), storing both only in the local variable `interval`. There is NO useRef and NO useEffect unmount cleanup anywhere in the file (confirmed via grep: clearInterval appears only at lines 125/134 inside the interval's own terminal-state branches, and line 139's timeout). 

Leak on unmount (real): if the user navigates away from /dashboard/settings while polling is in flight, the interval is never cleared on unmount and keeps firing for up to 10 minutes, calling apiFetch /api/payments/status/{txId} and setStatus/setSub (lines 122-132) against an unmounted component. Wasted polling (~up to 150 calls) and stale-closure setState are genuine. (React 18 suppresses the unmounted-setState console warning, so that specific symptom in the report is outdated, but the wasted work is real.)

Concurrency (real but narrower than implied): pollStatus is invoked only at line 111 in uploadReceipt, which is wired to the "Chekni yuborish" button (line 430) that is disabled while uploading (line 431 disabled={!file || uploading}). So a double-click during one upload cannot fire two pollers. However, after the first upload finishes (uploading resets at line 115) the button re-enables; since info and file both persist in state, the user can click again (e.g. re-upload for the same transaction_id), and uploadReceipt's guard `if (!info || !file) return` passes, so pollStatus is called a SECOND time at line 111 while the first interval is still alive — two pollers then race on setStatus. This is a plausible (not contrived) sequence.

Net: a genuine reliability defect. The proposed fix (interval id in useRef, clearInterval before starting a new poll, and a useEffect cleanup on unmount) is correct. Severity downgraded from high to medium: no data/security/correctness impact, the worst case is bounded wasted polling that self-terminates after the 10-minute safety timeout, and the concurrency path requires a deliberate re-upload.


## Все находки по областям (235)

### `bot:booking` — partial (3 находок)
_backend/bot/handlers/booking.py implements the full Telegram booking FSM: service -> (optional staff) -> date -> time -> promo -> phone-capture (first time) -> confirm, delegating creation to booking_service.create_booking (which holds a slot lock, checks per-staff/per-business conflicts, and is idempotent for the same client+slot). The single-resource flow is solid and end-to-end correct. The multi-staff flow is broken: the slot list shown to the client ignores the chosen staff, so it is simultaneously over-restrictive and inconsistent with the per-staff conflict check used at confirm. There is also no guard against booking times that have already passed today._
- **[high]** Slot availability shown ignores selected staff (per-business) while conflict check is per-staff — `backend/bot/handlers/booking.py L303`
  - pick_day calls get_available_slots(b.id, d, service.duration_minutes, db), which in backend/app/utils/slots.py (get_available_slots / get_bookings_for_date, lines 35-96) filters bookings ONLY by business_id and date with no staff filter. But the chosen staff is stored in FSM state (staff_id, set in pick_staff line 277) and create_booking validates conflicts PER-STAFF when staff_id is set (_check_slot_available, booking_service.py lines 93-126). Net effect for any business with 2+ staff: (a) a slot is hidden from EVERY client as soon as ANY one staff is booked at that time, so parallel bookings across staff are impossible from the bot even though the backend would allow them; (b) the times offered for staff A do not reflect staff A's real availability. Fix: thread staff_id through to get_available_slots and filter existing_bookings by staff_id when set (keep per-business behaviour when staff_id is empty/any), so displayed slots match the conflict semantics used at confirm.
- **[medium]** No guard against booking past times for today — `backend/bot/handlers/booking.py L303`
  - For d == today ('Bugun'), get_available_slots (app/utils/slots.py lines 47-96) enumerates slots from schedule.start_time with no comparison to current local time, and create_booking (booking_service.py) has no past-time validation either (grep found no now/past check in either file). A client opening the bot at 15:00 is offered and can confirm a 10:00 slot the same day, creating a booking in the past that then triggers owner notification and a '1 soat oldin eslatma' reminder for a time already gone. Fix: in get_available_slots, when d == local_today(), skip slots whose start is <= local_now(); optionally also reject past datetimes in create_booking as a server-side guard.
- **[low]** Promo discount computed against stale base_price captured at prompt time — `backend/bot/handlers/booking.py L621`
  - validate_promo_for_business is called with base_price from FSM state captured at prom_y time (line 553/564) from service.price. If the service price changes between entering the promo flow and confirming, the discount summary shown to the client (line 655) is computed against a stale base_price, while create_booking later recomputes payment from the current service. This is a display-vs-actual-charge consistency gap rather than a hard bug; consider validating base_price against the live service price inside _create_booking_sync.
  - ✅ Работает: Slot creation race is handled correctly in the service layer: create_booking acquires a slot lock (_acquire_slot_lock), then re-checks availability (_check_slot_available) before inserting, and is idempotent for the same client+exact slot (returns the existing PENDING/CONFIRMED booking) so double-clicks/retries do not error or duplicate.; All DB sessions are opened from SessionLocal and reliably closed in finally blocks; synchronous DB work (validate_promo, create_booking, save/read client phone, join waitlist) is correctly offloaded via asyncio.to_thread so the async event loop is not blocked.; staff_id is consistently carried through the FSM across the promo reset (pick_time/prom_n re-stash it after state.clear) and across the phone-capture detour (confirm_booking re-stashes sid/d_iso/t_str/promo_code/staff_id before set_state), and 'any master' maps to staff_id='' -> staff_uuid=None which correctly routes to the legacy per-business conflict path.; Phone capture validates the shared contact actually belongs to the sender (contact.user_id != message.from_user.id is rejected) and normalizes to +-prefixed form before saving.; Error mapping (_booking_error_text) translates backend ValueErrors (subscription/slot/service/business) into localized user messages instead of leaking raw exceptions, and create_booking failures roll back the session.; The 'all slots booked' dead-end is turned into a waitlist opt-in (wl: callback -> _join_waitlist_sync), which is idempotent via the waitlist unique constraint and commits its own transaction.

### `bot:mybookings+owner` — partial (6 находок)
_These two aiogram handlers cover the client "my bookings" experience (list active/completed bookings, leave/edit a star review, cancel) and the owner-side confirm/reject flow with reason selection and client notifications. The happy paths work and permission checks are present (client ownership on cancel/review; business-owner ownership on confirm/reject). However there are real defects: owner_confirm can resurrect a cancelled/no-show/completed booking, service names are interpolated into HTML notifications without escaping, the cancel-window timezone computation is wrong on the UTC host, and all DB access is synchronous inside async handlers, blocking the event loop._
- **[high]** owner_confirm can resurrect a cancelled/no-show/completed booking — `backend/bot/handlers/owner.py L39-43`
  - owner_confirm only short-circuits when status is already CONFIRMED. For any other status (CANCELLED, NO_SHOW, COMPLETED) it sets status=CONFIRMED and notifies the client. An owner pressing an old 'confirm' button on a booking the client already cancelled (cxl:) or that was auto-flipped to NO_SHOW will flip it back to CONFIRMED and send '✅ Yozilishingiz tasdiqlandi!' for a slot that no longer exists. Fix: only allow the transition from PENDING (e.g. `if booking.status != BookingStatus.PENDING: cb.answer('...'); return`).
- **[high]** Cancel-window timezone uses server-local time, not Asia/Tashkent — `backend/app/services/booking_service.py L384`
  - cancel_booking (reached from my_bookings.py:370 with by_client=True) computes `now_local = datetime.now(tz.utc).astimezone().replace(tzinfo=None)`. `.astimezone()` converts to the *server* timezone. The whole point of app/utils/clock.py is that Render runs in UTC while the business is Asia/Tashkent (UTC+5). So on the real host now_local is effectively UTC, and the `slot_dt - now_local < window_hours` late-cancel test is off by 5 hours — clients can be wrongly flagged (or wrongly not flagged) for late cancellation right at the boundary. Fix: use `local_now().replace(tzinfo=None)` from app.utils.clock instead of `.astimezone()`.
- **[medium]** Unescaped service name in HTML Telegram notification — `backend/bot/handlers/owner.py L51-69`
  - send_telegram_message sends with parse_mode='HTML' (notification_service.py:35). owner_confirm interpolates svc_name raw into the message body (`📋 {svc_name}`). A service name containing '<', '>' or '&' (e.g. 'Strijka < 15 min' or 'Mama & me') produces invalid HTML; Telegram returns a 400 and the confirmation notification is silently dropped (the except: pass at owner.py:73 hides it). The rest of the codebase escapes user text via app.utils.htmlsafe.h() — this path doesn't. Fix: wrap svc_name with h() before building the text, and also escape the reject `reason` if it ever becomes free-form.
- **[medium]** Synchronous DB session used directly inside async handlers blocks the event loop — `backend/bot/handlers/my_bookings.py L25-95`
  - Every handler in both files opens a blocking `SessionLocal()` and runs `db.query(...).all()/.first()` and `db.commit()` directly in the async coroutine (my_bookings.py:25-95, 101-134, 287-353, 359-374; owner.py:26-55, 89-113). These synchronous psycopg/SQLAlchemy calls block the single aiogram event loop for the duration of the DB round-trip, so one slow query stalls every other user's bot interaction. Note the owner notification correctly uses `asyncio.to_thread(send_telegram_message, ...)` for the HTTP call but not for the DB work. Fix: wrap the DB blocks in `await asyncio.to_thread(...)` (as already done for telegram sends), or move the bot to the async session used elsewhere in the project.
- **[medium]** Clients can rate a service before the appointment happens — `backend/bot/handlers/my_bookings.py L70`
  - The '⭐ Baho berish' button is rendered for active bookings (PENDING/CONFIRMED) at line 70, and start_review (205) / _save_review_from_state (289) only reject CANCELLED bookings — they accept PENDING/CONFIRMED. So a client who just booked for next week can immediately post a review that counts toward the business's public rating, before any visit. This pollutes the rating aggregate with reviews for services not yet delivered. Fix: only allow reviews for COMPLETED bookings (and standalone reviews), i.e. gate start_review / _save_review on `booking.status == COMPLETED`, and don't show the review button on active bookings.
- **[low]** N+1 queries when listing bookings — `backend/bot/handlers/my_bookings.py L55-93`
  - cmd_mybookings loops over up to 20 active + 20 completed bookings and issues 3 separate queries per booking (Business, Service, Review) at lines 56-58 and 76-78 — up to ~120 round trips per /mybookings. my_from_menu repeats this per booking at line 129. Combined with the synchronous-session issue above, each round trip blocks the loop. Fix: batch-load businesses/services/reviews by collected ids (single IN query each) or use joinedload/selectinload.
  - ✅ Работает: Cancel and review handlers enforce client ownership correctly: they look up the Client by cb.from_user.id and verify booking.client_id == client.id before acting (my_bookings.py:212, 294, 363).; Owner confirm/reject verify business ownership via biz.owner_id == owner.id and return 'Ruxsat yo'q' otherwise (owner.py:36, 97), so a non-owner cannot confirm/reject another business's bookings.; Rating input is validated: callback data is split with a fixed length check, parsed with int() inside try/except, and bounded 1<=rating<=5 before use (my_bookings.py:176-188, 228-240).; Client cancel is routed through booking_service.cancel_booking with by_client=True so the cancel-window/late_cancel policy is applied rather than naively flipping status in the handler (my_bookings.py:368-370).; User-supplied text shown back in bot messages is HTML-escaped via h() (business/service names, status) in the listing handlers (my_bookings.py:60-93, 130), and comment length is capped at 2000 chars (line 270).; Telegram send failures are isolated: notifications run via asyncio.to_thread and send_telegram_message swallows/logs HTTP errors, so a blocked or deleted client chat does not crash the owner's confirm/reject flow.

### `comp:booking-sheets` — partial (4 находок)
_Three React components for the owner dashboard: BookingCard/TimelineBlock (read-only list/timeline tiles), BookingSheet (view + confirm/complete/cancel + inline edit of an existing booking), and NewBookingSheet (4-step wizard to create a booking). The create/edit happy paths work and the backend re-validates and recomputes end_time/price and does proper slot-conflict checking with advisory locks, so data integrity at the DB level is sound. However the slot-picker in NewBookingSheet has real correctness defects: it marks slots busy by exact start-time only (ignoring duration overlap) and counts cancelled/completed bookings as busy, so the UI both hides genuinely-free slots and offers slots the backend will reject. Net verdict: functional but with slot-picking logic that diverges from the backend's actual availability rules._
- **[medium]** busySlots counts cancelled/completed bookings as busy, blocking free slots — `frontend/src/components/yz/NewBookingSheet.tsx L89-94`
  - The availability fetch GET /api/business/me/bookings?booking_date=${date} passes no status filter, so the list endpoint returns bookings of ALL statuses (it defaults to no status filter, bookings.py:262-276). busySlots is built from every returned row's start_time. But the backend conflict check only considers PENDING and CONFIRMED (bookings.py:217). Result: a slot whose only booking is CANCELLED or COMPLETED is shown disabled/line-through in the grid, so the owner cannot book a genuinely-free slot. Fix: request only active statuses, e.g. fetch with ?status=PENDING and ?status=CONFIRMED (or add a server param), or filter rows client-side to status in [PENDING, CONFIRMED] before building the Set.
- **[medium]** Slot picker ignores service duration, so multi-slot bookings are not blocked and rejected slots are offered — `frontend/src/components/yz/NewBookingSheet.tsx L91-92, 274-279`
  - busySlots is a Set of exact start-time strings ('HH:MM') and a grid cell is disabled only when busySlots.has(t) is an exact match. The backend treats availability as interval overlap (start < end AND end > start, bookings.py:218-219). A 90-minute service booked at 14:00 occupies 14:00-15:30, but the 15:00 grid cell is NOT marked busy because no booking *starts* at 15:00 — the user can select 15:00 and the create call then fails with HTTP 400 'Vaqt band'. Conversely the new service's own duration isn't considered against later bookings either. Fix: compute occupancy as intervals — for each active booking expand [start, end) and disable any grid slot t where [t, t+service.duration_minutes) overlaps an occupied interval.
- **[low]** Time step has no validation; default 14:00 can advance into a busy/invalid slot — `frontend/src/components/yz/NewBookingSheet.tsx L105-106, 62`
  - canNext returns true unconditionally for step===2, and time defaults to '14:00' (or defaultTime) without checking it against busySlots. If 14:00 is busy the cell is disabled but the state value is still '14:00', so the user can press 'Davom etish' and later hit a backend 'Vaqt band' on confirm. There is also no guard that the selected slot is one of the rendered options or that it is not in the past for today's date. Fix: in the step-2 branch require !busySlots.has(time) (and optionally a future-time check) before allowing next, and reset/clear time when it becomes invalid after a date change.
- **[low]** NewBookingSheet shows a fixed 09:00-18:00 hourly grid regardless of business working hours or service duration — `frontend/src/components/yz/NewBookingSheet.tsx L261-294`
  - The slot grid is hardcoded to ten hourly slots 09:00-18:00 and never consults the business schedule or the service duration. Businesses open outside these hours (or with 30/45-min services) cannot pick correct slots from this wizard, and slots after closing time are offered. This is a product-correctness gap rather than a crash. Fix: derive slot list from the business working-hours/schedule endpoint and step by the selected service's duration.
  - ✅ Работает: Mutations (confirm/complete/cancel/edit/create) all set busy/saving, disable buttons, toast on error, and close the sheet only on success; finally blocks always clear the busy flag.; BookingSheet edit and NewBookingSheet create both let the backend own end_time/price recomputation and conflict validation rather than trusting client-sent values (the client-computed end_time in finish() is redundant but harmless).; useEffect on [open, booking] correctly re-seeds the edit form fields and resets editing=false when the sheet closes, avoiding stale form state across openings.; Backend create/edit endpoints (bookings.py) use acquire_slot_lock plus SELECT FOR UPDATE and an interval-overlap predicate (start < new_end AND end > new_start) restricted to PENDING/CONFIRMED, which correctly serializes concurrent slot writes.; fmtSum/hm/durationMin/isoFor utilities are null-safe and isoFor builds the date string from local Y-M-D parts (no UTC off-by-one from toISOString).

### `core:config+db+deps` — partial (4 находок)
_These three files hold settings (Pydantic BaseSettings with production guards), the SQLAlchemy engine/session factory, and FastAPI dependency-injection auth guards. The wiring is coherent and works for the common case (sync sessions, JWT bearer auth, owner/membership business resolution). However the engine/sessions are synchronous yet several route handlers are declared async def, so blocking DB and file IO runs on the event loop; the production secret-key check keys off the wrong source (os.getenv vs the parsed field) and can be silently skipped; a download guard accepts the access token as a URL query param; and the role-restriction machinery (require_role) is defined but never wired anywhere._
- **[high]** Sync DB session + blocking IO used inside async route handlers blocks the event loop — `backend/app/database.py L17-27`
  - database.py builds a synchronous engine (create_engine) and SessionLocal, and get_db() yields a sync Session. Several route handlers are declared `async def` while taking `db: Session = Depends(get_db)` and then calling blocking sync ORM/IO directly on the event loop — e.g. files.py:115 upload_logo (`db.commit()` + `path.write_bytes()`), files.py:207 upload_photo, payments.py:175 upload_receipt, and webhooks payments.py:427/454. FastAPI does NOT offload `async def` handlers to a threadpool, so each blocking db.query/db.commit/file write stalls the whole worker's event loop, serializing concurrent requests and risking timeouts under load. Fix: drop `async` from handlers that only do sync DB/file work (FastAPI then runs them in a threadpool, safe for sync sessions), or migrate to async SQLAlchemy (create_async_engine/AsyncSession) and await the DB calls; for handlers that must stay async (await file.read()), wrap blocking calls in run_in_threadpool/asyncio.to_thread.
- **[high]** Production secret-key strength check reads os.getenv('APP_ENV') instead of the parsed app_env field — `backend/app/config.py L23-34`
  - validate_secret_key gates the weak-secret rejection on `os.getenv('APP_ENV','development').lower() == 'production'`. But app_env is a real settings field that can be supplied via the .env file (model_config env_file='.env'). If a deployment sets app_env=production in .env (or any non-env-var source) without ALSO exporting the APP_ENV process env var, os.getenv returns 'development' and the check is skipped — allowing the default 'change_me' or a <32-char SECRET_KEY in production, which makes HS256 JWTs forgeable (utils/auth.py signs with settings.secret_key). The model_validator validate_production uses self.app_env correctly for other checks but does NOT re-validate secret_key, so there is no backstop. Fix: validate secret_key inside the after-model validator using self.app_env (authoritative, fully parsed), e.g. append to errors when secret_key.lower() in _INSECURE_DEFAULTS or len(secret_key) < 32.
- **[medium]** Download auth accepts JWT access token as a URL query parameter (?token=) — `backend/app/deps.py L35-58`
  - get_owned_business_download accepts the access token via `?token=` query string for browser-tab downloads. Access tokens in URLs leak into web-server/proxy/CDN access logs, browser history, and the Referer header sent to any third-party resource the page loads. With a 60-minute access-token lifetime (config.access_token_expire_minutes=60) a leaked URL grants account access for up to an hour. The same pattern backs SSE/notification and PDF endpoints (business.py:386, files.py:91). Fix: mint a short-lived, single-purpose download token (separate `type`, ~1-2 min, scoped to the resource) instead of reusing the full access token; set Referrer-Policy: no-referrer on these responses and strip query strings from proxy logs.
- **[low]** Role-based access control (require_role) is defined but never used; get_active_business grants any membership role full access — `backend/app/deps.py L91-163`
  - require_role(*allowed) is a dependency factory meant to enforce OWNER/MANAGER/STAFF restrictions, but a repo-wide search shows zero call sites — it is dead code. get_active_business validates only that a Membership row exists for (user, business) with ANY role (deps.py:117-126), so a STAFF member resolves the active business identically to an OWNER. Because require_role is never layered on top, routers using get_active_business treat STAFF the same as OWNER/MANAGER — the role column carries no enforced privilege separation. Latent authorization gap (most routers still use owner-only get_owned_business) rather than an active exploit, but the documented STAFF/MANAGER permission model is unenforced. Fix: wire require_role(...) onto write/billing endpoints that should be owner/manager-only, or remove the unused machinery so it doesn't imply protection that isn't there. (The role comparison `m.role not in {r.value for r in allowed} | set(allowed)` is itself correct since Membership.role is a MembershipRole(str, Enum).)
  - ✅ Работает: JWT auth guard get_current_user correctly rejects missing creds, non-bearer schemes, invalid/expired tokens (get_user_from_token catches JWTError/ValueError), token type != 'access', and inactive users.; get_user_from_token enforces payload type=='access', preventing refresh tokens from being used as access tokens.; get_db uses try/finally to always close the session, avoiding connection leaks.; Engine is configured with sensible pool hygiene: pool_pre_ping=True, pool_recycle=1800, and bounded pool_size/max_overflow.; validate_production (model_validator) uses the parsed self.app_env and aggregates clear errors for bot_token, database_url, cors_origins, public_api_url, and webhook_secret in production.; webhook_secret defaults to a per-process random (secrets.token_hex) so dev is safe by default, with a documented requirement to pin it in production.

### `fe:dash-analytics` — partial (4 находок)
_The analytics page fetches four endpoints (revenue, bookings-by-day, popular-services, summary), renders a revenue hero card with a bar chart, four MiniStat tiles, and a popular-services list. Network/error handling is solid (each fetch has a .catch fallback) and empty states exist for the popular-services list. However the headline "revenue" bar chart actually plots booking COUNTS, not revenue, and the period-over-period percentage change is computed with broken logic comparing a series to its own first half. It renders without crashing but presents misleading numbers, hence partial._
- **[high]** Revenue card's bar chart plots booking counts, not revenue — `frontend/src/app/dashboard/analytics/page.tsx L60-64, 140-144`
  - The hero card is titled 'Davr daromadi' (period revenue) and shows summary.revenue, but the bar chart under it is fed `bars`, which is derived from `bookings` (the /bookings-by-day endpoint, value = x.bookings), not from the `rev` revenue series. The `rev` data is fetched but never charted (only summed for revSum/pctChange). So users see a revenue card whose graph and tooltip show daily booking COUNTS. Fix: build `bars` from `rev` (e.g. map rev.slice(-7) -> { day: weekday(x.date), value: x.amount }) so the chart matches the card, or relabel/move the chart. If both metrics are wanted, render two charts with correct sources.
- **[high]** Period-over-period % change compares a series to its own first half (wrong logic) — `frontend/src/app/dashboard/analytics/page.tsx L49-55, 59, 67-69`
  - prevSummary.revenue is the sum of the FIRST HALF of the `rev` series (r.slice(0, half)), and revSum is the sum of the WHOLE series. pctChange = (revSum - firstHalf) / firstHalf. Because revSum already contains firstHalf, this is not current-period vs previous-period; it measures (whole / first-half) which is always >= ~100% growth whenever the second half is non-zero and structurally inflated. The correct comparison would be secondHalf vs firstHalf: prev = sum(first half), current = sum(second half). Additionally the headline number shown is summary.revenue (summary endpoint) while pctChange is computed from revSum (revenue endpoint) — two different data sources, so the badge can contradict the displayed total. Fix: derive both halves from the same series and compute (secondHalf - firstHalf)/firstHalf, or fetch a real previous-period figure from the backend.
- **[low]** Highlight bar defaults to index 0 even when all values are zero — `frontend/src/app/dashboard/analytics/page.tsx L65`
  - highlightIdx is reduced with `cur.value >= (bars[acc]?.value || 0)` seeded at 0; when every bar is 0 the first bar is still painted as the highlighted (#FFC94A) bar, implying a 'best day' that doesn't exist. Minor but misleading on empty/no-activity periods. Fix: only highlight when maxBar > 0 (e.g. set highlightIdx = -1 when all values are 0).
- **[low]** Weekday label derived from date-only string can shift across timezones — `frontend/src/app/dashboard/analytics/page.tsx L61-62`
  - new Date(x.date).getDay() parses a date-only ISO string (e.g. '2026-06-28') as UTC midnight, then getDay() returns the weekday in the browser's local timezone. For Uzbekistan (UTC+5) this stays on the same calendar day so the label is correct, but for any user/browser at a negative UTC offset the bar would be labelled with the previous weekday. Fix: parse explicitly or split the string ('2026-06-28'.split('-')) to build a local Date, avoiding the UTC-vs-local shift.
  - ✅ Работает: Each of the four parallel apiFetch calls has a .catch fallback to a safe default ([] or zeroed summary), so a failing endpoint degrades gracefully instead of crashing the page.; The popular-services list has a proper empty state ('Hali ma'lumot yo'q') when popular.length === 0.; RevenueChart is dynamically imported with ssr:false and a loading placeholder, correctly avoiding SSR issues with recharts and reserving layout height.; Average-check tile guards against division by zero (summary.bookings_count ? ... : '—').; Popular-services bar width uses Math.max(8, pct) so tiny shares remain visible, and topTotal>0 is guarded before computing percentages.; useEffect correctly re-runs on [period] and the chart re-renders with new data.

### `fe:dash-bookings` — partial (4 находок)
_A client-side bookings screen with a week-day strip, day/week view toggle, status filters, an hourly day timeline (with empty-slot create buttons), and detail/new booking sheets. It loads bookings/services/clients in parallel and refreshes on a custom window event. The day view and core data flow work, but the "week" view does not actually scope to the selected week, and a couple of robustness/correctness issues exist around multi-hour/sub-hour bookings and the day-view empty state._
- **[high]** Week view ignores the selected week — lists ALL bookings across all dates — `frontend/src/app/dashboard/bookings/page.tsx L99-104`
  - In `visible`, the date filter is applied only when `view === "day"` (`if (view === "day") base = base.filter(r => r.date === selectedISO)`). In week view no date scoping is applied at all, so the list shows every booking in `rows` (up to limit=200) regardless of which week the week-strip is showing. The header/strip imply the user navigated to a specific week, but the week list shows unrelated past/future bookings, and the '%n ta yozilish' counter is also wrong for the week. Fix: in week view, filter to the displayed week, e.g. compute the set of ISO dates from `weekDays` and `base = base.filter(r => weekISOs.has(r.date))` (or filter by r.date being within weekDays[0]..weekDays[6]).
- **[medium]** Multi-hour bookings render only in their start hour; sub-hour ordering lost — `frontend/src/app/dashboard/bookings/page.tsx L242`
  - `matching = visible.filter(b => parseInt(b.start_time) === h)` buckets a booking solely by its start hour and ignores end_time. A booking 14:00–16:00 appears only in the 14:00 row and leaves 15:00 looking free (it even shows a 'Bo'sh slot' create button at 15:00, inviting a double-book). Also, bookings at e.g. 09:00 and 09:30 share one hour cell with no minute-based sort, so visual order is just array order. Fix: either render blocks proportionally to duration (using durationMin) or at minimum mark hours covered by an in-progress booking as occupied so the empty-slot button isn't shown over a booked span.
- **[low]** Day view never shows an empty state when there are no bookings — `frontend/src/app/dashboard/bookings/page.tsx L240-270`
  - `hours` always seeds DEFAULT_HOURS (08..19), so the day timeline always renders 12 hour rows of dashed 'Bo'sh slot' buttons even when the day has zero bookings. The friendly 'Yozilish yo'q' empty state (CalendarX2) exists only in the week branch. Not a crash, but the day view gives no clear 'nothing booked today' signal. Consider showing the empty state (or a hint) when the day's filtered list is empty.
- **[low]** Empty-slot create button passes hour-only time as default, may collide with NewBookingSheet validation — `frontend/src/app/dashboard/bookings/page.tsx L251 / 315`
  - `onClick={() => setNewOpen(hStr)}` sets `newOpen` to e.g. '09:00' and passes it as `defaultTime`. This is fine for whole hours, but combined with the multi-hour gap above, the dashed create button can appear on an hour already occupied by an in-progress booking (14:00–16:00 booking still shows a create button at 15:00), letting the user start a booking that overlaps an existing one. Server-side overlap validation (if any) is the real safeguard; verify NewBookingSheet/backend reject overlapping slots, otherwise this UI actively encourages double-booking.
  - ✅ Работает: isoFor/weekdayShort use local date components (getFullYear/getMonth/getDate), so the day key matches the user's local timezone and avoids the classic UTC off-by-one date bug; load() uses Promise.all with per-request .catch(() => []), so one failing endpoint doesn't blank the whole screen; weekDays computes Monday-start correctly via (getDay()+6)%7 and mutates only cloned Date objects, not the state Date; The hours set widens DEFAULT_HOURS to include any booking hour outside 08-19, so early/late bookings still render on the day timeline; Event listener for yz:bookings-changed is properly added and removed in the useEffect cleanup, no leak; Sheets are controlled correctly: onOpenChange only clears state on close (!v), and onChanged/onCreated re-run load() to refresh after mutations

### `fe:dash-clients` — partial (5 находок)
_Client-list screen: fetches /api/business/me/clients, renders cards with search + All/VIP/New filter chips, opens a ClientSheet detail (call/message/new-booking actions) and a NewBookingSheet. The list, search, last-visit and visit-count display work end-to-end, but several advertised features are dead because the list endpoint never returns the fields the UI consumes: VIP filter/badge, New filter/badge, and per-client total spent are all permanently empty/blank, and the in-sheet "block client" feature promised by the tour text does not exist in the UI at all._

The Row type marks total_spent optional which hides the gap at compile time. - **[medium]** VIP filter and VIP badge are permanently empty (is_vip never sent) — `frontend/src/app/dashboard/clients/page.tsx L81`

So the VIP chip always shows count 0, the VIP filter always yields an empty list, and the Avatar vip / YANGI-style VIP badge never appears. The feature is effectively non-functional. Fix: compute and return is_vip from the backend (e.g. spend/visit threshold), or remove the VIP chip.
- **[medium]** 'Yangi' (new) filter logic is dead: visits is always >=1 and is_new never sent — `frontend/src/app/dashboard/clients/page.tsx L82`
  - newCount and the 'new' filter use r.visits === 0 || r.is_new. But the backend list query uses an INNER JOIN on Booking (clients.py:39) and counts func.count(Booking.id), so every returned row has visits >= 1 — visits === 0 is impossible. is_new is also never returned. Result: the 'Yangi' chip always shows 0, the filter is empty, and the per-card 'YANGI' badge (line 165-169) never renders. Fix: return an explicit is_new flag from the backend (e.g. first booking within N days / visits == 1) and base the UI on that instead of visits === 0.
- **[medium]** Tour promises blocking from the client sheet, but no block UI exists — `frontend/src/components/yz/ClientSheet.tsx L91`

But ClientSheet only renders Call / Message / New-booking actions and never fetches /clients/{client_id} nor calls the block endpoint — so the documented blocking workflow is unreachable from this screen. The detail sheet also never shows visit history, NO_SHOW count or birthday that the tour and backend imply. Fix: wire ClientSheet to GET /clients/{id} and add block/unblock actions, or correct the tour copy.
- **[low]** List load failure is swallowed with no user feedback — `frontend/src/app/dashboard/clients/page.tsx L64`
  - The fetch chain does .catch(() => setLoading(false)) with no error toast or retry. On a failed /clients request the screen silently shows the empty-state 'Hali mijoz yo‘q' card, which is indistinguishable from a genuinely empty list and misleads the owner into thinking they have no clients. Fix: track an error state and render a distinct error/retry UI instead of the empty state.
  - ✅ Работает: Search is correctly memoized and filters on both full name and phone with safe null-guards (page.tsx:67-79).; last_visit is a plain YYYY-MM-DD date string from the backend, so .slice(0,10) is correct and free of timezone drift (page.tsx:172).; Distinct empty states for 'no clients yet' vs 'no match found' based on rows.length (page.tsx:122-134).; Name fallback to 'Mijoz' and null-coalescing of optional fields when building the ClientDetail prevent render crashes (page.tsx:137-155).; Backend block/unblock and detail endpoints enforce ownership via get_owned_business and _client_in_business_or_404, preventing cross-tenant client enumeration (clients.py:125-141) — the API side of blocking is solid even though the UI doesn't use it.; ClientSheet message action gracefully toasts when phone is missing instead of failing (ClientSheet.tsx:104-110).

### `fe:dash-profile+settings+security` — partial (5 находок)
_Three dashboard client pages: business profile edit (name/phone/address/description, location, bot texts, confirmation mode, logo upload/remove), settings hub (profile card, linked login methods incl. Google link/unlink, subscription card-payment flow with receipt upload + status polling, notifications toggle, tour replay, logout), and a security page to set a standalone login+password. The happy paths are wired correctly to the backend and error handling generally surfaces server `detail`. Verdict: mostly works, but the payment status poller has real lifecycle/leak bugs and the notifications toggle is non-functional, so I rate it partial._
- **[high]** pollStatus interval leaks and can run concurrently; setState after unmount — `frontend/src/app/dashboard/settings/page.tsx L119-140, 111`
  - pollStatus() creates a setInterval (every 4s, up to 10 min) but stores neither the interval id nor the timeout id in a ref/state, and there is no useEffect cleanup. (1) Leak/unmount: if the user navigates away from Settings before the tx completes, the interval keeps firing for up to 10 minutes calling setStatus/setSub on an unmounted component (React warning + wasted polling). (2) Concurrency: uploadReceipt() calls pollStatus(info.transaction_id) every time the user clicks 'Chekni yuborish'; a second upload (e.g. after a transient error, or re-uploading) starts a SECOND interval while the first is still running, so two pollers hit the API in parallel and race on setStatus. Fix: keep the interval id in a useRef, clearInterval before starting a new poll, and clear it in a useEffect(() => () => clearInterval(ref.current), []) cleanup on unmount.
- **[medium]** Notifications toggle is cosmetic only — no backend persistence — `frontend/src/app/dashboard/settings/page.tsx L148-162, 448-462`
  - toggleNotif() only writes localStorage('yozuv_notif_on') and toasts 'Bildirishnomalar yoqildi/o'chirildi'. Nothing reads this flag to actually suppress reminders/notifications (no API call, and reminders are sent server-side by the bot/Celery). The user is told notifications were turned off but they will keep arriving, and the setting does not sync across devices. Either wire it to a real backend preference endpoint or relabel/remove it so it doesn't make a false promise.
- **[low]** Receipt upload uses raw fetch, bypassing the 401-refresh-and-retry path — `frontend/src/app/dashboard/settings/page.tsx L93-117`
  - uploadReceipt() calls fetch() directly with a manually attached Bearer token instead of going through apiFetch. apiFetch transparently refreshes an expired access token and retries once (api.ts:84-95); the raw fetch does not. If the access token has expired by the time the user finishes filling the receipt form (tokens are short-lived), the upload fails with 401 and just toasts the error instead of refreshing. Note the logo upload in profile/page.tsx correctly routes FormData through apiFetch (api.ts detects FormData and skips the JSON Content-Type), so this endpoint could do the same. Fix: send the FormData via apiFetch to inherit refresh/retry.
- **[low]** Profile save sends no client-side validation; empty name/phone silently submitted — `frontend/src/app/dashboard/profile/page.tsx L111-125, 256-285`
  - save() PUTs the entire form with no required-field checks (name, phone, address are all editable to empty strings via the Field inputs). The 'Saqlash' button is never disabled for invalid state, so a user can clear the business name and save, relying entirely on the backend to reject. If the backend allows empty name, the bot greeting/profile renders blank. This is a validation gap rather than a hard bug — confirm the backend enforces name/phone non-empty; if not, add client validation (or at minimum disable Save when name is empty).
- **[low]** Phone-only accounts can never set a username via the security form — `frontend/src/app/dashboard/security/page.tsx L30, 42-48`
  - hasLogin = Boolean(username || phone). When a user has a phone but no username, hasLogin is true, so the login input is disabled and submit() sends login: undefined. The backend set_password only assigns a username when body.login is present AND !user.username (auth.py:324-343). Net effect: a phone-only user can set a password but can never choose a username login — the field is locked to their phone with no path to add one. If choosing a username is intended for such users, gate the disabled state on Boolean(me?.username) rather than on username-or-phone.
  - ✅ Работает: Logo upload validates type (image/*) and size (<=4MB) client-side before upload, routes FormData through apiFetch which correctly detects FormData and omits the JSON Content-Type, and resets the file input value in finally so re-selecting the same file refires onChange (profile/page.tsx:127-152).; apiFetch centralizes auth: single coalesced refresh-and-retry on 401, clears tokens and redirects to /auth/login on hard failure, and parses FastAPI {detail} (string or validation array) into readable error messages used by all the toasts (api.ts:84-123).; Security form gates submit correctly: password length >= 6, password === confirm, login required only when none exists, and busy guard; also shows a live 'parollar mos emas' mismatch hint (security/page.tsx:31-35, 134-136).; set-password backend guards against login clashes with a case-insensitive check against other accounts' username/phone and returns 409, preventing ambiguous password-login resolution (auth.py:324-343).; Google link flow correctly does a top-level navigation (OAuth can't carry a Bearer header) passing a short-lived token, and cleans ?linked/?link_error query params via replaceState so a refresh doesn't re-toast (settings/page.tsx:195-216).; Cascading geo selects are sound: changing viloyat resets tuman to '', the tuman select is disabled until a viloyat is chosen, and MapPicker only overwrites address when it's empty so manual input isn't clobbered (profile/page.tsx:70-81, 296, 311-335).

### `fe:dash-promo+reviews` — partial (5 находок)
_Two dashboard pages. promo/page.tsx is full CRUD for promo codes (list, create via sheet, toggle active, delete) backed by /api/business/me/promo-codes; it works end-to-end against the matching FastAPI router. reviews/page.tsx is read-only: it fetches reviews + a summary and renders an average/distribution and a list. The audit focus names "review replies," but no reply feature exists anywhere (no UI, no backend endpoint) — that capability is simply absent, not broken. The promo create flow has a real money/data-integrity trap where percent and amount discounts silently combine while the UI presents them as mutually exclusive._
- **[high]** Promo percent and amount discounts silently combine; UI claims they are exclusive — `frontend/src/app/dashboard/promo/page.tsx L44-49, 138-142, 231-251`
  - The create form labels the two inputs 'Chegirma %' and 'Yoki so‘m' (percent OR amount) and defaults discount_percent to '10'. Neither the frontend nor the backend enforces exclusivity: add() only rejects when BOTH are <=0 (line 69), and create_promo in backend/app/routers/promo.py only rejects when both are 0. But backend/app/services/booking_service.py:326 applies BOTH: discount = base_price*pct//100 + amount. So an owner who types an amount without clearing the pre-filled '10%' creates a promo that gives 10% PLUS the fixed sum at checkout — a larger discount than intended (real money loss). Worse, the card display at line 139-142 sets isPct = discount_percent > 0 and shows ONLY the percent, hiding the amount entirely, so the owner cannot even see the combined discount exists. Fix: make the inputs truly exclusive (zero the other field on input and on submit), validate server-side that not both are >0, and show both values on the card.
- **[medium]** "Review replies" feature is entirely missing — `frontend/src/app/dashboard/reviews/page.tsx L100-124`
  - The audit focus lists 'review replies' but the page only renders client name, date, stars and the comment; there is no reply input, no owner-reply display, and backend/app/routers/reviews.py has no reply endpoint or owner_reply column. If review replies are a required capability for this area it is unimplemented; if not required, the focus description is stale. No code defect, but the expected functionality does not exist.
- **[medium]** discount_amount has no upper bound or sanity check — `frontend/src/app/dashboard/promo/page.tsx L67-76`
  - Frontend validates percent is 1..100 (line 73) but applies no bound to discount_amount, and backend PromoCreate only enforces discount_amount >= 0. A fat-finger like 1000000000 is accepted and stored. At checkout _apply_promo clamps final price to max(0, ...) so the booking would be free rather than negative, but the owner gets no warning that the amount exceeds typical service prices. Fix: cap/validate discount_amount to a reasonable max and warn when it exceeds service prices.
- **[low]** Promo list silently swallows load errors, showing a false empty state — `frontend/src/app/dashboard/promo/page.tsx L51-54`
  - load() does apiFetch(...).catch(() => []) and setRows([]). A transient network/auth failure renders the 'Hali promo-kod yo‘q' (no promo codes yet) empty state, indistinguishable from genuinely having none — an owner could believe their codes were lost. The reviews page has the same pattern (reviews/page.tsx:39-40). Fix: track error/loading state and show a retry affordance instead of an empty state on failure.
- **[low]** Review created_at sliced as raw UTC string can show wrong local date — `frontend/src/app/dashboard/reviews/page.tsx L109`
  - created_at.slice(0,10) takes the first 10 chars of the backend ISO timestamp, which is UTC (Review.created_at is stored tz-aware UTC). For a review created near the day boundary in Uzbekistan local time (UTC+5), the UTC date can differ from the owner's local date, so the displayed date is off by one day. Fix: parse to Date and format in the local/business timezone rather than string-slicing the UTC value.
  - ✅ Работает: Promo CRUD wires correctly to backend: POST/GET/PATCH toggle/DELETE paths in page.tsx exactly match app/routers/promo.py routes and the PromoOut shape matches the Promo type.; get_owned_business dependency scopes every promo query by business_id, and toggle/delete additionally filter PromoCode.id AND business_id, so there is no IDOR — another owner cannot toggle/delete someone else's promo.; Backend create_promo enforces uniqueness (uq_promo_biz_code + explicit exists check) and validates code length and that at least one discount is set; Pydantic bounds discount_percent 0..100 and forbids negatives.; Reviews list endpoint avoids N+1 by batch-loading clients with Client.id.in_(client_ids) instead of per-row queries.; apiFetch centralizes 401 refresh-and-retry with a coalesced in-flight refresh, and surfaces FastAPI 'detail' error messages, so the promo form's catch block shows meaningful errors.; Review distribution width math guards division by zero (total ? ... : 0) and the average renders safely as 0.0 when there are no reviews.

### `fe:dash-schedule` — partial (4 находок)
_Owner-facing weekly schedule editor + one-off holiday manager. Loads /api/business/me/schedule (0=Mon..6=Sun, matching Python date.weekday() used by the slot engine, so the day-of-week convention is consistent end to end) and PUTs the full 7-day array; holidays are CRUD'd via /api/business/me/holidays. Core happy path works and the day-of-week + holiday timezone handling are correct. The main shortfalls are a UI gap (breaks can be sent/preserved but never edited) and missing server-side validation that the frontend's start<end check is the only thing protecting data integrity._
- **[medium]** Backend PUT /schedule trusts client; no server-side start<end / break validation — `backend/app/routers/schedule.py L61-81`
  - put_schedule deletes all rows and re-inserts whatever the client sends with zero validation. The only guard against end<=start (or break_end<=break_start, or breaks outside working hours) lives in the frontend save() at frontend/src/app/dashboard/schedule/page.tsx:136-144. A direct API call (the endpoint is reachable independent of this page, e.g. via the mobile app or curl with a valid token) can persist start_time>=end_time. get_available_slots() at backend/app/utils/slots.py:70 then yields zero slots for that weekday with no error, silently making the day unbookable. Fix: validate in ScheduleItem/put_schedule that for is_working days start_time<end_time, and if break_start/break_end are set that break_start<break_end and both fall within [start_time,end_time]; reject with 422 otherwise.
- **[low]** No uniqueness on holiday_dates(business_id, date) — duplicates accumulate — `backend/app/models/schedule.py L29-37`
  - HolidayDate has no UniqueConstraint on (business_id, date), and add_holiday (backend/app/routers/schedule.py:97-107) does no existence check. Adding the same date twice from the UI (page.tsx addHoliday, line 59) creates two rows. is_holiday() (slots.py:26-32) still works (any match counts), but the list shows duplicate entries and the user must delete each. Fix: add UniqueConstraint('business_id','date') + migration, and upsert/skip-or-409 in add_holiday.
- **[low]** Break times can never be set from this screen, though save() transmits them — `frontend/src/app/dashboard/schedule/page.tsx L239-260`
  - save() (lines 154-155) serializes break_start/break_end and the backend stores them, and the slot engine honors breaks (slots.py:73-81), but the edit panel only renders Boshlanish/Tugash (start/end) inputs — there is no UI to set or clear a break. Existing break values loaded from the API are preserved on save (kept in row state), but an owner can never create a lunch break through the product. Either remove the break round-tripping or add break inputs. Not a crash, but a real missing-feature/data-entry gap given the backend fully supports it.
- **[low]** Cleared time input silently reverts to 09:00 default — `frontend/src/app/dashboard/schedule/page.tsx L38-41`
  - toHMS('') returns '09:00:00'. If a <input type="time"> emits an empty string (cleared field, or locale/browsers that allow blank), update() stores '' in row state; the start<end validation at line 137 compares '' which sorts before any real time so it passes, then save() converts '' to '09:00:00' — silently substituting a time the user did not choose. Minor because the time picker rarely yields empty, but the fallback hides invalid input rather than blocking save. Fix: treat empty start/end as a validation error in save() instead of defaulting.
  - ✅ Работает: Day-of-week convention is consistent end-to-end: FE uses 0=Mon..6=Sun (DAY_NAMES, comment line 43), DB column documents 0=Monday..6=Sunday, and the slot engine keys off Python date.weekday() (slots.py:53) which is also 0=Mon — no off-by-one between editor and booking availability.; Holiday dates are plain calendar dates from <input type="date"> (YYYY-MM-DD) compared against local_today()-derived dates in is_holiday/next_working_dates — no UTC-vs-local drift, correct timezone handling.; Start<end validation in save() (lines 136-144) correctly uses zero-padded HH:MM lexicographic comparison, which is valid for 24h times, and reports the offending day by name before any network call.; PUT performs delete-all + re-insert inside a single commit (schedule.py:67-80), so the rewrite is atomic — no window where the business has a partial schedule.; All endpoints are scoped via get_owned_business and delete_holiday additionally filters HolidayDate.business_id == business.id (schedule.py:116), preventing cross-tenant holiday deletion by id.; React state updates use functional setState (update line 127, removeHoliday line 84), avoiding stale-closure races; load() merges API rows by day_of_week and backfills missing days so the editor always renders all 7 rows even with a partial DB.

### `fe:dash-services+staff` — partial (4 находок)
_Two dashboard CRUD screens: Services (list/create/edit/delete/toggle with a price-range + duration form) and Staff (list/create/edit/delete/toggle plus a two-step "save record then assign services" sheet). The happy path works end-to-end against the matching backend routers, with sensible reload-after-mutation and confirm-before-delete. The main weaknesses are in the Staff create-then-assign two-request flow (partial failure leaves an orphan record and re-submitting creates duplicates) and in missing numeric validation (negative/zero price and duration pass both client and server unchecked)._
- **[high]** Staff create-then-assign partial failure orphans a record and duplicates on retry — `frontend/src/app/dashboard/staff/page.tsx L234-278`
  - save() does two sequential HTTP calls for a new staff member: POST /staff (creates the row, returns id), then PUT /staff/{id}/services. If the second call fails (e.g. AssignServicesBody validation returns 400 'One or more service ids are invalid', or a transient network error), the catch only shows a toast and does NOT call onSaved(); the sheet stays open with initial still null. The staff row already exists in the DB but the list is never reloaded, so it is invisible. When the owner presses Saqlash again, initial?.id is still undefined, so a SECOND POST /staff runs, creating a duplicate staff member. Fix: after a successful create, store the returned id in state (or mutate initial) so a retry updates instead of re-creating; alternatively reload on any outcome, or make the backend create+assign atomic in a single endpoint.
- **[medium]** Negative price and negative/zero duration accepted (no client or server validation) — `frontend/src/app/dashboard/services/page.tsx L127-145`
  - priceVal = parseInt(form.price||'0',10)||0 and duration = parseInt(form.duration_minutes||'30',10)||30 accept negative numbers: '-5' parses to -5, which is truthy, so a negative price or negative duration is sent. The backend ServiceCreate/ServiceUpdate (backend/app/routers/services.py:14-32) declare price:int and duration_minutes:int with NO ge=0 / gt=0 constraint, so the value is persisted. A negative or zero duration_minutes corrupts slot generation in the booking flow, and a negative price corrupts displayed/charged amounts. Separately, entering '0' for duration silently becomes 30 via the `|| 30` fallback, masking invalid input. Fix: validate price>=0 and duration_minutes>0 on the client and add ge=0/gt=0 Field constraints on the backend.
- **[low]** Service active/inactive toggle silently swallows all errors — `frontend/src/app/dashboard/services/page.tsx L184-187`
  - toggle() does apiFetch(...).catch(() => {}) then unconditionally await load(). If the PATCH fails (auth expired, 404, server error) the failure is completely silent: the user taps FAOL/O'CHIQ, nothing changes after reload, and there is no toast explaining why. This diverges from removeSvc/toggle-staff which do surface errors. Fix: catch and toast the error message like the other mutations.
- **[low]** Staff edit can commit record change while silently dropping service-assignment change on partial failure — `frontend/src/app/dashboard/staff/page.tsx L242-270`
  - On edit, PUT /staff/{id} and PUT .../services are independent sequential awaits. If the first succeeds but the second throws, the name/phone/photo change is committed server-side while the service-assignment change is lost, yet the only feedback is a generic 'Xatolik' toast and the sheet stays open showing the user's intended (unsaved) selections — an inconsistent state that can mislead the owner into thinking nothing saved. Lower impact than the create case since no duplicate is produced. Fix: reload on partial success, or combine into one transactional request.
  - ✅ Работает: api.ts apiFetch correctly parses FastAPI {detail} (string and validation-array) into readable error messages and handles 204 with no body, so DELETE/toggle responses are consumed safely; Services delete and Staff delete both confirm() before the destructive call and surface failures via toast instead of swallowing them; load() on the services page maps 404/'business not found' to onboarding redirect and 401 to login, a reasonable error-routing strategy; Service form validates name non-empty and enforces price_max strictly greater than price before submit; price_max of 0/blank is normalized to null; Backend assign_services validates every service_id belongs to the business (rejects cross-tenant ids), and delete_staff relies on ondelete=SET NULL for existing bookings; Staff service-picker uses an immutable Set update pattern (new Set(prev)) so toggles re-render correctly, and edit pre-seeds the Set from initial.service_ids

### `infra:docker+reqs` — partial (4 находок)
_Docker/deploy infra for the FastAPI backend: a single-stage python:3.12-slim image that installs pinned deps, drops to a non-root user, prepares the uploads dir, and starts via `alembic upgrade head && uvicorn`. railway.toml mirrors that with a /api/health healthcheck and restart policy; pytest.ini configures the test runner. The image and deploy config are sound and will boot the app, so it is largely working. The notable gaps: the test suite's async tests cannot actually run (missing pytest-asyncio + no asyncio_mode), the DB URL is used verbatim with no postgres:// normalization, and asyncpg is a dead dependency since the app is fully sync SQLAlchemy. Note: the Dockerfile lives at backend/Dockerfile, not the repo-root path given in the task._
