- **[medium]** Async tests silently don't run: pytest-asyncio missing and no asyncio_mode — `backend/requirements.txt L24-26`
  - backend/tests/test_throttling.py declares three `@pytest.mark.asyncio` / `async def test_...` cases (lines 57-74), but requirements.txt pins no `pytest-asyncio`, and pytest.ini sets no `asyncio_mode`. Without the plugin, pytest treats `async def` tests as un-awaited coroutines: depending on version it emits 'coroutine was never awaited' and either skips them or marks them passed without executing the body. Either way the throttling assertions (the anti-spam guard for the bot) are never actually verified, so a regression there would pass CI. Fix: add `pytest-asyncio>=0.23,<1` to requirements and set `asyncio_mode = auto` (or `strict`) in pytest.ini's [pytest] block.
- **[medium]** DATABASE_URL passed to create_engine without postgres:// -> postgresql:// normalization — `backend/app/database.py L17`
  - create_engine(settings.database_url, ...) uses the raw env value with no scheme rewrite anywhere in the repo (grep found no `postgres://` handling, no `postgresql+psycopg2` rewrite). Several managed Postgres providers (Heroku-style URLs, some Railway/Render legacy instances) hand out `postgres://...`, which SQLAlchemy 2.0 rejects with 'Could not parse SQLAlchemy URL ... can't load plugin: sqlalchemy.dialects:postgres', crashing both alembic upgrade and uvicorn at boot. Since deploy targets are exactly these PaaS providers, this is a latent boot failure dependent on the provider's URL format. Fix: in config or database.py, normalize: `if url.startswith('postgres://'): url = url.replace('postgres://', 'postgresql+psycopg2://', 1)` before passing to create_engine (and apply the same in alembic env.py).
- **[low]** asyncpg is an unused dependency (app is fully synchronous SQLAlchemy) — `backend/requirements.txt L5`
  - asyncpg>=0.29 is pinned, but the codebase uses the sync engine exclusively: database.py imports `create_engine` and `sqlalchemy.orm.Session`, and grep finds no `create_async_engine` or `sqlalchemy.ext.asyncio` anywhere. asyncpg is dead weight in the image (larger build, more CVE surface, slower installs). The actual driver in use is psycopg2-binary, which is correctly present. Fix: drop asyncpg from requirements unless an async path is planned.
- **[low]** Migrations run on every container start command with no concurrency guard — `backend/Dockerfile L41`
  - Both the Dockerfile CMD and railway.toml startCommand run `alembic upgrade head` inline before launching uvicorn. If the service ever scales beyond one replica (or a deploy overlaps an old container), multiple processes race to apply migrations simultaneously, which can deadlock or partially apply DDL. Today this is safe only because the deployment is single-instance. Fix: move migrations to a dedicated release/pre-deploy step (Render preDeployCommand / Railway release phase) instead of the per-instance start command, or wrap with an advisory lock.
  - ✅ Работает: Image runs as a non-root user (uid 1000 `app`) and chowns /app and the uploads dir to it, so a future RCE can't write arbitrarily across the FS - explicitly reasoned about in the Dockerfile comment.; All Python deps are version-pinned with sane upper bounds (e.g. <3, <6) to avoid surprise major-version breakage; psycopg2-binary (the real driver), boto3 (used in tasks/backup.py), bcrypt and python-jose (used in utils/auth.py and google_oauth.py) are all present.; System build deps (build-essential, libpq-dev, libjpeg-dev, zlib1g-dev, libfreetype6-dev) correctly cover psycopg2/Pillow/reportlab/qrcode native builds, and apt lists are cleaned in the same RUN layer.; Healthcheck path /api/health exists (app/main.py:164) and returns a trivial {'status':'ok'} with no DB dependency, so it won't flap on transient DB load - a correct healthcheck design.; railway.toml correctly documents not running a second polling bot process (avoids TelegramConflictError) and the celery worker entrypoint `-A app.celery_app` matches the actual module (celery_app.py:13).; PIP_NO_CACHE_DIR / PYTHONDONTWRITEBYTECODE / PYTHONUNBUFFERED env vars are set appropriately for a container.

### `migrations:014-025` — partial (3 находок)
_Migrations 014-025 are a clean, mostly well-built sequence: schema additions (cancel window, photos, loyalty, birthday, waitlist, staff, recurrence) use NOT NULL + server_default correctly so they're safe on populated tables, and 021/024 do thoughtful Python backfills for portability. Up/down chains are linear and symmetric, and the case-insensitive username dedup in 023 is solid. The one real risk is in 024's password-identity backfill, which can hit a unique-constraint violation on databases that have duplicate phone numbers, because phone uniqueness isn't enforced until a later migration (027). Verdict: works for typical/fresh data, but the 024 backfill is data-dependent and can abort the upgrade on real production data._
- **[high]** 024 password-identity backfill can violate UNIQUE(provider,subject) on duplicate phones — `backend/alembic/versions/024_auth_identities.py L98-114`
  - For users with a password_hash but no username, the backfill computes subject = (username.lower() or phone). Two distinct users that share the same phone (or share a lowercased username that 023 didn't catch because one row had a username and the other only a phone) both produce identical (provider='password', subject) rows, which violates uq_auth_identity_provider_subject and aborts the entire upgrade. Phone is NOT yet deduped/unique at this point — phone uniqueness is only added in migration 027 (later in the chain). So on any production DB that has two password-set accounts with the same phone, `alembic upgrade head` fails at 024. Username dedup in 023 only guards the username branch, not the phone fallback. Fix: before inserting, dedup the password subjects in Python (skip/skip-duplicates keeping the oldest by created_at), or wrap each insert and ON CONFLICT DO NOTHING, or order users by created_at and track seen subjects. At minimum, run the phone-dedup (the 027 UPDATE ... blank duplicates) before 024 so the fallback subjects are unique.
- **[low]** 023/027 window-function dedup requires SQLite >= 3.25 — `backend/alembic/versions/023_user_username_unique.py L31-39`
  - The dedup uses row_number() OVER (PARTITION BY ...), a window function only available in SQLite 3.25+ (2018). On the project's test/dev SQLite (pysqlite) this is almost certainly fine, but the migration is otherwise written to be portable (the comment in 024 explicitly avoids Postgres-only features for SQLite). If any runtime ships an older bundled SQLite, this migration errors. Low risk; flagging for completeness. Fix: none needed unless an old SQLite is in play; could add a comment documenting the 3.25 floor.
- **[low]** 025 downgrade is silently lossy/irreversible once Google-only accounts exist — `backend/alembic/versions/025_user_telegram_id_nullable.py L31-36`
  - downgrade() re-adds NOT NULL on telegram_id. The docstring acknowledges this is 'reversible only if no NULL telegram_id rows exist,' but the code makes no attempt to detect or handle existing NULL rows — on a DB that has created any Google/password-only account (the whole point of this migration), the downgrade raises a NOT NULL violation mid-batch-rebuild. This is acceptable (downgrades are best-effort) but the failure is abrupt. Fix: optionally add an explicit guard that raises a clear error if NULL telegram_id rows exist, so the operator gets a readable message instead of a constraint error during table rebuild.
  - ✅ Работает: 014/016: NOT NULL columns added with server_default ('0', false) so they backfill safely on existing rows without a separate UPDATE step.; 015/018/019/021/024: new tables use ondelete=CASCADE FKs and explicit indexes; down() drops indexes before tables in correct order. Up/down are symmetric.; 019: bookings.staff_id uses ondelete='SET NULL' (correct — deleting a staff member shouldn't delete historical bookings).; 021: membership backfill correctly filters WHERE owner_id IS NOT NULL and generates UUIDs in Python for Postgres/SQLite portability; role server_default 'OWNER' matches the inserted value.; 023: case-insensitive username dedup keeps the oldest row per lower(username) collision group (ORDER BY created_at, id) and blanks the rest before creating the partial unique index with postgresql_where='username <> '' — empty sentinels correctly excluded, matching the User model's index definition.; 024: telegram backfill subject is str(telegram_id), which is guaranteed unique because telegram_id was UNIQUE and still NOT NULL at this point (025 hasn't run yet) — so the telegram branch can't collide. created_at falls back to now() when null. display_name truncated to [:255] to fit the column.

### `models:core` — partial (4 находок)
_These five core models (Business, User, Client, Membership, Staff) define the account/tenant graph for the booking SaaS. Schema, nullability, and uniqueness are mostly well thought out — nullability is correctly inferred from Mapped[T] vs Mapped[T|None], partial-unique indexes for case-insensitive usernames are correct, and DB-level ondelete rules are mostly consistent with intent. The main defect is an ORM relationship/cascade mismatch on Business.bookings (and the latent User.business): SQLAlchemy will try to NULL a NOT NULL FK on parent delete, which breaks the admin hard-delete path for any business that has historical bookings._
- **[high]** Business hard-delete crashes when historical bookings exist (cascade/NOT NULL mismatch) — `backend/app/models/business.py L59`
  - Business.bookings is declared as relationship('Booking', back_populates='bookings') with NO cascade and passive_deletes defaulting to False (verified: cascade='merge,save-update', passive_deletes=False). Booking.business_id is ForeignKey(ondelete='CASCADE') and nullable=False. When the admin endpoint does db.delete(b) (routers/admin.py:406, hard-delete path), SQLAlchemy — because passive_deletes is False and there is no delete cascade on this relationship — issues a SELECT for the business's bookings and then attempts UPDATE bookings SET business_id=NULL, violating the NOT NULL constraint and raising IntegrityError. The active-booking guard at admin.py:387-402 only blocks PENDING/CONFIRMED bookings, so any business with CANCELLED/COMPLETED/NO_SHOW history (i.e. essentially every real business) cannot be hard-deleted. Fix: add passive_deletes=True to the bookings relationship so SQLAlchemy relies on the DB ondelete='CASCADE' instead of nulling the FK: bookings: Mapped[list['Booking']] = relationship('Booking', back_populates='business', passive_deletes=True).
- **[medium]** User.business has same cascade/NOT NULL mismatch (latent until a User is ORM-deleted) — `backend/app/models/user.py L44`
  - User.business (relationship, uselist=False) has cascade='merge,save-update' and passive_deletes=False, while Business.owner_id is ForeignKey(ondelete='CASCADE'), unique=True, nullable=False. Any future db.delete(user) (none exists in the app today; admin wipe uses table-level deletes in FK order, so this is latent) will make SQLAlchemy attempt UPDATE businesses SET owner_id=NULL, which violates NOT NULL. Fix: declare relationship('Business', back_populates='owner', uselist=False, passive_deletes=True) so DB cascade handles it. Same latent concern applies to the other passive_deletes=False parent relationships (services/schedules/holidays/subscriptions) which currently work but load+delete children row-by-row (N+1 on delete) instead of letting the DB CASCADE run.
- **[low]** Redundant duplicate index on businesses.slug — `backend/app/models/business.py L18`
  - slug is declared with both index=True (line 25, creates a plain non-unique index) and a UniqueConstraint('slug', name='uq_businesses_slug') (line 18, creates a unique index). Two indexes cover the exact same column, doubling write/maintenance cost with no read benefit since the unique index already serves equality lookups. Fix: drop index=True on the slug column and keep only the UniqueConstraint.
- **[low]** No server_default on NOT NULL columns with Python-side defaults — `backend/app/models/business.py L27`
  - Many NOT NULL columns (Business.category/description/address/confirmation_mode/language/cancel_window_hours/is_active, User.username/is_active, Staff.is_active/order, Membership.role, etc.) use Python-side default= only, with no server_default. Any INSERT that bypasses the ORM (raw SQL, bulk loads, the admin restore path at routers/admin.py:916 which re-inserts coerced rows, or a migration backfilling new NOT NULL columns) that omits these columns will fail with a NOT NULL violation because the DB has no default. Within normal ORM usage this is fine; flagged because the codebase has a raw insert/restore path. Fix: where these columns may be written outside the ORM, add server_default (e.g. server_default='true'/text('0')/the enum value) alongside the Python default.
  - ✅ Работает: Nullability is correctly derived from type annotations: Mapped[T] columns are NOT NULL and Mapped[T | None] columns are nullable (verified via __table__ introspection), so optional fields like latitude/longitude, password_hash, birthday, deleted_at, price_max are correctly nullable while required fields are NOT NULL.; User uniqueness model is well designed: partial unique index uq_users_username_lower on lower(username) with WHERE username <> '' (both postgresql_where and sqlite_where) correctly enforces case-insensitive username uniqueness while allowing multiple password-less accounts; telegram_id is unique+nullable so multiple Google/password-only accounts (NULL telegram_id) coexist, which Postgres and SQLite both permit.; Client.telegram_id is unique+NOT NULL, correctly preventing the duplicate-client race the comment describes for concurrent first-time bookings.; FK ondelete semantics match intent: business_id=CASCADE (tenant-scoped rows die with the business), service_id/client_id/staff_id=SET NULL (bookings survive as historical records and fall back to shared-calendar/anonymous), and staff_services M2M uses CASCADE on both sides so association rows clean up.; Membership has a correct UniqueConstraint(user_id, business_id) preventing two roles per user per business, with both FKs CASCADE and indexed.; Child relationships that DO need ORM cascade (services/schedules/holidays/subscriptions, User.identities) correctly declare cascade='all, delete-orphan', matching their DB CASCADE FKs.

### `router:clients` — partial (3 находок)
_This router exposes the owner-facing client CRM under /business/me: list clients (with visit aggregates), client detail with booking history and block status, patch birthday, and block/unblock/list-blocked. All endpoints authenticate via get_owned_business so the business is owner-scoped. The mutating and block endpoints correctly gate access through _client_in_business_or_404, but the GET /clients/{client_id} detail endpoint does NOT apply that ownership check, creating a cross-tenant PII leak. Otherwise the queries are sound and business-scoped. Verdict: functionally works for the happy path but has one real authorization/privacy defect plus a couple of aggregate-semantics bugs._
- **[high]** client_detail leaks any client's PII across tenants (IDOR) — `backend/app/routers/clients.py L71-98`
  - GET /clients/{client_id} loads the client with `db.query(Client).filter(Client.id == client_id).first()` and returns first_name, last_name, phone, telegram_id and birthday WITHOUT verifying the client has any booking at the caller's business. The bookings/stats/block sub-queries are business-scoped, so for an unrelated client they come back empty, but the top-level `client` object is still returned in full. An owner of business A can enumerate UUIDs (or reuse a UUID seen elsewhere) and read the PII of any client in the system, including their Telegram id and phone. This is exactly the leak the sibling helper `_client_in_business_or_404` (lines 125-141) was written to prevent — but client_detail doesn't call it. Fix: replace the line-71 lookup with `c = _client_in_business_or_404(db, business.id, client_id)` so the client must have at least one booking at this business before any data is returned (and it preserves the existing 404 behavior).
- **[low]** last_visit can be a future booking date, mislabeling the metric — `backend/app/routers/clients.py L37,48,59`
  - `func.max(Booking.date)` is reported as `last_visit` and used to order the list, but it includes future bookings (a client with an appointment next week shows a last_visit in the future) and bookings of any status (PENDING/CANCELLED/NO_SHOW count as a 'visit'). So 'visits' over-counts and 'last_visit' is really 'latest booking date'. If the UI presents these as historical visit metrics they are wrong. Fix: if the intent is realized visits, filter to completed/past bookings, e.g. add `Booking.status.in_([COMPLETED, CONFIRMED])` and/or `Booking.date <= today` to the aggregate, or rename the fields to reflect 'latest booking'.
- **[low]** visits/no_show counts include cancelled bookings inconsistently between list and detail — `backend/app/routers/clients.py L58,80,110`
  - list_clients counts every booking row as a 'visit' (line 58, no status filter), while client_detail's total_bookings (line 110) and no_show_count (line 80) are computed over the same unfiltered set. There is no status filtering anywhere, so cancelled bookings inflate both the per-client visit count in the list and total_bookings in the detail. This is a data-quality/semantics issue rather than a crash, but the numbers shown to owners will not match intuitive 'visits'. Fix: decide and apply a consistent status filter in both endpoints.
  - ✅ Работает: All endpoints depend on get_owned_business, which scopes the resolved business strictly to Business.owner_id == user.id, so there is no way to act on a business you don't own.; The mutating/sensitive endpoints (patch_client, block_client) correctly call _client_in_business_or_404, which enforces both existence and that the client has booked at this business before allowing edits/blocks — preventing global Client enumeration via those routes.; Block creation is genuinely idempotent and backed by a DB UniqueConstraint (uq_block_biz_client), and unblock is safe/idempotent (no error if the block is absent, returns blocked:false).; All booking and block sub-queries are filtered by business_id, so booking history, stats, and the blocked-clients list never cross tenants.; client_id path params are typed as UUID, so malformed ids are rejected with 422 before hitting the DB; BlockBody.reason is length-capped (max_length=512) matching the column width.; str-enum BookingStatus comparison (b.status == BookingStatus.NO_SHOW) and serialization (str(b.status)) work correctly because the status column stores the enum's string value.

### `router:payments` — partial (7 находок)
_This router handles subscription payments via Payme/Click gateways (auto), a manual card flow (create -> upload receipt -> admin approve/reject), platform card-info settings, admin pending list, status polling, and refunds. The card/admin flows, authz scoping, and receipt access control are solid. The automatic gateway webhook handlers are the weak spot: they identify the transaction by regex-scraping the first UUID out of the serialized callback and complete the subscription without validating the callback's amount or following the gateway protocol, and they run blocking sync DB + blocking HTTP on the event loop. Verdict: card/admin path works; gateway webhook path is fragile and under-validated._
- **[high]** Webhooks identify the transaction by scraping the first UUID in the payload — `backend/app/routers/payments.py L377-387, 436, 467`
  - _find_tx_id serializes the whole callback to JSON and returns the FIRST regex-matched UUID. Payme/Click payloads can contain other UUID-shaped values (or future fields), and the matched UUID is order-dependent on dict serialization. If a non-transaction UUID appears earlier, the handler will look up / complete the wrong transaction (or none). Fix: extract the transaction id from the documented field for each gateway (Payme: params.account.id; Click: merchant_trans_id) instead of regex-scanning the entire body.
- **[high]** Payme/Click webhook completes the subscription without validating the paid amount — `backend/app/routers/payments.py L440-450, 474-480`
  - Both webhooks call complete_transaction_and_notify(db, tx) which activates a full subscription using tx.amount, but never compares the amount reported in the callback to tx.amount. A buggy/partial gateway callback (or an underpaid Payme transaction) would still activate the full plan. For Click the signed sign_string covers amount so tampering is blocked, but the handler still never asserts callback amount == tx.amount. Fix: validate the callback amount equals the expected tx.amount before completing; reject/ignore otherwise.
- **[high]** Blocking sync DB and blocking httpx call run on the event loop in async webhook handlers — `backend/app/routers/payments.py L427, 448, 454, 478`
  - payme_webhook and click_webhook are 'async def' but execute synchronous SQLAlchemy queries and complete_transaction_and_notify -> send_telegram_message, which does a blocking httpx.post with a 15s timeout. All of this runs directly on the asyncio event loop, blocking every other request for the duration of the Telegram round-trip (up to 15-30s). Fix: either make these endpoints plain 'def' (so FastAPI runs them in the threadpool) or offload the DB/notify work via asyncio.to_thread, as upload_receipt already does for send_telegram_photo (line 230).
- **[medium]** Payme webhook completes on PerformTransaction without implementing the JSON-RPC handshake/response contract — `backend/app/routers/payments.py L444-450`
  - The Payme merchant protocol is a JSON-RPC flow (CheckPerformTransaction, CreateTransaction, PerformTransaction, CancelTransaction) and expects specific JSON-RPC result/error responses keyed by the request id. This handler only reacts to method=='PerformTransaction' and always returns {"ok": true}, ignoring CreateTransaction/CancelTransaction and never returning the structured result Payme expects. This will likely cause Payme to treat callbacks as malformed and retry, and CancelTransaction (refund/void initiated on Payme side) is silently dropped, leaving subscriptions active after a gateway-side cancel. Fix: implement the documented Payme JSON-RPC methods and responses (the paytechuz library used for create likely provides a webhook handler).
- **[medium]** Click webhook ignores the gateway error code and acts only on action — `backend/app/routers/payments.py L471-480`
  - Click Complete callbacks carry an 'error' field; a completion with action=='1' can still report a negative 'error' (failed/cancelled). This handler completes the subscription whenever action=='1' regardless of error, and never handles the Prepare (action=='0') step or error<0 reversals. Fix: only complete when action=='1' AND int(error)==0, and handle reversal/cancel codes by not activating (or by cancelling).
- **[low]** Receipt file is written to disk before the row is updated and is never cleaned up on failure — `backend/app/routers/payments.py L202-209`
  - path.write_bytes(contents) persists the file, then tx fields are set and db.commit() runs. If the commit fails, the orphaned file remains. Combined with the project's known ephemeral /tmp uploads, receipts are also lost on dyno restart so screenshot_url can dangle. Fix: write after a successful flush or remove the file in an except/finally on commit failure; consider storing receipts in Postgres media_blobs like logos already are.
- **[low]** int(owner.telegram_id) in service notify paths can raise outside try/except — `backend/app/services/payment_service.py L220, 197, 269`
  - complete_transaction_and_notify (reached by both webhooks and approve) calls send_telegram_message(int(owner.telegram_id), ...). If owner.telegram_id is None (a username/password-only owner with no Telegram link), int(None) raises TypeError. send_telegram_message swallows its own httpx errors, but the int() conversion happens before the call, so the exception propagates out of complete_transaction_and_notify and the webhook/approve handler 500s after the status was already mutated in the session. Fix: guard 'if owner and owner.telegram_id:' before converting, as reject_card_payment already does (line 192).
  - ✅ Работает: Card manual flow is correctly ownership-scoped: upload_receipt, get_status load the tx and reject it if tx.business_id != business.id (lines 183, 311).; get_receipt (line 237) properly prevents IDOR: rejects path traversal via os.basename equality check, and for non-admins verifies the requesting user owns the business that created the tx before serving the file.; Approve/reject/refund are admin-gated via get_admin_user, and refund is correctly admin-only with the service layer re-checking COMPLETED status + business ownership under a row lock (free-money exploit avoided).; Webhook auth fails closed: _verify_payme_auth and _verify_click_signature both return False when the secret is unconfigured, and both use hmac.compare_digest for constant-time comparison.; Idempotency on completion: both webhooks and approve_card_payment short-circuit if tx.status == COMPLETED, preventing double-activation.; Telegram caption is HTML-escaped via h(...) (line 222-227), preventing HTML injection into the admin notification.

### `service:audit_service` — partial (3 находок)
_audit_service.py provides a single best-effort helper log_admin_action that stages an AdminAuditLog row recording which admin performed which action on which target, with an arbitrary JSON payload. It is called from admin.py and payments.py, which then commit. It works for the common Telegram-admin case, but its core "never fail the calling write" safety guarantee is structurally ineffective, and it silently drops audit records for non-Telegram (Google/password) admins._
- **[medium]** try/except does not actually protect the caller's write — wrong scope — `backend/app/services/audit_service.py L18-30`
  - The stated contract (line 17: "never fail the calling write because of logging") is not met. db.add(entry) only stages the ORM object in the session's identity map; it issues no SQL and almost never raises. The real database errors — NOT NULL violation on admin_telegram_id, value-too-long for String(64) columns, non-JSON-serializable payload, integer-coercion errors — occur at flush/commit time, which happens in the CALLER (e.g. admin.py:319 db.commit(), payments.py:348 db.commit()), entirely outside this try/except. So a bad audit entry will abort the entire business/payment write at commit, exactly the failure the comment promises to prevent. Fix: build and validate the entry inside the try, and either (a) flush the audit insert in a SAVEPOINT (db.begin_nested()) here so a failure can be rolled back without poisoning the outer transaction, or (b) pre-validate/truncate fields and JSON-serialize payload before staging. Minimum viable: wrap db.add + db.flush() in begin_nested() and roll back the savepoint on exception.
- **[low]** Audit records silently dropped for non-Telegram (Google/password) admins — `backend/app/services/audit_service.py L20`
  - User.telegram_id is nullable (app/models/user.py:33 Mapped[int | None]); the product supports username/password and Google OAuth admins with no Telegram link. int(admin.telegram_id) raises TypeError when telegram_id is None. The bare except (line 29) swallows it, so the admin action is never recorded — a silent gap in the security audit trail for an entire class of admins. Because admin_telegram_id is nullable=False there is no clean null fallback without a schema change. Fix: make admin_telegram_id nullable (or add a separate admin_user_id UUID column) and record the action regardless of telegram_id presence; at minimum log a warning instead of silently swallowing so the loss is observable.
- **[low]** Bare except: pass hides real bugs and provides no observability — `backend/app/services/audit_service.py L29-30`
  - except Exception: pass swallows everything (TypeError from int(None), AttributeError, etc.) with zero logging. Combined with the wrong-scope issue above, this means audit failures are completely invisible: there is no log line, no metric, nothing. For an audit/security feature this is a meaningful blind spot. Fix: log the exception (logger.warning("audit log failed", exc_info=True)) so dropped audit writes are detectable in production.
  - ✅ Работает: Best-effort design intent is sound: isolating audit logging so it cannot break primary writes is the right goal (the implementation just doesn't fully achieve it).; Defensive field handling is reasonable: empty-string fallbacks for target_type/target_id, payload or {} default, and a sensible admin_name composition (first+last, falling back to username).; target_id stringification via str(target_id) safely accommodates both UUID (36 chars) and string ids within the String(64) column.; action/target_type values are hardcoded short literals at all call sites, so String(64) truncation is not a realistic risk in practice.; The model correctly uses JSONB on Postgres with a portable JSON variant for SQLite tests (admin_audit_log.py:8), and timezone-aware created_at via datetime.now(timezone.utc).

### `service:event_bus` — partial (2 находок)
_A tiny in-process pub/sub bus backing Server-Sent Events for the dashboard bell. publish(business_id, kind) fan-outs a string "kind" into per-subscriber asyncio.Queues; subscribe() is an async generator yielding kinds (with a 30s "ping" heartbeat on timeout) and cleaning up its queue on disconnect under an asyncio.Lock. The design intent (single-process, best-effort, dropped events recovered by heartbeat + frontend re-fetch) is sound and cleanup is correct. But the actual call sites publish from sync `def` route handlers, which FastAPI runs in a worker thread, not the event-loop thread. Calling put_nowait on a loop-bound asyncio.Queue cross-thread is unsafe and may fail to wake the waiting consumer, so instant delivery is unreliable in practice — hence "partial". It degrades gracefully because the frontend re-fetches and the 30s heartbeat masks the failure._
- **[high]** publish() calls asyncio.Queue.put_nowait cross-thread from sync handlers (not thread-safe, may not wake consumer) — `backend/app/services/event_bus.py L45-47`
  - publish() is invoked from synchronous `def` route handlers (bookings.py:113, bookings.py:364, reviews.py:85; business.py PUT /me is also sync). FastAPI runs sync handlers in an anyio worker THREAD, while the SSE subscribe() generator and its q.get() run on the asyncio event-loop thread. asyncio.Queue is explicitly NOT thread-safe and is bound to the loop it was created on. put_nowait() from a foreign thread mutates queue internals without locking AND schedules the waiter wakeup via loop.call_soon, which is itself not thread-safe from another thread. Result: data races on queue internals and, critically, the waiting get() coroutine may never be scheduled to wake — so the event is enqueued but the SSE stream does not emit it until the next 30s heartbeat (or not at all if state is corrupted). The 'instant bell update' this module exists for is therefore unreliable. Fix: capture loop = asyncio.get_running_loop() per queue in subscribe(), and in publish do loop.call_soon_threadsafe(q.put_nowait, kind); or make the publishing handlers async; or use asyncio.run_coroutine_threadsafe. The QueueFull catch also won't behave correctly since put_nowait isn't running on the owning loop.
- **[low]** publish() reads/iterates _subs without the async lock across the thread boundary — `backend/app/services/event_bus.py L42-45`
  - publish() does _subs.get(business_id) and iterates the set from a worker thread, while subscribe() adds/removes queues and pops empty buckets under _lock on the event-loop thread. The tuple(queues) snapshot on line 45 prevents 'Set changed size during iteration' for the loop itself, but the read of the set/defaultdict is still unsynchronized cross-thread (a concurrent bucket.discard/_subs.pop during the tuple() snapshot is unsynchronized). Part of the same root issue as finding #1: the module assumes single-threaded-async access that the real callers violate. Acceptable for best-effort, but a threadsafe scheduling fix should also cover this read.
  - ✅ Работает: subscribe() cleanup is correct and leak-free: the finally block discards the queue under _lock and pops the business bucket when empty, so disconnected streams don't accumulate queues or empty defaultdict entries.; Queue is bounded (maxsize=64) and publish uses put_nowait with a QueueFull catch, so a slow/stuck consumer can never block or unbounded-buffer the publisher.; publish() never raises (broad except + logging), honoring the contract that a bus problem must not break the booking/review write.; 30s heartbeat via asyncio.wait_for(...timeout=30) plus frontend re-fetch-on-signal makes dropped/missed events self-healing, bounding worst-case staleness.; Events carry only a tiny string 'kind' rather than the notification payload, so publishers don't need to know the response shape — a clean, low-coupling contract.; Ordering at call sites is safe: publish_event is called AFTER db.commit() (e.g. bookings.py:363-364), so the committed data is already visible when the frontend re-fetches in response to the signal.

### `service:notification_service` — partial (3 находок)
_Thin wrappers around Telegram Bot HTTP API (sendMessage/sendPhoto) with sync and async variants. The happy-path sends work and the file is correct in isolation. However, all four functions deliberately swallow every error (including 4xx/5xx and exceptions) and never raise or return a status, which silently breaks the only feature that depends on knowing send outcomes: the admin broadcast/retry success-vs-failure accounting in admin.py treats every send as a success regardless of whether Telegram actually delivered._
- **[high]** Broadcast success/failure stats are meaningless — async send never signals failure to caller — `backend/app/services/notification_service.py L85-100`
  - send_telegram_message_async catches every exception inside _do and only logs a warning on non-2xx responses; it never re-raises and returns None unconditionally. The broadcast fan-out in backend/app/routers/admin.py (_send_broadcast_to lines 661-667 and retry_broadcast lines 777-783) wraps the call in try/except and treats a raised exception as failure (return False) and a clean return as success (return True). Because the function never raises — even on HTTP 403 (user blocked the bot), 429 (rate limited), or network timeouts — every recipient is counted as `sent`, `failed_recipients` is always empty, and the persisted BroadcastMessage.sent_count/failed_count/failed_recipients stored in the DB are wrong. The retry endpoint is therefore also dead: failed_recipients is never populated, so /broadcasts/{id}/retry always returns no_failed. Fix: make the async send return a bool (or raise on non-2xx / on exception) so callers can distinguish real delivery from failure, then update _send_broadcast_to/retry_broadcast to use that signal.
- **[low]** No handling of Telegram 429 rate limiting; broadcast can get throttled with no backoff — `backend/app/services/notification_service.py L87-92`
  - On a 1k-recipient broadcast the code fires with a semaphore of 20 concurrent sends (admin.py line 655). Telegram enforces ~30 msg/s per bot and returns HTTP 429 with a retry_after value when exceeded. This module only logs the 429 as a warning and drops the message — there is no respect for retry_after and no retry. Combined with the finding above, throttled recipients are silently counted as delivered. Fix: detect status_code==429, read retry_after from the JSON body, and either sleep-and-retry or surface the failure so it lands in failed_recipients for the retry endpoint.
- **[low]** send_telegram_photo_async is dead code — `backend/app/services/notification_service.py L103-124`
  - Grep across the repo shows send_telegram_photo_async has no callers; the only photo send (payments.py line 230) uses the sync send_telegram_photo via asyncio.to_thread. The async variant is unused and untested, so its claim that 'the read happens off the event loop because httpx streams it' is unverified — and is in fact wrong: open(...,'rb') with a sync file handle passed to httpx files= is read synchronously on the event loop during multipart encoding, so for an 8 MB receipt it would briefly block the loop. Not currently harmful (no callers), but the docstring is misleading and the code is rot. Fix: remove it, or if it is intended for future use, read the file via asyncio.to_thread/aiofiles before posting.
  - ✅ Работает: Sync and async variants correctly short-circuit and return when settings.bot_token is unset, so the app and tests run without a configured bot.; Exceptions are caught with logger.exception (full traceback) so a single bad chat_id never crashes a Celery task, request handler, or broadcast loop.; Non-2xx responses are logged with truncated body (resp.text[:200]) — avoids unbounded log spam while preserving the error reason.; Async send accepts an optional shared httpx.AsyncClient, and the broadcast caller passes one, so connection pooling is correctly reused across the fan-out.; parse_mode=HTML and reply_markup passthrough are handled consistently across sync/async message senders.; Reasonable timeouts are set (15s for messages, 30s for photo uploads), preventing indefinite hangs on a stalled Telegram API.

### `service:payment_service` — partial (6 находок)
_payment_service.py drives subscription billing: it creates Payme/Click/Card payment transactions, activates subscriptions on success, and handles manual card approve/reject and admin refunds. The happy paths work and locking inside activate_subscription/refund is thoughtfully done, but there are real defects: payment completion crashes for owners without a Telegram ID (a fully-supported auth mode), webhook idempotency is not enforced under concurrency (the COMPLETED guard is checked outside any lock), and provider-reported amounts are never verified against the stored amount. Verdict: works for the common Telegram-user case but partial — exploitable/breakable in supported scenarios._
- **[high]** Payment completion crashes for owners with no Telegram ID — `backend/app/services/payment_service.py L220`
  - complete_transaction_and_notify calls send_telegram_message(int(owner.telegram_id), msg) unconditionally. User.telegram_id is nullable=True (backend/app/models/user.py:33) and the project explicitly supports username/password and Google OAuth signups that have no telegram_id. For such an owner, int(None) raises TypeError. This propagates up through the Payme/Click webhook and the admin approve endpoint, aborting the request after tx.status was set to COMPLETED in the session; db.commit() never runs, so the whole activation is rolled back. The payment provider charged the customer but no subscription is activated and the webhook returns 500, causing the provider to keep retrying against a tx that will fail again. Fix: guard like reject_card_payment does — `if owner and owner.telegram_id:` before sending, and wrap the send in try/except so notification failure never aborts billing.
- **[high]** Refund crashes for owners with no Telegram ID — `backend/app/services/payment_service.py L267`
  - refund_transaction does `if owner:` then send_telegram_message(int(owner.telegram_id), ...) — but owner.telegram_id can be None (nullable). int(None) raises TypeError, aborting the refund after tx was already marked REFUNDED and the subscription CANCELLED in-session; db.commit() never runs and everything rolls back, so an admin clicking refund on a non-Telegram owner's payment silently fails with a 500. Fix: change the guard to `if owner and owner.telegram_id:` and wrap the send in try/except, mirroring reject_card_payment (lines 192-199).
- **[high]** Webhook idempotency not enforced under concurrent retries — duplicate subscription activation — `backend/app/routers/payments.py L440`
  - In payme_webhook (and identically click_webhook at 474), the tx is fetched WITHOUT with_for_update and the idempotency guard `tx.status == COMPLETED` is evaluated before any lock is taken. Payment providers deliver the same callback multiple times. Two concurrent deliveries each open their own DB transaction, each read the committed PENDING status (guard passes for both), then both call complete_transaction_and_notify -> activate_subscription. activate_subscription serializes on the Business row lock, but the second caller never re-reads tx status under that lock, so it creates a SECOND ACTIVE Subscription row (the first one having been swapped to EXPIRED) and re-sets the already-COMPLETED tx. Net effect: duplicate subscription rows and/or double-extended expiry from a single payment. Fix: select the tx with with_for_update() inside complete path and re-check `if tx.status == COMPLETED: return` after acquiring the lock, or add a unique partial constraint so only one ACTIVE subscription per business can exist.
- **[high]** Provider-reported payment amount is never verified against tx.amount — `backend/app/routers/payments.py L448`
  - complete_transaction_and_notify activates the subscription using tx.amount (the amount the system expected), but neither the Payme nor Click webhook compares the amount actually paid (present in the callback body) against tx.amount. The tx id is extracted from the body via a loose regex (_find_tx_id) and the only check is signature/auth. A customer who initiates a YEARLY/expensive tx but completes a smaller charge at the provider, or replays a callback referencing a cheaper tx id, gets a full subscription. The Click signature does include amount, but the code never asserts that signed amount equals tx.amount. Fix: parse the paid amount from the callback and reject (or do not complete) when it does not equal tx.amount.
- **[medium]** activate_subscription locks the Business row but discards the result, providing no real serialization across the completion flow — `backend/app/services/payment_service.py L35`
  - The SELECT ... FOR UPDATE on Business is the intended concurrency gate, but it is only taken inside activate_subscription, after the webhook/approve caller has already decided to proceed based on an unlocked tx.status read. Because the tx row itself is never locked in the completion path (unlike refund_transaction, which does lock the tx), the Business lock cannot prevent the duplicate-activation race described in the webhook finding — it only serializes the writes, not the decision. Fix: lock the PaymentTransaction row (with_for_update) and re-check status==COMPLETED at the start of complete_transaction_and_notify, making the Business lock redundant or complementary.
- **[low]** complete_transaction_and_notify treats any non-YEARLY plan string as MONTHLY — `backend/app/services/payment_service.py L206`
  - `if tx.plan == "YEARLY": plan = YEARLY else: plan = MONTHLY`. tx.plan is a free-form String(32) column (payment.py:31) defaulting to 'MONTHLY'. Any unexpected/typo value silently becomes a MONTHLY (30-day) activation rather than failing. Combined with the owner message hardcoding '30 kunga' for the MONTHLY branch, a malformed plan would grant a short subscription with no error. Low impact today since plan is set from the enum .value at creation, but it is brittle. Fix: map explicitly and raise on unknown plan values.
  - ✅ Работает: activate_subscription locks the Business row (with_for_update) and the prior ACTIVE subscription before swapping it to EXPIRED, serializing concurrent activations within a single DB transaction; refund_transaction locks the tx row and re-checks status under the lock, and validates business ownership and COMPLETED state before refunding; approve_card_payment is idempotent for an already-COMPLETED tx (returns early) and validates provider type and allowed source statuses; Money amounts are integer UZS (no float rounding) and amount_paid is persisted onto the subscription; All datetimes use timezone.utc consistently (datetime.now(timezone.utc)); no naive/aware mixing; External gateway construction and create_payment calls are wrapped in try/except so a provider outage degrades to an empty link rather than a 500 mid-transaction

### `task:reminders` — partial (6 находок)
_backend/app/tasks/reminders.py defines five Celery beat tasks: a per-minute 1-hour-before booking reminder (send_hourly_reminders), a nightly no-show flagger (flag_no_shows), daily birthday greetings, daily re-engagement nudges, and a daily trial-expiry warning. The core scheduling logic is mostly correct: timezone handling is deliberate and right (bookings stored as naive Tashkent local, compared against naive now in TZ; Celery beat is configured for Asia/Tashkent so the crontab hours match the local comments), and the per-booking commit makes the reminder_sent_at dedup guard race-free against the overlapping 2-minute send window. Verdict: works for the happy path, but has a fragile reminder-delivery window, several N+1 query patterns, a no-show edge case, and a couple of timezone/robustness gaps in the outreach and trial tasks._
- **[high]** 1-hour reminder can be silently skipped if a single beat run is missed — `backend/app/tasks/reminders.py L47`
  - The send window is REMINDER_WINDOW_MIN=59 .. MAX=61, i.e. only ~2 minutes wide, while Celery beat fires every minute (celery_app.py:19). A booking therefore has at most ~2 chances to be caught. If the worker is busy, redis hiccups, or a deploy restarts the worker during those two minutes (very common on Render), the booking's minutes_until moves below 59 on the next successful run and the reminder is NEVER sent (reminder_sent_at stays NULL but the time window has passed). There is no catch-up logic. Fix: widen the window and make it open-ended on the lower bound combined with the reminder_sent_at guard, e.g. send when minutes_until <= REMINDER_WINDOW_MAX (and >= some small floor like 0) AND reminder_sent_at IS NULL. The dedup column already prevents double-send, so a wide 'fire as soon as we're within ~61 min and haven't sent yet' window is both safer and still single-shot.
- **[medium]** N+1 queries: per-booking client/business/service lookups — `backend/app/tasks/reminders.py L49`
  - send_hourly_reminders loads all candidate bookings, then for each one issues three separate queries (Client, Business, Service at lines 49-51). The candidate set is pre-filtered to bookings whose date >= today and not yet reminded, but on a busy day this is still 3*N round-trips plus a commit per row. Same N+1 shape appears in send_birthday_greetings (per-client last-booking + business lookups, lines 145-154), send_reengagement_nudges (per-client client + business lookups, lines 194-209), and trial_expiry_warnings (per-sub business + owner lookups, lines 245-250). Fix: either eager-load via joinedload/selectinload on the Booking relationships (Booking already has business/service/client relationships) or batch-fetch the related rows by id set. The booking reminder query in particular should use .options(selectinload(Booking.client), selectinload(Booking.business), selectinload(Booking.service)).
- **[medium]** flag_no_shows day-boundary filter can flip a same-day booking whose slot hasn't passed grace yet, and skip same-day ones that have — `backend/app/tasks/reminders.py L92`
  - The SQL pre-filter is Booking.date <= cutoff_local.date(). cutoff_local = now - 2h. At 03:00 Tashkent (the scheduled run time) cutoff is 01:00, so cutoff_local.date() is still today; today's bookings ARE included and then correctly filtered by the slot_end > cutoff check at line 98. That happens to work at 03:00. But the task is fragile: if it ever runs later in the day (manual trigger, retry, schedule change), the date<= filter still only fetches up to cutoff's date, so a booking from earlier today whose end_time was, say, 14:00 with a 03:00 run would never even be loaded if cutoff date logic shifted — and more importantly bookings on cutoff_local.date() that ended after cutoff are loaded and correctly skipped, but the in-Python slot_end check is the only real guard. The pre-filter Booking.date <= cutoff_local.date() should be Booking.date <= now_local.date() (today) so that today's already-finished slots are always considered regardless of the 2h offset; otherwise a slot that ended 30 min ago on the current day can be excluded by the date arithmetic when grace pushes cutoff into the previous day (e.g. a run shortly after local midnight). Fix: filter on now_local.date() for the date bound and keep the slot_end > cutoff Python check for the grace period.
- **[medium]** trial_expiry_warnings treats a naive expires_at as already-local, risking wrong calendar day — `backend/app/tasks/reminders.py L240`
  - expires_local = s.expires_at; only if it is tz-aware is it converted to Tashkent. If Subscription.expires_at is stored naive (other DateTime columns in this codebase mix datetime.utcnow() and now(timezone.utc)), a naive UTC value is compared directly via .date() == tomorrow (Tashkent), which is off by +5h. A subscription expiring at, e.g., 2026-06-29 21:30 UTC is 2026-06-30 02:30 Tashkent; if stored naive it would be matched against the UTC date, firing on the wrong day (or missing the warning entirely near midnight). Fix: when expires_local.tzinfo is None, assume UTC (replace(tzinfo=timezone.utc)) before astimezone(TZ), mirroring the explicit handling already done in _under_cooldown (lines 122-123).
- **[low]** send_hourly_reminders dereferences client.telegram_id without int-conversion guard but assumes non-null; OK, but service.name HTML-escaped while business.name escaped too — confirm send path — `backend/app/tasks/reminders.py L58`
  - Minor robustness: int(client.telegram_id) at line 58 (and int(owner.telegram_id) at 254, int(client.telegram_id) in birthday/reengagement) will raise if telegram_id is ever 0/empty or owner has no telegram link. telegram_id is non-nullable on Client so the booking path is safe, but the trial task reads User.telegram_id (line 254) which may be null for password/Google-only owners — int(None) raises TypeError inside the loop. Because trial_expiry_warnings has no try/except around the send and no per-row commit, one owner without a telegram_id aborts the whole task run (and since it never commits anything, that part is harmless, but later owners in the loop are skipped). Fix: guard `if owner and owner.telegram_id:` before sending.
- **[low]** Birthday/reengagement messages interpolate client.first_name and biz.name into HTML without escaping — `backend/app/tasks/reminders.py L160`
  - send_birthday_greetings (lines 160-162) and send_reengagement_nudges (lines 215-217) build HTML messages with parse_mode=HTML using raw client.first_name and biz.name, unlike send_hourly_reminders which routes business/service names through h() (line 55-56). A business or client name containing '<', '&', or an unbalanced tag will cause Telegram to reject the message (HTTP 400 'can't parse entities'), so that user silently never gets the greeting. Not a security issue (recipient is the named party), but a delivery-reliability/data-integrity bug. Fix: wrap name and biz.name in h() as the reminder path already does.
  - ✅ Работает: Timezone handling for the reminder path is correct and deliberate: bookings are stored as naive Tashkent-local date/time, now_local = datetime.now(TZ).replace(tzinfo=None) makes an apples-to-apples naive comparison, and Celery beat is configured timezone=Asia/Tashkent so the crontab hour=N comments match local time.; The duplicate-send guard is race-free: send_hourly_reminders commits reminder_sent_at per booking inside the loop (line 62), so even though the 2-minute window overlaps two consecutive per-minute runs, the second run's reminder_sent_at.is_(None) filter excludes the already-sent row. The model comment (booking.py:64-70) documents exactly this intent.; Broken/orphaned rows are handled: when client or business is missing, the booking is still marked reminder_sent_at (lines 59-61) so it cannot re-enter the window forever.; _under_cooldown correctly normalizes a naive last_outreach_at to UTC before comparison (lines 122-123), preventing offset-naive vs offset-aware TypeErrors, and the 14-day cooldown is shared by both outreach tasks so birthday + re-engagement don't stack.; send_telegram_message itself swallows exceptions and logs (notification_service.py:45-46), so a single failed Telegram send does not abort the per-booking loop in send_hourly_reminders.; flag_no_shows applies a Python-side slot_end > cutoff grace check (lines 97-99) in addition to the SQL date filter, and only commits if at least one row flipped (line 102), avoiding empty commits.

### `util:ratelimit` — partial (2 находок)
_A tiny in-memory per-IP sliding-window rate limiter exposed as a FastAPI dependency factory (`rate_limit(scope, limit, window_seconds)`). It maintains a global dict of per-key buckets, each holding a deque of monotonic-clock hit timestamps guarded by a lock, evicts timestamps older than the window, and raises 429 with a Retry-After header when the limit is exceeded. The sliding-window math and locking are correct and it is wired into auth/login/refresh/public-booking endpoints. Verdict: works for the happy path on a single process, but its protection value is undermined by client-controllable IP derivation and it leaks memory unboundedly, so I rate it partial._
- **[high]** Rate limit trivially bypassed via spoofed X-Forwarded-For — `backend/app/utils/ratelimit.py L38-45,52`
  - _client_ip() unconditionally trusts the first value of the client-supplied X-Forwarded-For header as the rate-limit key, with no trusted-proxy allowlist. Because the attacker fully controls this header, they can send a different (or random) XFF on every request and each request lands in a brand-new bucket, completely defeating the per-IP limits that protect brute-force-sensitive endpoints (auth_login limit=10/min, auth_tg=30/min, public_booking=10/min). This negates the stated purpose ('blocks brute-force'). Fix: only honor X-Forwarded-For when the immediate peer (request.client.host) is a known/trusted proxy (e.g. Render's load balancer), and parse the rightmost untrusted hop rather than the leftmost client-controlled one; otherwise fall back to request.client.host. Make the trusted-proxy set configurable via settings.
- **[medium]** Unbounded memory growth: buckets are never evicted — `backend/app/utils/ratelimit.py L25,29-35`
  - _BUCKETS is a process-global dict that only ever grows: _bucket_for() creates a _Bucket per distinct key and nothing ever removes empty/idle buckets. Every unique client IP (and, given finding #1, every spoofed X-Forwarded-For value) permanently consumes a dict entry plus a deque and a Lock. An attacker rotating XFF values can inflate this without bound, and even legitimately the table grows monotonically over the process lifetime — a slow memory leak. Fix: add periodic reaping of buckets whose hits deque is empty (or whose last hit is older than the window), e.g. opportunistically delete the key under _BUCKETS_LOCK when the deque empties after pruning, or run a background sweeper. Switching to Redis with TTLs (as the module docstring already anticipates) also resolves this.
  - ✅ Работает: Sliding-window pruning is correct: timestamps older than now - window_seconds are popped from the left of the deque before the count check, giving an accurate rolling window rather than a fixed-bucket window.; Uses time.monotonic() instead of wall-clock time, so the limiter is immune to NTP adjustments / clock jumps and cannot be tricked by system time going backward.; Concurrency is handled correctly: a global lock guards bucket creation (check-then-create is atomic) and each bucket has its own lock guarding its deque, so the prune/count/append sequence is atomic. Sync def dependencies run in FastAPI's threadpool, where these threading.Locks are the right primitive.; Retry-After computation (bucket.hits[0] + window_seconds - now, +1 ceiling) is sensible and the value is returned both in the 429 detail and the standard Retry-After header.; Reasonable fallback chain for client identification ending in 'anon' so the dependency never crashes on a missing request.client.

### `bot:keyboards+throttle` — working (0 находок)
_inline.py builds all the bot's inline keyboards with colon-delimited callback data (role/book/svc/day/time/confirm/own_*/rej/qrev). throttling.py is a global update-level middleware that rate-limits only callback-query button presses per user to 0.5s, answering throttled callbacks so the spinner stops and letting plain (FSM-text) messages through untouched. Both files are correct and consistent with their consumers in handlers/booking.py, owner.py, start.py. No real defects found; the colon-in-time-value parsing is handled correctly everywhere via split with the right maxsplit, and the throttle map is pruned to avoid unbounded growth._
  - ✅ Работает: Callback-data colon scheme is parser-safe: time values like "14:30" contain a colon, but every consumer (pick_time, promo_skip, promo_apply, confirm) parses with cb.data.split(":", 3), and the time-bearing keyboards (times_kb, confirm_kb) emit exactly time:{sid}:{d_iso}:{t}, so the trailing HH:MM is preserved intact (booking.py:481,483).; All in-scope keyboard callbacks stay under Telegram's 64-byte callback_data limit: the longest, confirm:{uuid}:{date}:{HH:MM}, is ~61 bytes. (The only over-limit pattern, stfok with two UUIDs ~79 bytes, lives in booking.py, outside this audit.); Throttling correctly scopes to callback queries only and explicitly lets non-callback updates (FSM text: phone, promo code, review comment) pass through, avoiding silently dropping user-typed input.; Throttled callbacks are answered (callback.answer() in a try/except) so the client's loading spinner clears instead of hanging, and the answer failure is swallowed safely.; The per-user timestamp map is bounded: once it exceeds 10k entries it is rebuilt keeping only entries newer than 1h, preventing unbounded memory growth from one-off users; time.monotonic() is the right clock for elapsed-time comparison (immune to wall-clock/NTP jumps).; Defensive guards: event_from_user is checked for None before use; back/menu navigation always carries the slug so terminal screens can return to the business menu; can_review/owner_view gating conditionally adds buttons without breaking the base layout.

### `bot:start` — working (4 находок)
_This module is the Telegram bot's entry/onboarding surface: /start with no arg routes to owner-greeting or role-choice; /start <slug> renders a business landing card (logo + welcome text + menu); callback handlers drive a viloyat -> tuman -> category business-search funnel, contacts, back-to-menu, and the review-picker. It appears to work end-to-end: HTML injection is consistently neutralized via h() on all user-controlled strings, callback_data is parsed defensively with length/format checks, edit errors are swallowed by safe_edit_text, and DB sessions are opened/closed in try/finally. The defects found are edge-case (over-long slugs producing invalid deep-link buttons), an inconsistency (deactivated-business contacts still reachable), minor N+1, and dead code._
- **[medium]** Slug up to 128 chars produces an invalid Telegram deep-link button, breaking the whole search-results message — `backend/bot/handlers/start.py L357`
  - filter_results builds URL buttons as https://t.me/{bot_username}?start={b.slug}. Telegram's start deep-link parameter is limited to 64 characters; the slug schema (backend/app/schemas/business.py:25, SLUG_PATTERN max_length 128) allows up to 128 chars. A business whose slug is 65-128 chars yields a malformed url=, and Telegram rejects the ENTIRE inline keyboard with TelegramBadRequest. safe_edit_text only swallows 'message is not modified', so this exception propagates and the user's search returns an error instead of results -- and one bad business in the list of 30 breaks the whole page. Fix: cap slug length at 64 in the schema, or skip/guard businesses whose slug exceeds 64 chars when constructing deep-link buttons in the bot.
- **[low]** contacts handler does not filter on is_active, exposing deactivated businesses — `backend/bot/handlers/start.py L386`
  - The contacts callback fetches Business by slug only (filter(Business.slug == slug)), unlike cmd_start (line 89), back_to_menu (line 408) and qr_review_pick_booking (line 441) which all also require Business.is_active.is_(True). A user who deep-linked into a now-deactivated business and taps 'Kontaktlar' still gets its phone/address. Minor info-consistency gap. Fix: add `Business.is_active.is_(True)` to the contacts query filter for consistency with the rest of the module.
- **[low]** N+1 queries in review-picker booking list — `backend/bot/handlers/start.py L467`
  - qr_review_pick_booking loops over up to 10 bookings and runs two separate queries per booking -- Service lookup (line 468) and Review lookup (line 469) -- i.e. up to ~20 round trips on a synchronous session that blocks the event loop. Fix: batch-load services by service_id IN (...) and reviews by booking_id IN (...) into dicts before the loop, or use selectinload/joinedload.
- **[low]** Dead code: _user_can_review is defined but never called — `backend/bot/handlers/start.py L50`
  - _user_can_review() is unused anywhere in the codebase (grep confirms a single definition site). Since commit e764a5f the menu hardcodes can_review=True (lines 117, 426), so eligibility is no longer gated by this helper -- actual gating now happens inside the qrev flow. The orphaned function is harmless but misleading; remove it or wire it back if the 'show only to eligible users' behavior is ever wanted again.
  - ✅ Работает: HTML injection is consistently prevented: every user-controlled string (welcome_text, business name, owner first_name, phone, address) is wrapped in h() before interpolation into HTML-mode messages (lines 96-97, 129-130, 390, 412-413, 504). The htmlsafe.h() helper escapes via html.escape. Button label text is left unescaped, which is correct because Telegram does not HTML-parse inline-button text.; Callback_data is parsed defensively: split with explicit maxsplit and exact-length checks (flt:c expects 4 parts line 266, flt:r expects 5 line 277), and int()/index lookups are wrapped in try/except (ValueError, IndexError) so malformed or stale callbacks degrade to a 'Xato' alert rather than crashing (lines 218-222, 286-299).; safe_edit_text correctly swallows only the harmless 'message is not modified' TelegramBadRequest and re-raises everything else, preventing phantom errors on double-tapped nav buttons while not hiding real failures.; Every DB session is opened with SessionLocal() and reliably closed in a finally block across all handlers. The sync Session in async handlers is intentional given the sync engine in app/database.py.; Review-eligibility query is correct: filters by client_id, business_id, status COMPLETED and date <= local_today() (lines 57-66, 453-464), and the timezone-aware local_today() is used rather than a naive date.; _logo_local_path safely resolves only its own /api/business/logos/ prefix via os.path.basename and existence checks, avoiding path traversal and gracefully returning None (with logo send wrapped in try/except) so a missing file on ephemeral storage never breaks the landing card.

### `bot:wiring+locales` — working (2 находок)
_This area is the dispatcher/bot factory (setup.py), the local polling entrypoint (main.py), the i18n string table (locales.py), and an empty handlers package marker (__init__.py). The wiring is sound: build_bot_and_dispatcher() creates the Bot with HTML parse mode, installs throttling middleware on the update observer, and includes the start/booking/my_bookings/owner routers; the same factory is reused by both the production webhook path (app/main.py lifespan + POST /webhook with secret-token header validation) and the dev polling path. Verdict: functionally working end-to-end, but the locales module is largely dead — only 2 of its 9 keys are used, and the bot's interactive handlers ignore i18n entirely, so RU businesses' clients see Uzbek in the booking flow._
- **[medium]** RU translations in locales.py are dead; bot flow is hardcoded Uzbek — `backend/bot/locales.py L1-24`
  - Only two keys ('reminder', 'new_booking_owner') are ever passed to t(): app/tasks/reminders.py:54 and app/routers/bookings.py:95. None of the four bot handlers (start.py, booking.py, my_bookings.py, owner.py) import bot.locales or call t() (grep for 'locales'/'t(' in bot/handlers/*.py returns nothing) — they emit hardcoded Uzbek strings. The Business.language column supports UZ/RU (app/models/enums.py:22-24), but a business with language='RU' still gets its entire interactive booking flow (welcome, choose_service/date/time, confirm_booking, booking_confirmed, cancellation) in Uzbek. The RU entries for 'welcome', 'choose_service', 'choose_date', 'choose_time', 'confirm_booking', 'booking_confirmed', 'booking_cancelled_by_owner' are unreachable dead translations. Fix: route handler-facing text through t(lang, key) using the business's language, or remove the unused keys to avoid a false impression of bilingual support.
- **[low]** Stale docstrings reference non-existent /webhook/{token} endpoint — `backend/bot/main.py L3-5`
  - main.py's module docstring (and the comment at app/main.py:40) describe the production endpoint as '/webhook/{token}', but the actual route is the token-less POST /webhook (app/main.py:168), authenticated via the X-Telegram-Bot-Api-Secret-Token header. set_webhook (app/main.py:67-74) also targets f'{api_url}/webhook'. The stale docs could mislead an operator debugging webhook delivery into looking for a token in the path. Fix: update both comments to '/webhook'.
  - ✅ Работает: build_bot_and_dispatcher() is a single shared factory reused by both webhook (app/main.py) and polling (bot/main.py), preventing dispatcher/handler drift between run modes; Router include order and middleware registration are correct: ThrottlingMiddleware is attached to dp.update so it sees the raw Update and correctly extracts callback_query; Polling entrypoint defensively calls delete_webhook(drop_pending_updates=True) before start_polling, avoiding TelegramConflictError when a webhook is still registered; t() is defensive: it upper-cases input, falls back to UZ for any non-R-prefixed value, and returns the key on a missing lookup rather than raising KeyError, so a bad language string or absent key never crashes the caller; The two keys actually used by t() ('reminder', 'new_booking_owner') exist in both UZ and RU, so the live i18n paths have no missing-key gaps; set_menu_button and set_webhook guard on https:// prefixes and wrap Telegram calls in try/except, so a misconfigured PUBLIC_APP_URL/PUBLIC_API_URL degrades gracefully instead of crashing startup

### `comp:atoms` — working (3 находок)
_A set of small presentational atoms (Avatar, Logo, Chip, StatusBadge, Loader, Toast, Section) under frontend/src/components/yz/. They are simple, well-typed, and used widely across dashboard/booking screens. They appear to work end-to-end; defects are limited to a couple of edge-case robustness gaps rather than functional breakage._
- **[low]** StatusBadge crashes if backend returns an out-of-enum status — `frontend/src/components/yz/StatusBadge.tsx L20`
  - const s = MAP[status] does an unchecked lookup. status is typed as BookingStatus, but the value originates from API JSON which is cast to the type, not validated at runtime. If the backend ever sends a status outside the four keys (e.g. a new 'NO_SHOW' or a lowercase variant), MAP[status] is undefined and the very next access s.bg throws a TypeError, breaking every booking row/card that renders the badge. Fix: const s = MAP[status] ?? MAP.PENDING (or a neutral fallback entry), or guard: if (!s) return null.
- **[low]** Avatar.initials breaks single-character surrogate-pair / multi-byte first chars — `frontend/src/components/yz/Avatar.tsx L9`
  - initials() uses parts[0][0] + parts[1][0] (UTF-16 code unit indexing). For names whose first letter is an astral-plane char (emoji, some scripts) this slices half a surrogate pair and renders a broken glyph. Also colorFor uses name.charCodeAt(0) which is the first code unit, so two distinct surrogate-pair names can collide on color. Low impact for typical Uzbek/Cyrillic/Latin names (which are BMP), but worth using Array.from(name)[0] / codePointAt for correctness if client names can contain emoji.
- **[low]** Toast timeout not cleared on unmount — `frontend/src/components/yz/Toast.tsx L20`
  - push() schedules setTimeout(...2400) that calls setItems after the delay. The timer id is never tracked or cleared, so if ToastProvider unmounts (e.g. route teardown) while a toast is pending, the deferred setState fires on an unmounted component. React 18 tolerates this without a hard error, but it is a latent leak. Minor; clear timers in a cleanup effect or track ids if this provider is ever conditionally mounted.
  - ✅ Работает: StatusBadge MAP keys exactly match the BookingStatus union (PENDING|CONFIRMED|CANCELLED|COMPLETED) in types/index.ts, so the typed happy path is exhaustive and correct.; Chip correctly renders a count of 0 by using count !== undefined rather than a truthiness check, avoiding the classic falsy-zero bug.; Avatar guards empty/whitespace names: initials() returns '?' for zero parts and colorFor() returns COLORS[0] when name is falsy, preventing NaN index lookups for empty strings.; colorFor uses charCodeAt(0) % COLORS.length which keeps the index in bounds for any non-empty string.; Logo correctly uses unoptimized + priority for the PNG and object-contain, and exposes aria-label='Yozuv'.; Toast context has a safe no-op default ((text)=>{}) so useToast() never throws when used outside a provider; push is memoized via useCallback/useMemo so the context value is stable.

### `comp:auth-shell` — working (3 находок)
_Three client components: AuthBootstrap gates the dashboard (validates stored access token via /api/auth/me, refreshes on 401/403, exchanges Telegram initData, forces /auth/setup when has_password===false, and redirects to /auth/login with a loop guard); Sheet wraps Radix Dialog as a bottom-sheet with a pointer-events cleanup workaround; DashboardShell lays out sidebar/tabbar/content and mounts the global NewBookingSheet. The flows are largely correct and the error/transient handling in AuthBootstrap is thoughtful. Main real issues are an accessibility gap (no Radix Dialog Title) and a stale session flag edge case._
- **[medium]** Radix Dialog rendered without a DialogTitle (a11y violation + runtime error) — `frontend/src/components/yz/Sheet.tsx L61-71, 88`
  - SheetContent renders DialogPrimitive.Content but never includes a DialogPrimitive.Title, and SheetHeader uses a plain <h2> (line 88) instead of DialogPrimitive.Title. Radix Dialog requires an accessible title for every Content: in dev it throws/logs `DialogContent requires a DialogTitle` and screen readers announce the dialog with no name. Every sheet in the app (ClientSheet, NewBookingSheet, BookingSheet, NotificationSheet, TabBar sheet, services/clients/promo pages) is affected. Fix: make SheetHeader's heading a DialogPrimitive.Title (asChild on the h2), or render a VisuallyHidden DialogPrimitive.Title inside SheetContent, and set aria-describedby={undefined} on Content (or add a Description) to silence the description warning.
- **[low]** yz_auth_redirect_attempt flag never cleared on the browser/native path, can suppress a legitimate login redirect — `frontend/src/components/dashboard/AuthBootstrap.tsx L175-195`
  - The redirect-loop guard sets sessionStorage 'yz_auth_redirect_attempt'='1' before bouncing to /auth/login, and only clears it after a successful exchangeInitData() (the Telegram path, line 195). For browser/native users exchangeInitData() always returns false, so the flag is never cleared for the rest of the tab session. After a successful password login the user returns to /dashboard with a token (state→ready) without ever clearing it. If the token later becomes definitively unauthenticated in the same tab (refresh returns invalid, falling through at line 164-167) or the user navigates back to /dashboard without a token, exchangeInitData() returns false, the flag is already '1', and instead of redirecting to /auth/login the component shows the 'failed' screen. Fix: clear sessionStorage.removeItem('yz_auth_redirect_attempt') as soon as a valid session is established (in the existing-token success branch around line 148-151 and after a successful fresh /me), not only on the Telegram exchange path.
- **[low]** Access/refresh tokens persisted in localStorage are exposed to XSS — `frontend/src/components/dashboard/AuthBootstrap.tsx L63-64, 108-109`
  - Both access_token and refresh_token are stored in localStorage. Any XSS on the dashboard origin can exfiltrate the long-lived refresh token and fully impersonate the user; localStorage is also readable by every script on the origin. This is a consistent app-wide design choice (api.ts reads the same keys) and may be intentional for the Telegram/Capacitor flows, but it is the highest-impact security tradeoff in this area. If httpOnly cookies are not viable cross-origin (Vercel front / Render back), at minimum keep the refresh token out of localStorage or shorten its lifetime and rotate aggressively.
  - ✅ Работает: AuthBootstrap correctly distinguishes auth failures (401/403 → drop tokens / re-auth) from transient/network failures (catch and 5xx → keep tokens, show retry), avoiding nuking a recoverable session (fetchMe/refreshTokens MeResult discriminated union).; Access-token-rejected path mints a new token from the refresh token before discarding the session (lines 141-146), preventing a logout on every dashboard load after the ~60min access token expires.; gateOnPasswordSetup only redirects on an explicit has_password===false, so an older backend that omits the field is a no-op rather than a redirect loop (lines 123-129).; Redirect-loop guard checks both document.referrer and a sessionStorage flag before bouncing to /auth/login, and uses window.location.replace so the failed attempt is not added to history.; cancelled flag from the effect cleanup guards all setState calls, avoiding state updates after unmount.; SheetRoot's pointer-events workaround only clears document.body pointer-events after confirming no other [role=dialog][data-state=open] remains, so it does not break a chained ClientSheet→NewBookingSheet open.
