### `comp:landing-2` — working (2 находок)
_Three presentation-only landing components (Features, Pricing, Categories) for the Uzbek-language marketing page. They render static arrays of cards with no data fetching, side effects, or async logic. Prices match the backend source of truth (MONTHLY_AMOUNT_UZS = 187_500, YEARLY_AMOUNT_UZS = 1_875_000 in payment_service.py), the 14-day trial claim matches business.py (timedelta(days=14)), and all CTA hrefs (/auth/login, /dashboard/settings) resolve to real pages. The components work end-to-end. The only issues are content-accuracy nits, the most notable being a self-contradictory yearly discount badge._
- **[low]** Yearly badge says "15% TEJASH" but actual saving is ~16.7% (and 2 free months) — `frontend/src/components/landing/Pricing.tsx L46`
  - The yearly tier advertises three figures that don't agree: badge `15% TEJASH` (15% off), note `2 oy bepul` (2 months free), and perk `2 oy sovg'a — yiliga 375 000 so'm tejaysiz`. Math: 12 × 187 500 = 2 250 000; yearly price is 1 875 000; saving = 375 000 = exactly 2 months = 16.67%, not 15%. So the badge understates the discount and contradicts the '2 months free' framing on the same card. Fix: change the badge to `2 OY BEPUL` or `~17% TEJASH` so all three figures are consistent (the docs/LANDING_COPY.md spec prescribed `15% TEJASH`, so the discrepancy traces back to the copy spec, but it is still wrong on the rendered page).
- **[low]** Paid-tier CTAs send anonymous visitors to an auth-gated page (extra redirect hop) — `frontend/src/components/landing/Pricing.tsx L24`
  - Oylik and Yillik CTAs link to `/dashboard/settings`. That page calls getToken() and, when no token is present, does `window.location.href = "/auth/login"` (settings/page.tsx:145). A logged-out landing visitor who clicks 'Oylik tarifni tanlash' therefore lands on /dashboard/settings, gets bounced to /auth/login, and after auth must navigate back to settings to actually pick the plan — losing the intent of which tier they chose. Fix: point logged-out paid CTAs to `/auth/login?next=/dashboard/settings&plan=MONTHLY` (or similar) so the chosen plan survives the auth round-trip, or gate the href on auth state.
  - ✅ Работает: Pricing figures match the backend source of truth: 187 500 so'm and 1 875 000 so'm equal MONTHLY_AMOUNT_UZS / YEARLY_AMOUNT_UZS in backend/app/services/payment_service.py:21-22; Daily-cost anchor is accurate: 187 500 / 30 = 6 250, rendered as '~6 200 so'm'; Yearly savings figure is arithmetically correct: 12×187 500 − 1 875 000 = 375 000 = exactly 2 months; '14 kun' trial claim matches backend trial length (timedelta(days=14) in business.py:82); All CTA hrefs resolve to real routes: frontend/src/app/auth/login/page.tsx and frontend/src/app/dashboard/settings/page.tsx both exist; /dashboard/settings is genuinely where plan selection + Payme/Click payment happen; '≈ $15' uses the approximation symbol, so it stays accurate across UZS/USD rate drift

### `comp:map+brochure` — working (5 находок)
_MapPicker is a Leaflet-based lat/lng picker that lazy-loads Leaflet from unpkg CDN at runtime, drops a draggable marker, supports map-click and geolocation, and reverse-geocodes via Nominatim. BrochureTrifold3D is a pure-CSS/3D-transform decorative double-sided trifold rendered from business data (services, contacts, schedule, pricing) with a deterministic non-scannable QR fallback. Both are client components ("use client") and are SSR-safe in practice. They appear to work end-to-end; the issues found are perf/correctness edge cases rather than outright breakage._
- **[medium]** value-sync effect re-fires every render and fights user interaction (new object identity) — `frontend/src/components/yz/MapPicker.tsx L128-132`
  - The caller (profile/page.tsx:328-332) builds a fresh `{ lat, lng }` object on every render, so `value` has a new reference each time. The effect `useEffect(..., [ready, value])` therefore runs on EVERY render where lat/lng are set, calling `markerRef.setLatLng` and `mapRef.setView(...)`. Combined with the click/drag handler which calls onChange -> parent setForm -> new value -> effect -> setView, every map click triggers an extra programmatic recenter/zoom-to-14 jump that the user did not request (e.g. clicking while zoomed to 11 yanks the view to zoom 14). Fix: gate the effect on actual numeric change, e.g. track last applied coords in a ref and bail if value.lat/value.lng are unchanged, or have the parent memoize the value object. Also avoid setView on coordinates that originated from the user's own click/drag.
- **[low]** Concurrent reverseGeocode calls; later result can overwrite earlier with no ordering guard — `frontend/src/components/yz/MapPicker.tsx L92-99`
  - handlePoint awaits reverseGeocode and then calls onAddressLookup(addr) with no request-sequencing. Rapid clicks/drags fire overlapping Nominatim requests; responses can resolve out of order so a stale address can win. Nominatim also enforces ~1 req/sec and an identifying User-Agent/Referer policy; bursts of clicks may be rate-limited/blocked, silently returning empty. Fix: track a monotonically increasing request id (or AbortController) and ignore results that are not the latest; optionally debounce drag/click before geocoding.
- **[low]** getCurrentPosition success path lacks try/catch around await; busy can stick on geocode throw — `frontend/src/components/yz/MapPicker.tsx L137-149`
  - In useMyLocation the success callback is `async (pos) => { ... await reverseGeocode(...); setBusy(false); }`. reverseGeocode swallows its own errors so this is usually fine, but if onAddressLookup (caller-supplied) throws, setBusy(false) never runs and the button stays disabled/'Kutilmoqda…' forever. The error callback correctly clears busy, but the success path has no finally. Fix: wrap the body in try/finally so setBusy(false) always runs.
- **[low]** No geolocation permission/secure-context guard; failures are silent — `frontend/src/components/yz/MapPicker.tsx L134-150`
  - useMyLocation returns silently if navigator.geolocation is undefined and the error callback does nothing but clear busy (no toast/message). On non-HTTPS origins (geolocation requires a secure context) or when the user denies permission, the user gets no feedback. Minor, but in the Capacitor/Telegram-webview context permission denial is common. Fix: surface an error message via a callback/toast on the error path.
- **[low]** reverseGeocode does not URL-encode and trusts unbounded coordinates — `frontend/src/components/yz/MapPicker.tsx L55-65`
  - lat/lng are interpolated raw into the query string. For map clicks they are valid numbers, but geolocation/marker values are not clamped; if a wrapped longitude (>180/<-180 from continued map panning across the antimeridian) is passed, Nominatim may reject it. Low impact given inputs, but clamping lat to [-90,90] and normalizing lng to [-180,180] before geocoding and before onChange would make the picker robust. No encodeURIComponent is strictly needed for numerics but should be added if inputs ever broaden.
  - ✅ Работает: SSR-safe: loadLeaflet guards on typeof window === 'undefined' and rejects; all DOM access is inside useEffect; both components are 'use client'. Leaflet script/link injection is deduped via querySelector and reuses window.L if already present.; Map lifecycle cleanup is correct: the init effect's cleanup sets cancelled=true (guarding the async then) and calls map.remove() in a try/catch, nulling refs to avoid leaks and double-init.; Existing-script branch handles the in-flight load case by attaching load/error listeners and also resolving immediately if window.L already exists.; BrochureTrifold3D is fully deterministic and self-contained: CSS is scoped under .yztf and injected once, avoiding global leakage; no SSR hazards (no window/document at module or render scope; window.setTimeout only inside the flip handler).; formatSchedule correctly groups consecutive working days with identical hours into ranges, skips non-working/out-of-range days, and slices times to HH:MM safely.; decorativeQr is a pure deterministic FNV-1a-seeded xorshift generator producing stable output for a given seed (memoized via useMemo), with proper finder patterns and timing lines; explicitly documented as non-scannable fallback.

### `comp:nav` — working (2 находок)
_Three navigation primitives: Sidebar (desktop md+ rail), TabBar (mobile bottom bar with a "Yana" sheet for overflow links), and ScreenHeader (page title bar with optional back button). All nav hrefs map to real routes under /app/dashboard/*, active-state logic correctly special-cases /dashboard to avoid matching every child route, and null pathname is handled. The area appears to work end-to-end. Only minor active-state and UX edge issues found, no correctness or security defects._
- **[low]** "Yana" tab not highlighted when admin is on /dashboard/admin — `frontend/src/components/yz/TabBar.tsx L88`
  - moreActive is computed from the static moreLinks array (line 88), which does NOT include the admin link. The admin link is only appended into allMore (line 90-92) and rendered inside the overflow sheet. So when an admin user navigates to /dashboard/admin (a real route, confirmed at frontend/src/app/dashboard/admin/page.tsx), the bottom-bar "Yana" button shows the inactive grey state even though the current page lives under that menu. Fix: compute active state against allMore, e.g. move the moreActive computation after allMore is built: const moreActive = allMore.some((l) => isActive(l.href)); (and define allMore before it).
- **[low]** ScreenHeader default back uses router.back() which can exit the app on direct/deep entry — `frontend/src/components/yz/ScreenHeader.tsx L24`
  - When back is true (not a string) and no onBack is given, go() calls router.back(). If the user opens a deep dashboard page directly (Telegram WebApp deep link, push notification, refresh, shared URL) with no in-app history entry, router.back() navigates to the browser's previous external page (or does nothing), pulling the user out of the app instead of to a sensible parent screen. Fix: prefer an explicit fallback route — callers should pass back="/dashboard" (string) where a deterministic parent exists, or guard router.back() with a history-length / referrer check and fall back to a default route when there is no in-app history.
  - ✅ Работает: Active-state logic correctly special-cases /dashboard so the home link is only active on exact match, while child links use pathname === href || pathname.startsWith(href + "/") to also highlight on nested routes (Sidebar L89-90, TabBar L83-86); All navigation hrefs map to real App Router pages — every /dashboard/* target in both Sidebar links and TabBar tabs/moreLinks has a corresponding page.tsx (verified via glob); no dead links; No false-positive active states: none of the nav hrefs are string-prefixes of another (e.g. no /dashboard/service vs /dashboard/services collision), and the + "/" boundary in startsWith prevents partial-segment matches; Null pathname is handled safely — Sidebar uses optional chaining (pathname?.startsWith) and TabBar coalesces usePathname() || ""; Admin link is gated behind an /api/auth/me is_admin check with a catch that silently no-ops on failure, so a failed auth call simply hides the admin entry rather than crashing the nav; External support link uses target="_blank" with rel="noopener noreferrer", avoiding the reverse-tabnabbing security issue

### `comp:sheets-misc` — working (3 находок)
_Three presentational sheet/drawer components: ClientSheet (client detail card with call/message/new-booking actions + stats tiles), NotificationSheet (scrollable notification list with relative timestamps and tap-to-navigate), and HelpDrawer (static collapsible FAQ accordion with support links). All are thin display components driven by props/local state with no data fetching of their own; they render and behave correctly for the data the backend actually produces. Verdict: functionally working, with a couple of latent fragilities and one likely-broken external action (Telegram message-by-phone)._
- **[medium]** "Xabar" action builds an invalid Telegram URL (t.me/+<phone> is an invite-link hash, not a phone lookup) — `frontend/src/components/yz/ClientSheet.tsx L104-110 (calls messageTelegram in utils.ts:106-123)`
  - The 'Xabar' button calls messageTelegram(client.phone), which constructs `https://t.me/+${digits}`. Telegram does NOT resolve `t.me/+<digits>` to a chat by phone number — the `+` form of a t.me link is a private group/channel invite-link hash, so the digits get interpreted as an invite token and the link will fail to open the client's chat (typically 'invalid invite link' or nothing). There is no public t.me URL that opens a 1:1 chat by phone. The utils comment claims it 'resolves to the chat of whoever owns that phone', which is incorrect. Fix: use the tg deep link `tg://resolve?phone=<digits>` (and inside the WebApp prefer Telegram.WebApp.openTelegramLink with the tg:// form), or drop the by-phone message feature and message via the stored telegram_id when present. Note client.telegram_id is already on ClientDetail but unused.
- **[low]** NotificationSheet crashes if backend ever emits an unknown notification type (no ICONS fallback) — `frontend/src/components/yz/NotificationSheet.tsx L92-93`
  - `const meta = ICONS[n.type]; const Icon = meta.icon;` dereferences meta with no guard. The TS union constrains n.type at compile time, but items come from the network (untrusted). If the backend adds a new notification type (or sends a typo) not present in ICONS, meta is undefined and `meta.icon` throws, blanking the whole list. Currently safe because backend (business.py:316-369) only emits the 5 mapped types, so this is latent, not live. Fix: `const meta = ICONS[n.type] ?? { icon: Bell, bg: 'bg-ink-100', fg: 'text-ink-500' };` and skip/relax the type narrowing.
- **[low]** Total-spent compact display rounds up and overstates the amount — `frontend/src/components/yz/ClientSheet.tsx L137`
  - `spent >= 1000 ? \`${fmtSum(Math.round(spent / 1000))}k\` : fmtSum(spent)` uses Math.round, so 1500 so'm renders as '2k' and 1900 as '2k', overstating the client's spend; 1499 renders '1k'. For a money figure shown to the business owner this is a misleading rounding. Fix: use Math.floor for a 'k' suffix (compact values conventionally truncate), or show one decimal (e.g. (spent/1000).toFixed(1)+'k') to avoid overstating.
  - ✅ Работает: ClientSheet guards against a null client (returns null) and falls back gracefully: name defaults to 'Mijoz', phone to '—', visits/total_spent to 0, favorite_service to '—'.; ClientSheet's 'Xabar' and 'Yozilish' actions correctly handle missing data — they toast 'telefoni saqlanmagan' when phone is absent and toast a fallback when onNewBooking isn't provided, and close the sheet after invoking onNewBooking.; NotificationSheet.relTime guards future timestamps with Math.max(0, ...) so clock skew yields 'hozir' rather than a negative duration, and degrades to the ISO date prefix for items older than a week.; NotificationSheet only navigates when n.link is present (guarded), closing the sheet after router.push so it doesn't stay open over the new route.; Notification list correctly distinguishes loading / empty / populated states, and items use stable n.id keys.; HelpDrawer is a pure static accordion: openIdx single-open logic is correct (toggling the open item collapses it), it early-returns when closed, and click-outside / stopPropagation on the inner panel is implemented correctly so backdrop taps close and inner taps don't.

### `comp:tour` — working (4 находок)
_A spotlight onboarding system: WelcomeModal (one-shot intro on first dashboard open), Tour (the dim-overlay + spotlight + tooltip engine with "info" and "action" step modes), and TourFloat (mounts Tour for per-page tours plus a replay "?" pill and a guided-onboarding progress chip). The happy path works end to end for the only mode actually used in production (all current steps are mode:"info"): measure target, dim around it, show tooltip, advance/finish, and (during guided onboarding) chain across pages. Neither Tour nor WelcomeModal locks body scroll or sets body pointer-events, so there is no pointer-events leak to clean up. The main real defect is that the "element not found" bailout calls finish()/onComplete instead of onClose, contradicting the component's own documented contract and falsely triggering completion side effects on the dashboard._
- **[medium]** Missing-target bailout calls finish()/onComplete, violating the documented contract and falsely launching the onboarding chain — `frontend/src/components/yz/Tour.tsx L107-109`
  - When the target element is still absent after the FIND_RETRY_MS budget, the locate() bailout does `if (!isLast) setIdx(idx+1); else finish();`. finish() = `(onComplete ?? onClose)()`. But the component docstring (lines 44-50) explicitly states that 'bailing on a missing element always calls onClose'. On the dashboard, Tour is wired with onComplete=finishDashboardTour and onClose=dismissDashboardTour (frontend/src/app/dashboard/page.tsx:553-554). finishDashboardTour() marks the tour seen AND kicks off startOnboarding() — the full forced multi-page guided chain. So if the LAST dashboard tour step's anchor is conditionally missing (not yet mounted / hidden), the tour treats a failed measurement as a successful completion and shoves the owner into the entire guided onboarding sequence they never opted into. Fix: in the missing-element branch call onClose() directly (early-dismissal semantics) rather than finish(): `if (!isLast) setIdx(idx+1); else onClose();`.
- **[low]** Tour has no Escape-to-close and no escape during the rect-pending black screen — `frontend/src/components/yz/Tour.tsx L169-176`
  - Tour registers no keydown handler, so Escape does not dismiss it (WelcomeModal handles Escape, Tour does not). Worse, while a step's target is being located (up to FIND_RETRY_MS=1200ms, or longer on a slow anchor that keeps re-measuring), rect===null renders only `<div className="fixed inset-0 z-[3000] bg-black/60" />` with pointer-events:auto, no close button, no tooltip and no Escape — a full-screen black overlay the user cannot dismiss until measurement resolves. Fix: add a keydown(Escape)->onClose listener (mirroring WelcomeModal), and render a small close affordance in the rect===null fallback.
- **[low]** WelcomeModal declares aria-modal but implements no focus trap — `frontend/src/components/yz/WelcomeModal.tsx L28-48`
  - The modal sets role="dialog" aria-modal="true" and focuses the container on open, but there is no Tab/Shift+Tab focus trap and no inert/aria-hidden on the background. Keyboard and screen-reader users can Tab straight out of the dialog into the still-interactive dashboard behind the z-2900 backdrop, contradicting the aria-modal contract. Fix: trap focus within modalRef (cycle first/last focusable on Tab/Shift+Tab) or apply inert to the rest of the page while open.
- **[low]** action-mode tours that open a Sheet/modal will be buried under the tour overlay (latent — no action steps exist yet) — `frontend/src/components/yz/Tour.tsx L197-246`
  - Tour renders at z-[3000] and its four dim divs cover the whole viewport except the spotlight. Sheets/dialogs render at z-50 (frontend/src/components/yz/Sheet.tsx:60,63). The 'action' mode is designed so the user clicks the highlighted control to advance, but if that control opens a Sheet/Dialog (the common case for an 'add' button), the newly opened sheet at z-50 sits far below the tour's z-3000 black overlay and is visually unreachable, while the tour either advances or finishes. This is currently dormant because every tour step in the app uses mode:"info" (no mode:"action" anywhere under dashboard pages), but the action path is broken for any future use. Fix: when in action mode either drop the tour overlay z-index below sheet overlays, or do not render the full dim while waiting for an action that triggers an overlay, or raise sheet z-index above the tour.
  - ✅ Работает: No body scroll-lock or body.style.pointerEvents mutation in Tour or WelcomeModal, so there is nothing to leak/clean up — the spotlight uses absolutely positioned dim panels, leaving the spotlight region naturally clickable for action mode (Tour.tsx:199-224).; Effect cleanups are thorough: the locate/measure effect cancels its rAF, clears the retry timer, and removes resize+scroll listeners on unmount/step-change (Tour.tsx:122-128); the action-mode click effect removes the capture-phase listener and clears its deferred timer (Tour.tsx:161-165).; Action-mode double-advance is guarded by a `consumed` flag so a fast double-click cannot skip two steps (Tour.tsx:153-155).; rect is reset to null on every step change so a new step never reuses the previous step's rectangle, and state is never mutated during render — all advancement lives in effects (Tour.tsx:71-73, 169-176).; Tooltip is clamped into the viewport both vertically and horizontally and flips above/below the target based on its vertical position, keeping buttons on-screen on short/mobile viewports (Tour.tsx:179-185).; usePageTour clears the deferred advanceOnboarding timer on unmount and before rescheduling, preventing a navigation firing after the component is gone when the user X-quits inside the 250ms window (use-page-tour.ts:46-55, 77-83).

### `core:main+obs+celery` — working (4 находок)
_App wiring is sound: FastAPI is built with a lifespan that starts the aiogram bot in webhook mode, CORS is configured from explicit env-driven origins (fail-fast if empty), routers are mounted under /api with a deliberate ordering note, there's a catch-all exception handler plus a reverse proxy to the Next.js frontend, and Sentry/Celery are initialized per-process with sensible tags and a beat schedule pinned to Asia/Tashkent. It appears to work end-to-end. The defects found are edge-case/operational rather than show-stoppers: a few cleanup paths and proxy fall-through behaviors that can mask bugs or leak resources._
- **[medium]** Catch-all frontend proxy masks API 404s (unregistered /api/* paths get proxied to Next.js) — `backend/app/main.py L214-252`
  - frontend_proxy is mounted as @app.api_route("/{path:path}", ...) and matches ANY path not matched by an earlier route, including mistyped or unregistered /api/* paths (e.g. GET /api/typo, or a real endpoint hit with the wrong HTTP method). Instead of returning a JSON 404/405 from the API, the request is forwarded to the Next.js upstream and the client receives frontend HTML with a 200/404 from Next. This silently masks API routing/method bugs and produces confusing non-JSON error bodies for API consumers (the mobile app / frontend fetch code expecting JSON). Fix: guard the proxy to reject /api and /webhook prefixes explicitly, e.g. `if path == 'webhook' or path.startswith('api/'): raise HTTPException(404)` at the top of frontend_proxy, so genuine API misroutes surface as JSON 404s.
- **[low]** Frontend httpx client and bot teardown skipped when BOT_TOKEN is unset — `backend/app/main.py L50-53, 90-106`
  - The try/finally that closes _frontend_client and the bot session lives only in the code path taken when settings.bot_token is truthy. When BOT_TOKEN is empty the lifespan does `yield; return` at lines 52-53 and never enters the finally block, so on shutdown the shared httpx.AsyncClient created lazily by _get_frontend_client() is never aclose()d. In practice this leaks only at process exit (so impact is small), but the cleanup is structurally tied to the wrong condition: _frontend_client cleanup is independent of whether the bot is running. Fix: move the _frontend_client.aclose() into an outer try/finally that wraps the entire lifespan body regardless of bot_token, so the proxy client is always closed on shutdown.
- **[low]** set_webhook uses allowed_updates that drop update types the bot may rely on (e.g. my_chat_member, inline) — `backend/app/main.py L73`
  - allowed_updates is hard-coded to ["message", "callback_query"]. Telegram will then silently drop every other update type for the webhook. If any handler in bot/ ever listens for my_chat_member (block/unblock detection), chat_member, edited_message, or pre_checkout_query/successful_payment, those updates will never arrive and the failure is invisible (no error, just missing events). This is a latent footgun rather than a confirmed bug today. Fix: derive allowed_updates from the dispatcher's resolved update types (aiogram exposes dp.resolve_used_update_types()) instead of a manual literal, so the webhook subscription stays in sync with registered handlers.
- **[low]** WEBHOOK_SECRET random per-process default breaks across multi-worker / restart deployments — `backend/app/config.py L41`
  - webhook_secret defaults to secrets.token_hex(16), generated at import time per process. The lifespan registers the webhook with this secret (main.py:71) and the /webhook handler validates against it (main.py:173). If the deployment runs more than one Uvicorn/Gunicorn worker, each worker imports config separately and gets a DIFFERENT default secret; whichever worker ran lifespan and called set_webhook registered its own secret, but incoming webhook requests are load-balanced across workers, so workers with a different default will reject valid Telegram requests with 403. The config validator (config.py:99) only checks length >= 16, not that it was explicitly set, so the random default passes validation in non-production too. The comment at config.py:38-40 acknowledges production must set it, but nothing enforces it and the multi-worker hazard is silent. Fix: in the production validator require WEBHOOK_SECRET to be explicitly provided (env present), not just non-empty/length-ok, so misconfigured multi-worker deploys fail fast at boot.
  - ✅ Работает: CORS is driven by explicit, comma-split origins with a fail-fast RuntimeError when empty (main.py:111-115); allow_credentials=True is safe here because origins are never the wildcard.; Telegram webhook secret is passed via the X-Telegram-Bot-Api-Secret-Token header and constant-compared before processing (main.py:172-174), and the bot token never appears in the URL — good secret hygiene.; Router registration order is deliberate and documented: /business/me/* specific routers are mounted before business.router so /business/{slug} doesn't shadow them (main.py:139-158).; init_sentry is idempotent via the _initialised guard, gracefully degrades when sentry-sdk is missing or DSN is empty, and explicitly sets send_default_pii=False to avoid shipping phone numbers / receipts (observability.py:31-65).; Sentry is initialized independently in both the API process (main.py:38) and the Celery worker (celery_app.py:9) with distinct component tags, correctly reflecting that they are separate processes.; Celery beat schedule is pinned to Asia/Tashkent and times are chosen in quiet windows; tasks are also explicitly imported (celery_app.py:48-49) so beat-registered tasks are actually discoverable even if autodiscover misses them.

### `core:schemas` — working (2 находок)
_These four Pydantic v2 schema modules define request/response models for analytics, auth, booking, and business endpoints. They work end-to-end: routers and the bot import and use them as verified, response models map cleanly from ORM via from_attributes, and money is consistently handled as int (no float rounding bugs). The security-sensitive design is deliberate and mostly correct (password hashes/tokens never exposed in UserMe; is_active excluded from BusinessUpdate to block self-reactivation; client_telegram_id reset server-side from verified initData). The defects found are missing-validation/data-integrity gaps rather than functional breakage._
- **[low]** latitude/longitude accept any float — no geographic bounds — `backend/app/schemas/business.py L32-33, 49-50`
  - BusinessCreate.latitude/longitude and BusinessUpdate.latitude/longitude are typed `float | None` with no ge/le constraints. The DB columns (business.py model lines 33-34) are plain Float, so values like latitude=9999 or longitude=-5000 are accepted and persisted, producing garbage map pins on the public business page. Fix: add bounds, e.g. `latitude: float | None = Field(default=None, ge=-90, le=90)` and `longitude: float | None = Field(default=None, ge=-180, le=180)` on both schemas.
- **[low]** Unbounded client_phone / names / promo_code can exceed DB column limits → 500 instead of 422 — `backend/app/schemas/booking.py L31-36`
  - BookingCreatePublic.client_first_name, client_last_name (DB Client.first_name/last_name = String(255)), client_phone (DB String(32)), and promo_code carry no max_length. While first/last name typically come from trusted Telegram initData, client_phone and promo_code are accepted from the request body and flow unbounded into get_or_create_client (booking_service.py:62-69) and _apply_promo (booking_service.py:227). A phone string >32 chars (or name >255) raises a DB DataError on flush/commit, surfacing as an unhandled 500 rather than a clean 422 (the router only catches ValueError at bookings.py:69). Fix: add max_length on these fields, e.g. client_phone max_length=32, client_first_name/client_last_name max_length=255, promo_code max_length=64, so Pydantic rejects with 422 before the DB write.
  - ✅ Работает: auth.py UserMe (lines 33-44) exposes no password hash, no auth-identity secrets, and no tokens — only id/telegram_id/username/name/phone/is_admin; sensitive fields are not leaked.; auth.py LoginRequest/SetPasswordRequest (lines 10-20) enforce sensible bounds (login 3-64, password 6-128) preventing empty/oversized credentials.; business.py BusinessUpdate (lines 54-56) deliberately omits is_active with a documented rationale — a blocked owner cannot re-activate themselves via PUT /business/me. Real privilege-escalation guard.; business.py SLUG_PATTERN (line 13) anchors slug to ^[a-z0-9][a-z0-9-]{0,127}$, preventing slugs like '..', 'me', or route-prefix aliases; applied via Field pattern on BusinessCreate.slug.; business.py caps long-form owner text at LONG_TEXT_MAX=2000 and address/phone fields, preventing pathological large blobs from reaching Telegram message sends.; business.py cancel_window_hours bounded ge=0 le=168 (line 53) — sane cap that prevents typos from flagging every cancel.

### `fe:auth-callback` — working (0 находок)
_This client component is the OAuth return target. The backend (backend/app/routers/auth.py:274) redirects the browser to /auth/callback with access/refresh JWTs in the URL fragment; the page parses the fragment via URLSearchParams, stores both tokens in localStorage under yozuv_access/yozuv_refresh, and redirects to /dashboard with history.replace to drop the token-bearing URL. The localStorage key names match what lib/api.ts reads (api.ts:20,25), so the flow is consistent end-to-end. Verdict: working; the logic, key names, and fragment-based token transport are all correct, with no real defects found._
  - ✅ Работает: Tokens are transported in the URL fragment (never sent to server / logs) and the page correctly strips the leading '#' before parsing with URLSearchParams (line 17-18).; localStorage keys 'yozuv_access'/'yozuv_refresh' written here (lines 22-23) exactly match the keys read by frontend/src/lib/api.ts (lines 20, 25), so the auth handoff is consistent end-to-end.; Uses window.location.replace('/dashboard') (line 25) instead of push, correctly removing the token-bearing URL from browser history so the secrets aren't recoverable via Back.; Both access AND refresh are required (line 21) before storing/redirecting; a partial/empty fragment (e.g. 'access=' yields falsy '') falls through to the failure UI rather than persisting half a session.; All parsing is wrapped in try/catch (lines 16-31) with a graceful failure state offering a 'Qayta urinish' link back to /auth/login (lines 34-45), so malformed input cannot throw an unhandled error.; Runs in useEffect with an empty dep array (line 32), so it executes once on mount client-side, appropriate since window/localStorage are browser-only and the component is marked 'use client'.

### `fe:auth-login-register` — working (3 находок)
_The login page implements three auth paths (Telegram Mini App auto-login, username/phone+password form, Google OAuth redirect) with client-side platform detection deciding which are shown; it POSTs to the backend, stores the returned JWT pair in localStorage, and hard-redirects to /dashboard. The contract matches the backend (`{login,password}` -> `{access_token,refresh_token}`). The register page is intentionally static marketing content that funnels users to the login page (Telegram-first signup), so there is no real registration form to break. Overall the area works end-to-end; the defects found are low/medium severity around token-shape validation and raw error leakage, not flow-breaking bugs._
- **[medium]** Raw backend response body leaked verbatim into the Telegram-login error UI — `frontend/src/app/auth/login/page.tsx L133`
  - On a non-OK Telegram auth response the code shows `setErr(\`HTTP ${res.status}: ${text}\`)`, dumping the raw response body (up to full length here; the debug bag truncates to 200 but `err` does not) directly to the end user. If the backend (or an upstream proxy / WAF / 500 handler) returns a stack trace, internal hostnames, or HTML error page, that content is rendered to the user. Fix: show a generic localized message for non-OK statuses and keep the raw body only in the collapsed diagnostics pane (which is already gated behind the debug toggle).
- **[low]** Token response cast without shape validation can persist literal "undefined" — `frontend/src/app/auth/login/page.tsx L69-72, 138-141`
  - On a 2xx response the code does `const tokens = JSON.parse(text) as {access_token, refresh_token}` and immediately `localStorage.setItem('yozuv_access', tokens.access_token)`. If the backend ever returns 200 with an unexpected body (e.g. a proxy/HTML interstitial, or a partial payload), `tokens.access_token` is undefined and localStorage stores the string "undefined", after which the app redirects to /dashboard and every subsequent authenticated request fails with a confusing 401 loop rather than a clean error. Fix: validate `typeof tokens.access_token === 'string' && tokens.access_token` (and refresh) before storing; otherwise setErr and abort the redirect. Also `JSON.parse(text)` itself can throw on a non-JSON 200 body — wrap it so it surfaces as an error instead of an unhandled exception in the password handler (the telegram handler's outer try/catch happens to cover it, but the password handler's try also covers it, so this is mainly the silent-undefined case).
- **[low]** Phone-login placeholder advertises a spaced format the backend never matches — `frontend/src/app/auth/login/page.tsx L294`
  - The login input placeholder is `+998 90 123 45 67 yoki username` and the client only does `loginId.trim()` (no internal-space stripping). The backend login matches `func.lower(User.phone) == ident` exactly against a stored phone that comes from Telegram's contact share (compact `+998901234567`, no spaces). A user who types the phone the way the placeholder shows it (with spaces) will get "Login yoki parol noto'g'ri" even with correct credentials. Fix: normalize the phone client-side (strip spaces/dashes/parens) before sending, or change the placeholder to a compact format, and ideally normalize on the backend too for symmetry with how phones are stored.
  - ✅ Работает: Request/response contract is correct: POST /api/auth/login with {login, password} and the {access_token, refresh_token} shape both match backend schemas (backend/app/schemas/auth.py, routers/auth.py login()).; Error parsing for the password form is robust: it reads text then tries JSON.parse to extract `.detail`, falling back to raw text and finally `HTTP <status>` (lines 58-66).; Submit button is correctly guarded against empty/short input and double-submit: disabled when pwBusy || login<3 || password<6, plus an early `if (pwBusy) return` guard (lines 49, 320).; Platform-aware rendering is sound: Telegram/Google blocks are hidden in the native APK and inside the Mini App as appropriate, and auto-login only fires when isTelegramMiniApp() is true (lines 151-165, 206, 331).; Failed Google round-trips are surfaced cleanly by reading the `?e=` query param and mapping to localized messages (lines 156-161).; autoComplete hints (username / current-password) are set correctly for password manager support (lines 292, 311).

### `fe:biz-slug` — working (2 находок)
_Public business landing page (frontend/src/app/biz/[slug]/page.tsx) — a Next.js App Router async Server Component that fetches a business by slug plus its services and review summary, renders an SEO-optimized page with LocalBusiness JSON-LD, OG/Twitter meta, and a "Yozilish" CTA deep-linking into the Telegram bot. The data contract matches the backend exactly (BusinessPublic, services list, reviews-summary {average_rating, count}), error states are handled via notFound() for missing businesses and empty fallbacks for services/summary. It appears to work end-to-end; only minor latent edge cases were found, no blocking defects._
- **[low]** OG/Twitter image breaks if logo_url is an external absolute URL — `frontend/src/app/biz/[slug]/page.tsx L101`
  - generateMetadata builds logoAbs = biz.logo_url ? `${API}${biz.logo_url}` : `${API}/logo.png`. This assumes logo_url is always a relative path. The backend (backend/app/routers/files.py:59) explicitly treats logo_url as possibly 'external' ('Map a stored logo_url back to a file path, or None if it's external/empty'), meaning a logo_url like 'https://cdn.example/x.png' is a supported value. In that case logoAbs becomes 'https://yozuv.onrender.com https://cdn...' — a malformed URL that yields a broken OG/Twitter preview image and a broken JSON-LD `image` (same pattern at line 148). Fix: guard with absolute-URL detection, e.g. const abs = (u:string)=> /^https?:\/\//.test(u) ? u : `${API}${u}`; then logoAbs = biz.logo_url ? abs(biz.logo_url) : `${API}/logo.png`. Low severity because the current upload path always stores a relative /api/... path.
- **[low]** Telegram start deep-link can silently fail for slugs outside [A-Za-z0-9_-] — `frontend/src/app/biz/[slug]/page.tsx L147`
  - botLink = `https://t.me/${BOT}?start=${encodeURIComponent(biz.slug)}`. Telegram's start parameter only accepts the character set A-Z a-z 0-9 _ and - (1-64 chars); anything else (including the %XX produced by encodeURIComponent for non-ASCII) is rejected/ignored by Telegram, so the bot would open without the business context and the deep-link booking entry would break. If slug generation ever permits non-ASCII (e.g. Cyrillic/Latin-Uzbek business names) this CTA silently degrades. Fix: ensure slugs are constrained to Telegram's allowed charset at creation time (verify the slug generator), or fall back to a numeric base64-safe payload. Low because slugs are likely already ASCII-only, but this was not confirmed in a slug-sanitizing routine.
  - ✅ Работает: Data-fetch contract matches backend exactly: fetchBusiness -> GET /api/business/{slug} (BusinessPublic), fetchServices -> /services, fetchSummary -> /reviews-summary returns {average_rating, count} (backend/app/routers/reviews.py:180), all field names/types align.; Error handling is correct: fetchBusiness returns null on !res.ok and the page calls notFound() (404), while services/summary degrade gracefully to [] and {average_rating:0,count:0} so a partial backend failure still renders the page instead of 500ing.; SSR caching via next:{revalidate:60} is a sensible tradeoff (owner edits appear within 60s, share-storms don't hammer the backend) and is applied consistently to all three fetches.; slug is correctly passed through encodeURIComponent in all three fetch URLs, preventing path-injection / breakage on special characters at the API layer.; JSON-LD is built defensively with conditional spreads (telephone, address parts, geo, aggregateRating, makesOffer) so absent fields are omitted rather than emitted as empty/null, keeping the structured data valid.; aggregateRating is only emitted when summary.count > 0, avoiding an invalid zero-review rating that Google would flag.

### `fe:catalog-map` — working (4 находок)
_A client-only Leaflet map page that fetches the public business catalog (limit=100), plots every business that has coordinates as a marker, binds a styled popup with rating/address and a Telegram "Yozilish" deeplink, and auto-fits bounds. It correctly lazy-loads Leaflet off the SSR bundle, tears down the map on re-render/unmount, and HTML-escapes user-supplied name/address. - **[medium]** Map only ever shows first 100 businesses with no pagination — silent data truncation — `frontend/src/app/catalog/map/page.tsx L55`
  - The fetch hardcodes /api/business/catalog?limit=100 (the backend max, business.py:454 le=100) and there is no offset loop. Once the catalog exceeds 100 active businesses, the map silently omits the rest, and the header count (`${items.length} ta biznes`, line 166) misleadingly shows '100' as if that were the total. For a 'find nearby business' map this is wrong as the directory grows. Fix: either page through the catalog endpoint (loop offset until a short page is returned) or add a server endpoint that returns all coordinate-bearing businesses; at minimum stop presenting the truncated count as the total.
- **[medium]** fitBounds with a single marker zooms to maxZoom, disorienting the user — `frontend/src/app/catalog/map/page.tsx L131`
  - When withCoords.length === 1, L.featureGroup([m]).getBounds() is a zero-area bounds; map.fitBounds(...pad(0.2)) snaps to the layer's maxZoom (19), dropping the user onto a street-level tile with no context. Fix: when markers.length === 1 use map.setView([lat,lng], 14) instead of fitBounds, or pass {maxZoom: 14} to fitBounds.
- **[low]** Header is 56px (h-14) but map fills 100vh-56px while inside min-h-screen parent — can overflow to page scroll — `frontend/src/app/catalog/map/page.tsx L195`
  - The <main> is min-h-screen and contains the 56px header plus a div of height calc(100vh - 56px). Total content height = 56px + (100vh-56px) = 100vh, which is fine only if there is no other in-flow content. But when `error` is set, the error card (lines 171-180) renders ABOVE the map div which is still in the DOM at full calc(100vh-56px) height, pushing total height past 100vh and creating a stray scroll plus an empty/blank map area below the error. Fix: don't render the map div when error is set (or hide it), e.g. gate the map container on !error.
- **[low]** loadLeaflet rejection on a slow/blocked CDN leaves the loading spinner stuck unless it rejects — `frontend/src/app/catalog/map/page.tsx L136`
  - The map effect only sets error in .catch. If unpkg.com (leaflet.js) is reachable but extremely slow, or the script tag's load event is missed, the promise neither resolves nor rejects and the page sits on 'Xarita yuklanmoqda…' forever because `items` is already set so the first spinner block (line 182, gated on !items) has already disappeared — actually once items load and map hasn't initialized there is no spinner at all, just a blank area. Minor: consider a timeout on loadLeaflet so a CDN stall surfaces the 'Xaritani yuklab bo\'lmadi' error instead of a blank pane. This depends on third-party CDN availability (unpkg), which is a runtime SPOF for this screen.
  - ✅ Работает: escapeHtml is correctly applied to all user-controlled popup fields (name, address) and covers &, <, >, double-quote, and single-quote, preventing stored XSS via business name/address injected as raw Leaflet popup HTML; The Telegram deeplink slug is passed through encodeURIComponent (line 117), preventing URL/param injection; Leaflet is lazy-loaded client-side via loadLeaflet with a shared in-flight promise and dedup of the <script>/<link> tags, keeping it off the SSR bundle; Map lifecycle is handled correctly: previous instance is .remove()'d before re-creating, and the effect cleanup removes the map and clears marker refs on unmount, avoiding leaks/duplicate maps during HMR or items re-fetch; Both effects use a `cancelled` flag to guard against setState/map-creation after unmount or stale fetch resolution; Coordinate filtering (latitude/longitude !== null) before plotting, with an explicit empty-set early return that still stores mapRef so cleanup works

### `fe:dash-admin` — working (3 находок)
_A single large client component for the platform admin panel (stats, businesses CRUD, subscriptions, card-payment approve/reject/refund, broadcast, backup import/export, audit log). Admin status is determined by GET /api/auth/me (is_admin) and used purely as a render guard; all mutations go to /api/admin/* and /api/payments/* endpoints whose authorization must be enforced server-side. The flows are wired correctly end-to-end and the code is generally careful (confirm dialogs on destructive actions, blob-URL revocation, coalesced token refresh in apiFetch). Findings are minor — no client-side auth bypass is present here, since real security depends entirely on the backend which is out of scope for this file._
- **[low]** Transient /api/auth/me failure locks a real admin out — `frontend/src/app/dashboard/admin/page.tsx L210-214`
  - useEffect calls apiFetch('/api/auth/me').then(set is_admin).catch(() => setIsAdmin(false)). Any transient network error or one-off 500 on the identity check resolves to isAdmin=false, which permanently renders the 'Kirish cheklangan' (access denied) screen until a full reload — there is no retry and nothing re-triggers the effect. A genuine admin hitting a momentary blip is told the page is admin-only. Fix: distinguish 'definitely not admin' (200 with is_admin=false) from 'could not determine' (network/5xx) and offer a retry / re-fetch on the latter instead of silently denying.
- **[low]** Subscription expiry date forced to UTC midnight-eve, shifting the local day — `frontend/src/app/dashboard/admin/page.tsx L474-476`
  - saveSub builds the ISO timestamp as new Date(`${subForm.expires_at}T23:59:59Z`).toISOString() — the literal 'Z' pins it to UTC. The admin (Uzbekistan, UTC+5) picks a calendar date; sending 23:59:59Z means the subscription actually ends at 04:59:59 the NEXT local day. Conversely openSubForm reads back expires_at.slice(0,10), so an expiry stored as e.g. 2026-06-30T19:00:00Z (which is 2026-07-01 00:00 local) will display as '2026-06-30', a day earlier than the owner experiences. For a paid-subscription end date this off-by-one-day boundary is a real access/billing correctness issue. Fix: pick one timezone convention (e.g. end of day in Asia/Tashkent) and apply it consistently for both the write and the slice(0,10) read-back.
- **[low]** Concurrent loadPending calls can revoke blob URLs still referenced by render — `frontend/src/app/dashboard/admin/page.tsx L244-260`
  - loadPending awaits all screenshot fetches, then calls setImageUrls(prev => { revoke every prev URL; return the freshly built urls }). approve() calls loadPending() again (Promise.all([loadPending(), loadRecent()])) and the initial isAdmin effect can also run it. Two overlapping invocations each revoke the other run's just-created object URLs inside the setState callback, so whichever finishes second can leave the displayed <img src> pointing at a revoked blob (broken thumbnail) and/or leak URLs created by the run whose setImageUrls executed first. Fix: guard with an in-flight flag / abort token or a request-sequence id so a stale run does not revoke the live map.
  - ✅ Работает: Destructive actions are gated behind window.confirm with explicit warnings: hard-delete businesses (line 498), refund which cancels the active subscription (line 545), and backup import which wipes all data (line 650).; Blob URLs for payment screenshots are revoked both on every reload (line 257-260) and on unmount via a dedicated cleanup effect (line 318-325), avoiding the common memory leak.; Reject requires a non-empty reason before calling the API (line 570-573), and card save validates 12–19 digits plus a non-empty holder before PUT (line 593-601).; New-business creation validates the owner Telegram ID (>0) and the slug against ^[a-z0-9][a-z0-9-]*$ on the client (line 407-417) in addition to backend checks, with slug input forced lowercase and telegram-id stripped to digits.; apiFetch centralizes auth: bearer token injection, a single coalesced refresh on 401 (refreshInFlight), token clearing + redirect to /auth/login on hard 401, and structured FastAPI 'detail' error extraction so toasts show meaningful backend messages.; All admin data loads (summary/businesses/pending/recent/audit/broadcast) are inside effects guarded by `if (!isAdmin) return`, so non-admins never trigger the privileged GETs, and per-tab loads (audit, broadcast) are lazy.

### `fe:dash-onboarding+qr` — working (3 находок)
_Two dashboard screens. Onboarding is a 3-step wizard (business details, services, schedule) that POSTs business, then loops POSTing services, then PUTs the weekly schedule, redirecting to /dashboard. QR page fetches business info plus a QR PNG and brochure PDF as blobs, offers QR/brochure download and a Telegram share link. Both appear to work end-to-end against the real backend endpoints; the only material issues are a service-duplication risk on the onboarding resume path and a couple of blob/URL robustness edges on the QR page._
- **[medium]** Onboarding resume path duplicates services (and silently drops schedule changes) — `frontend/src/app/dashboard/onboarding/page.tsx L179-198`
  - finish() wraps only the POST /api/business call in a try/catch that swallows errors matching /already exists/i, to support resuming a partially-completed onboarding. But if the business was created on a prior attempt and a later step failed (e.g. one of the per-service POSTs at line 187-198, or the schedule PUT), re-clicking 'Tayyor' swallows the 'Business already exists' error and then unconditionally re-POSTs ALL services. backend/app/routers/services.py:66 create_service does no dedup — it blindly inserts — so the user ends up with duplicate services (e.g. 'Soch olish' x2). Fix: make the service-creation step idempotent, e.g. on resume first GET /api/business/me/services and skip/replace existing ones, or have the backend upsert by (business_id, name), or only run the services loop when the business POST actually succeeded (track a 'created' flag and on resume fetch current state instead of re-posting).
- **[low]** Brochure/QR blob fetches bypass apiFetch token-refresh; a stale access token yields no QR with no error — `frontend/src/app/dashboard/qr/page.tsx L70-85`
  - The QR PNG and brochure PDF are fetched with raw fetch() using getToken() directly (lines 71, 79), not via apiFetch. apiFetch (frontend/src/lib/api.ts:84-96) performs a transparent 401 refresh-and-retry; raw fetch does not. If the access token is expired but the refresh token is still valid, the /api/business/me probe via apiFetch (line 52) will refresh the token and succeed, but the subsequently-stored token is not re-read here — these two raw fetches still use the token captured at line 49, which may be the just-refreshed one or, in a race, the stale one. On a 401 the catch blocks swallow it silently (lines 77, 85), so the QR card just shows 'Yuklanmoqda…' forever with no error toast. Fix: route these downloads through apiFetch (returning blob) or re-read getToken() after the /me call and surface a toast on non-ok responses.
- **[low]** downloadBrochure Telegram-WebApp branch leaves the button stuck on success — `frontend/src/app/dashboard/qr/page.tsx L106-111`
  - In the Telegram WebApp path, after tg.openLink(...) the function returns early (line 110). The finally block (line 128-130) still runs setDownloading(false), so that is fine — but note the early return is inside the try, so finally executes correctly. The real edge: if tg.openLink is present but token is null (line 106 requires both), it silently falls through to the blob path which inside Telegram mobile WebApp 'don't trigger the OS save dialog' per the code's own comment, so the download just fails with no feedback. Low impact since token is essentially always present here, but worth guarding: if running inside Telegram WebApp without a token, show an explicit message rather than attempting a blob download that the comment says won't work.
  - ✅ Работает: Onboarding 'business already exists' resume guard correctly distinguishes the recoverable 'Business already exists' (400) from the non-recoverable 'Slug already taken' (400): the regex /already exists/i matches only the former, so a slug collision still surfaces an error instead of being swallowed (verified against backend/app/routers/business.py:38,42).; QrPage correctly routes the 'business not found' case to onboarding: apiFetch throws the backend detail string 'Business not found' (deps.py), and the /business not found/i test at line 64 catches it, redirecting to /dashboard/onboarding.; Blob URL lifecycle on QrPage is sound: the effect tracks created object URLs in a local array and revokes them all on cleanup (lines 46-90), and the revoked flag prevents setState after unmount.; Schedule payload is well-formed: HH:MM values are suffixed to HH:MM:SS (lines 207-208) matching the backend ScheduleItem time fields, and the end<=start validation (line 152) is lexicographically valid for zero-padded HH:MM strings and only runs for working days.; Slug handling is safe for the Telegram deep link: slugify() restricts to [a-z0-9-] (lines 59-65) so biz.slug embedded in the t.me/...?start= URL needs no further encoding.; Services parsing is defensive: parseInt with '|| 0' / '|| 30' fallbacks (lines 193-194) prevents NaN from empty price/duration fields reaching the backend.

### `fe:dash-shell` — working (5 находок)
_The dashboard shell wraps content in AuthBootstrap (token validation / Telegram initData exchange / login redirect) then DashboardShell chrome; the dashboard home page fetches a single /api/business/me/dashboard bundle, renders stats, today's bookings, quick actions, share link, notifications (SSE + 5-min poll), and a first-visit tour. End-to-end the flow appears coherent and functional. There are a few real correctness/UX/security defects: an over-broad error-to-onboarding redirect, a mislabeled "trend" percentage, a JWT-in-URL leak for SSE, and a timezone-fragile unread-count comparison._
- **[high]** Any dashboard fetch error redirects established users to onboarding — `frontend/src/app/dashboard/page.tsx L139-141`
  - load() is the initial bundle fetch, and its .catch() unconditionally does router.replace('/dashboard/onboarding'). apiFetch already handles 401 (refresh, then redirect to /auth/login on failure), so any error reaching this catch is a non-auth error: a transient network failure, a 500, a 502 from Render cold-start, a JSON parse error, etc. An established business owner who hits a momentary backend hiccup is bounced into the onboarding flow instead of seeing a retry/error state. Fix: distinguish 'business not found / not onboarded' (e.g. a 404 or a specific error) from generic failures — only redirect to onboarding for the not-onboarded case, and show an error/retry UI otherwise.
- **[medium]** JWT access token passed in SSE URL query string — `frontend/src/app/dashboard/page.tsx L234-237`
  - The notifications EventSource URL appends ?token=<access JWT> because EventSource can't set headers. Tokens in URLs leak into Render/proxy access logs, browser history, and any Referer headers, and are higher-risk than header-borne tokens. The code comment acknowledges the pattern but it remains a real exposure. Mitigations: use a short-lived, single-purpose stream token instead of the full access JWT; or proxy SSE through the same-origin Next app with a cookie; at minimum ensure the backend never logs the query string for this route and keep access-token TTL short.
- **[medium]** "+X%" trend badge actually shows today-revenue as a fraction of week-revenue — `frontend/src/app/dashboard/page.tsx L346-352`
  - The badge renders a TrendingUp icon with `+{Math.round((summary.revenue / summary.weekRevenue) * 100)}%`. This is today's revenue divided by the week's total revenue — a share-of-week, not a growth/trend percentage. With a TrendingUp arrow and a leading '+', users will read it as growth. It is also unstable: early in the week today's revenue can be a large fraction (or, if week revenue includes today, it's bounded but still not a trend); the value can swing wildly and mislead. Fix: either compute a real period-over-period delta (e.g. today vs same weekday last week, or vs daily average) or relabel the badge so it doesn't imply growth.
- **[low]** Unread notification count uses local-time Date parsing vs Date.now() — `frontend/src/app/dashboard/page.tsx L196-203`
  - lastSeen is stored as Date.now() (epoch ms, line 260) and compared against new Date(n.created_at).getTime(). If the backend's created_at lacks an explicit UTC marker (e.g. '2026-06-28T10:00:00' with no 'Z'/offset), JS parses it as local time, shifting the comparison by the UTC offset (Asia/Tashkent is +05:00). That can make freshly-created notifications appear already-seen (undercount) or stale ones appear unread (overcount). Fix: ensure the API serializes created_at with a timezone designator (ISO-8601 with Z), and/or normalize on the client before comparing.
- **[low]** "Keyingi yozilish" (next booking) can show a booking already in the past — `frontend/src/app/dashboard/page.tsx L275`
  - next = bookings.find(b => b.status !== 'CANCELLED') || bookings[0]. This picks the first non-cancelled booking of the day regardless of its start_time relative to now. At, say, 18:00 the header still labels the 09:00 appointment as 'Keyingi yozilish' (the next booking). Assuming bookings_today is sorted ascending, this should filter to the next booking whose start_time is >= current time (falling back to the last one). Minor, but the label is actively wrong later in the day.
  - ✅ Работает: AuthBootstrap correctly handles the three auth states (checking/ready/failed) with a redirect-loop guard (document.referrer + sessionStorage flag) so it won't ping-pong between /dashboard and /auth/login.; apiFetch centralizes auth: coalesces concurrent 401s into a single /refresh via refreshInFlight, does exactly one transparent retry, clears tokens and redirects to /auth/login on hard 401, and parses FastAPI 'detail' (string or validation-array) for useful error messages.; The duration calc on lines 404-406 is correct: parseInt('HH:MM') yields the hour, slice(3,5) yields the minutes, so (endH-startH)*60 + (endM-startM) gives minutes.; The render gate `if (!ready || !biz) return <YzLoader fullscreen />` prevents rendering against null business data and avoids the tour mounting before anchors exist (tour is deferred until ready).; EventSource lifecycle is clean: listeners attached, a 5-min safety poll as fallback, and the useEffect cleanup closes the stream and clears the interval; the bookings-changed window event also reloads and is properly removed on unmount.; Notification fetch failures are intentionally swallowed (non-critical) without breaking the page, and notifLoading is reset in finally.

### `fe:lib-api` — working (3 находок)
_A thin fetch wrapper for the Next.js client: resolves the API base URL from NEXT_PUBLIC_API_URL (with an onrender fallback), reads/stores JWT access+refresh tokens in localStorage, attaches a Bearer auth header, coalesces concurrent 401s into a single /refresh call, transparently retries once after a successful refresh, and normalizes FastAPI error bodies (string or validation-array `detail`) into thrown Error messages. The logic is sound and matches how all callers use it. Verdict: works end-to-end for the JSON/FormData request patterns actually in use; the issues below are edge-case robustness/security hardening, not blockers._
- **[low]** Default backend fallback can silently send credentialed JWTs to a hardcoded host — `frontend/src/lib/api.ts L16`
  - `const API = ENV_API || "https://yozuv.onrender.com"` means a misconfigured production build (NEXT_PUBLIC_API_URL unset) still proceeds and sends Bearer access/refresh JWTs to the hardcoded onrender host. The code logs console.error (lines 12-14) but does NOT stop using the default, so tokens are transmitted there anyway. This is a real (if low-probability) token-exfiltration vector if that domain ever lapses or is reassigned. Fix: in production with no ENV_API, throw / block authenticated requests rather than silently defaulting, since the fallback transmits credentials.
- **[low]** No backoff / negative cache for a known-bad refresh token across request waves — `frontend/src/lib/api.ts L42-62`
  - refreshInFlight is cleared in the `finally`, so each new wave of 401s spawns a fresh /refresh call even when the refresh token is already known-expired/revoked (the previous attempt returned null). Coalescing only works within a single concurrent burst, not across sequential bursts, so a hard-down or 401-returning backend produces one /refresh per wave with no backoff. Not an infinite loop, but wasteful and can hammer the auth endpoint. Fix: add a short-lived negative cache so repeated waves skip /refresh while the token is known-bad.
- **[low]** Hard redirect on 401 discards unsaved form state and loses return URL — `frontend/src/lib/api.ts L89-94`
  - On a definitive 401 the code does `window.location.href = '/auth/login'` (a full page reload) unless already under /auth/. This drops any unsaved form input on the current page and does not preserve where the user was, so after re-login they land on the app root instead of returning to their edit. Fix: append `?next=${encodeURIComponent(location.pathname + location.search)}` and restore it on the login page; consider router navigation instead of a full reload.
  - ✅ Работает: Concurrent-401 coalescing via a single refreshInFlight promise correctly prevents a thundering herd of /refresh calls when a page fires multiple requests at once within one burst (lines 36-62).; FormData is correctly detected and Content-Type is NOT forced to application/json for it, so the browser sets the multipart boundary itself (lines 67-70); string/FormData bodies are also safely reusable on the single retry, and all callers use only JSON strings or FormData.; Content-Type is only set when a body is present and not already specified, avoiding clobbering caller-supplied headers (lines 68-70).; SSR-safe: token getters/clear and all localStorage writes guard on typeof window, so the module imports cleanly during Next.js server rendering (lines 19, 24, 29, 51).; 204 No Content is handled explicitly so res.json() doesn't throw on an empty body (line 124).; FastAPI error normalization robustly handles both string `detail` and the Pydantic validation array (list of {msg}), with a try/catch around JSON.parse and a fallback to raw text/statusText (lines 98-123).

### `fe:lib-leaflet+types` — working (2 находок)
_leaflet.ts is a client-only lazy loader for Leaflet CSS/JS; types/index.ts holds plain TS interfaces. SSR safety is correct. Two reliability defects in the loader; no defects in types._
- **[medium]** Failed Leaflet load cached forever — `frontend/src/lib/leaflet.ts L30-47`
  - inflight is never reset to null on resolve or reject. After one failed load, every loadLeaflet() returns the same rejected promise (line 21 short-circuit), so the map cannot recover without a full page reload. Fix: set inflight = null before reject in s.onerror and the existing-tag error listener (line 36).
- **[low]** Existing-script branch can hang forever — `frontend/src/lib/leaflet.ts L34-39`
  - If a leaflet script tag already exists but already finished loading while window.L is falsy (CSP-stripped or externally inserted), the load/error events already fired and never fire again, so the promise never settles (and poisons inflight). Fix: add a timeout fallback or re-inject a fresh script when window.L is absent.
  - ✅ Работает: SSR guard rejects server-side and caller runs inside useEffect; window.L cached and de-duped via inflight promise; callers guard against unmount with cancelled flag; type defs consistent with backend serialization

### `fe:lib-onboarding+tour` — working (2 находок)
_These three files implement a two-layer tutorial system: tour-state.ts persists a per-device "seen" map in localStorage; onboarding.ts is a small state machine (active flag + integer step cursor in localStorage) driving a guided multi-page sequence; use-page-tour.ts is the hook that auto-opens a page's tour (gated by seen-flag OR active onboarding step), and on dismiss advances the onboarding cursor and routes to the next page. The state machine, persistence, and hook lifecycle (timer cleanup on unmount, SSR guards, try/catch around localStorage) are all coherent and correctly wired. It appears to work end-to-end. Only minor edge-case defects found._
- **[low]** Fractional/corrupted stored step yields undefined step and silently stalls onboarding with active flag still set — `frontend/src/lib/onboarding.ts L55-65`
  - getOnboardingStep does Math.max(0, Math.min(length-1, n)) but never coerces to an integer. setStep only ever writes integers so normal flow is safe, but if STEP_KEY is corrupted externally (manual edit, a future build that changed the value, cross-tab tampering) to e.g. '1.5', the clamp leaves 1.5, and ONBOARDING_SEQUENCE[1.5] is undefined. Then isOnboardingTour returns false for every tourId (no tour ever auto-fires) and advanceOnboarding returns early because `current` is undefined, so the cursor never moves and endOnboarding is never reached — the user is stuck with the active flag set, no tours, and a progress chip whose label is '' (stepLabel falls back to ''). Fix: floor/parse to int, e.g. `const n = raw ? Math.trunc(Number(raw)) : 0;` and treat out-of-range as a reset (endOnboarding) rather than clamp, so a stale cursor from a shrunken sequence self-heals.
- **[low]** Progress chip briefly shows the old step/label after dismiss before navigation — `frontend/src/components/yz/TourFloat.tsx L46-54`
  - TourFloat re-reads getOnboardingProgress() on [tour.open]. dismiss() flips open->false immediately, but the cursor advance (advanceOnboarding) is deferred 250ms and the route change happens after that. So when the effect re-runs on close, it reads the still-current (old) step, showing the previous N/label for ~250ms+nav until the next page's TourFloat mounts. Harmless and self-corrects on the new page, but the chip momentarily lags. If a smoother transition is wanted, advance the cursor synchronously and defer only router.push, or re-read progress after the advance timer fires.
  - ✅ Работает: onboarding.ts state machine is internally consistent: startOnboarding sets active+step0, advanceOnboarding only acts when active AND tourId matches current step, last-step path calls endOnboarding+routes to /dashboard, no off-by-one (nextIdx>=length terminates correctly); All localStorage access is wrapped in try/catch with SSR guards (typeof window === 'undefined'), so quota/private-mode/server-render never throws (onboarding.ts:46-74, tour-state.ts:11-30); use-page-tour.ts correctly clears the deferred advance timer on unmount and before re-scheduling (lines 48-55, 77-79), preventing a navigation firing after the component is gone; Auto-open effect intentionally depends only on [tourId] with a documented eslint-disable, avoiding the immediate re-fire that including the fresh `steps` array would cause (lines 65-68); The seen-flag override during guided onboarding (isThisStep || !hasSeenTour) correctly lets already-seen tours replay as part of the chain (use-page-tour.ts:61-62); getOnboardingProgress/isOnboardingActive double-gate in TourFloat and the +1/-1 label indexing line up correctly with the stored 0-based cursor

_platform.ts is the single source of truth for runtime environment detection (Telegram Mini App vs Capacitor native shell vs plain browser), used by login, AuthBootstrap, and the Capacitor deep-link component to branch auth/UI logic. utils.ts exposes the standard cn() Tailwind class merge helper. Both are small, correctly SSR-guarded, and behave as documented; no real defects found._
  - ✅ Работает: isTelegramMiniApp() correctly requires non-empty initData (string + length>0), matching the documented intent that a Telegram link opened in a normal browser (script present but no initData) is treated as browser/password path (platform.ts:35-39).; All three detection functions guard typeof window === 'undefined' first, so they are safe to call during Next.js SSR without throwing ReferenceError (platform.ts:36, 43, 62 via getPlatform).; isNativeApp() safely handles both modern Capacitor (isNativePlatform function check) and older Capacitor (getPlatform()==='android'/'ios') with proper typeof and optional-chaining guards, avoiding crashes when Capacitor is absent (platform.ts:42-49).; getPlatform() priority order (telegram > native > browser) is sensible: signed initData is the strongest auth signal and correctly wins over the native shell (platform.ts:55-59).; cn() is the canonical clsx + twMerge composition, the correct pattern for de-duplicating conflicting Tailwind classes (utils.ts:4-6).

### `fe:root` — working (2 находок)
_frontend/src/app/layout.tsx is the root App Router layout: it wires up two Google/Geist fonts as CSS variables, defines static SEO metadata (title/description/OG/canonical/icons/themeColor), sets lang="uz", injects the Telegram WebApp SDK script in <head>, and renders children. frontend/src/app/page.tsx is the marketing landing page, a pure server component composing Hero/Features/HowItWorks/Categories/Pricing sections plus an inline-styled dark CTA and a footer. Both files are simple, well-formed, and appear to work end-to-end; the custom Tailwind tokens (rounded-4xl, shadow-soft-lg, bg-lilac, bg-ink-50) are defined in tailwind.config.ts and used consistently elsewhere. No correctness, security, or data-integrity defects found — only one minor SSR/hydration nit around the dynamically computed footer year._
- **[low]** Footer year via new Date().getFullYear() can cause a hydration mismatch / stale year — `frontend/src/app/page.tsx L60`
  - The footer renders `© {new Date().getFullYear()}` inside a server component. Next.js statically renders this page at build time, so the year is frozen to the build year — after a New Year rollover with no redeploy the copyright shows the previous year (cosmetic but visible). More subtly, if this page is ever switched to dynamic/SSR rendering, the year is evaluated on the server at request time and again on the client at hydration; if the request crosses midnight Dec 31 the two values differ and React logs a hydration mismatch and may patch the DOM. Fix: avoid time-dependent values in render. Either hardcode/derive the launch year, or compute the year in a small client-only effect (useState(initial) + useEffect to set the real year) with suppressHydrationWarning, or read it from a build-time constant. Severity is low because for a static landing page the only practical effect is a once-a-year stale label.
- **[low]** Telegram WebApp SDK loaded synchronously (async={false}) on the public landing page blocks render and is unused there — `frontend/src/app/layout.tsx L45`
  - The root layout injects `https://telegram.org/js/telegram-web-app.js` with async={false} (render-blocking) for EVERY route, including the public marketing landing page that has no Telegram WebApp dependency. A render-blocking third-party script in <head> delays first paint/LCP on the landing page and creates a hard dependency on telegram.org availability for the whole site to render. The explicit comment elsewhere in the codebase about needing the SDK is real for the Telegram-mini-app routes, but loading it synchronously site-wide is heavier than needed. Fix: load it only on routes that actually use Telegram.WebApp (e.g. via next/script with strategy="afterInteractive" inside the relevant layout/segment), or at minimum drop async={false} so it does not block document parsing. Low severity: functional, just a startup-performance and availability concern.
  - ✅ Работает: Root layout metadata is well-formed: metadataBase is built from NEXT_PUBLIC_SITE_URL with a sensible https://yozuv.uz fallback, canonical/openGraph/icons/themeColor are all set, and locale uz_UZ matches html lang="uz" — solid SEO baseline.; Viewport.themeColor is correctly exported via the separate `viewport` export (Next 14 App Router convention) rather than being stuffed into metadata, avoiding the deprecation warning.; Landing page is a clean pure server component (no client hooks, no 'use client'), so it renders statically with zero client JS for the page shell itself — good for LCP.; The dark CTA gradient is deliberately applied via inline style with a documented rationale (guarding against Tailwind purge/HMR dropping the dynamic background), a pragmatic and correct call since white text over a possibly-missing dark background would be invisible.; All custom utility classes used (rounded-4xl, shadow-soft-lg, bg-lilac, bg-ink-50/100/400/900, eyebrow, tap, font-display) are defined in tailwind.config.ts / globals.css and used consistently across ~49 files, so no missing-class rendering bugs.; Decorative blur/glow divs correctly use pointer-events-none so they don't intercept clicks on the CTA link beneath them.

### `infra:alembic-env` — working (0 находок)
_Standard Alembic env that wires `target_metadata = Base.metadata` and supports offline/online migration modes, pulling the DB URL at runtime from `get_settings().database_url`. The explicit model imports in env.py are a partial list (12 names) versus the 20+ tables exposed by app/models/__init__.py, but because `from app.models import (...)` executes the package __init__, every model module is imported and every table registers on the shared single `Base` (all models import `Base` from app.database). So autogenerate sees the full schema. The sync `engine_from_config` matches the sync `create_engine` in app/database.py, so the env is internally consistent and works end-to-end for sync Postgres URLs._
  - ✅ Работает: target_metadata = Base.metadata correctly points at the single declarative Base shared by every model (all 20+ model modules do `from app.database import Base`), so autogenerate/migrations see the complete schema.; `from app.models import (...)` on env.py:8 forces execution of app/models/__init__.py, which imports ALL model modules (including the staff_services association table and models not named in env.py's list), so the partial import list does not cause missing tables in metadata.; get_url() reads database_url lazily from get_settings() (env.py:30-31) instead of relying on the placeholder `sqlalchemy.url = driver://user:pass@localhost/dbname` in alembic.ini, so migrations use the real configured DB.; run_migrations_online uses pool.NullPool (env.py:53), the correct choice for short-lived migration connections, avoiding leaking a pooled engine.; Sync engine_from_config in env.py is consistent with the sync create_engine/Session in app/database.py, so the alembic toolchain matches the actual runtime DB access layer (no async/sync driver mismatch between them).; Both offline and online paths wrap run_migrations in context.begin_transaction(), giving transactional DDL on Postgres.

### `infra:fe-config` — working (2 находок)
_Frontend build/tooling config for the Next.js 14 app: next.config.mjs (standalone output, strict mode, two dev rewrites), tailwind.config.ts (design tokens, animations), postcss.config.mjs (tailwind+autoprefixer), and package.json (deps pinned to Next 14.2.18 / React 18 / Capacitor 6). The config is internally consistent and the app builds/runs with it. Verdict: working, with one latent rewrite misconfiguration risk and the (intentional) absence of HTTP security headers worth flagging._
- **[low]** Rewrites for /webhook and /health default to localhost:8000 in production — `frontend/next.config.mjs L2,9-17`
  - BACKEND_LOCAL defaults to http://localhost:8000 and is used as the rewrite destination for /webhook/:path* and /health. On Vercel there is no backend on localhost:8000, so if BACKEND_LOCAL_URL is unset any request to these paths via the frontend origin will fail (proxy to a dead host). In the current topology the bot/backend live on Render and nothing in frontend/src references /webhook or /health, so this is latent rather than active — but if a Telegram webhook or uptime check is ever pointed at the Vercel domain it will silently break. Fix: guard the rewrites to only register when BACKEND_LOCAL_URL is set (e.g. return [] when unset), or document/require the env var for any deploy that proxies these paths.
- **[low]** No HTTP security headers (CSP, X-Frame-Options, HSTS, etc.) — `frontend/next.config.mjs L4-19`
  - next.config.mjs defines no async headers(), and grep finds no Content-Security-Policy / X-Frame-Options / Strict-Transport-Security anywhere in the frontend. The app is a credentialed dashboard that stores JWTs in localStorage (frontend/src/lib/api.ts:18-32), which is reachable by any injected script, so the lack of a CSP and X-Frame-Options (clickjacking) increases blast radius of any XSS. Vercel may add some defaults, but app-level headers are absent. Fix: add an async headers() block setting at minimum X-Frame-Options/frame-ancestors, X-Content-Type-Options: nosniff, Referrer-Policy, and a CSP. Note this is a hardening gap, not an exploited bug.
  - ✅ Работает: Dependency versions are coherent and pinned: Next 14.2.18 with matching eslint-config-next 14.2.18, React 18.3 + react-dom 18.3 + @types aligned, Capacitor 6.x across all @capacitor/* packages, Tailwind 3.4 with matching postcss/autoprefixer — no obvious version skew or peer-dep conflicts.; postcss.config.mjs correctly wires tailwindcss + autoprefixer, matching the Tailwind 3 (not 4) major used in devDependencies.; tailwind content glob ./src/**/*.{ts,tsx} correctly covers the App Router source tree so classes aren't purged; darkMode class strategy and tailwindcss-animate plugin are properly declared.; output: 'standalone' is the right setting for the containerized Render/Capacitor build, and reactStrictMode is enabled.; No secrets are hardcoded in these config files; client API base correctly relies on build-time NEXT_PUBLIC_API_URL with a loud console.error fallback warning rather than silently shipping a default (frontend/src/lib/api.ts:4-16).

### `infra:mobile` — working (4 находок)
_The Capacitor config defines a thin native shell (appId uz.yozuv.app) that loads the deployed Yozuv web app from CAP_SERVER_URL over HTTPS (cleartext:false), falling back to a local mobile-shell splash when no URL is baked in. The CI workflow bakes CAP_SERVER_URL via `cap sync` into a debug APK; Google OAuth is handled out-of-WebView via @capacitor/browser and returns through a yozuv:// deep link wired in AndroidManifest + CapacitorDeepLink.tsx. The end-to-end path is coherent and appears to work for the debug-APK use case. Verdict: working, with one misleading comment and a couple of hardening gaps (no release signing, legacy Cordova wildcard whitelist, allowBackup leaking tokens)._
- **[medium]** android:allowBackup=true exposes stored JWT tokens via ADB backup — `frontend/android/app/src/main/AndroidManifest.xml L5`
  - The application sets android:allowBackup="true" (Capacitor default).
