Because OAuth/login tokens are persisted in WebView localStorage (yozuv_access / yozuv_refresh, written in CapacitorDeepLink.tsx:43-44), an attacker with physical/ADB access (or Android auto-backup to the user's cloud on older devices) can extract the WebView data directory via `adb backup` and recover long-lived refresh tokens, enabling full account takeover. For an auth-bearing app this should be disabled. Fix: set android:allowBackup="false" (and/or add android:fullBackupContent / dataExtractionRules excluding the WebView storage) in AndroidManifest.xml.
- **[medium]** Legacy Cordova <access origin="*"/> wildcard whitelist + no Capacitor allowNavigation restriction — `frontend/android/app/src/main/res/xml/config.xml L3`
  - res/xml/config.xml ships the Cordova-era `<access origin="*" />` whitelist. While Capacitor (not Cordova) governs in-WebView navigation via server.allowNavigation, capacitor.config.ts sets no allowNavigation entries, so the WebView's navigation guard relies solely on the implicit single-host rule of server.url. Combined with the wildcard config.xml this is confusing and over-permissive: any unexpected top-level navigation (e.g. an injected/redirecting link) is not explicitly constrained to the trusted Yozuv host. Fix: remove/ignore the legacy config.xml wildcard and add an explicit `server.allowNavigation: ['<frontend-host>']` (plus the OAuth provider host only if the flow ever loads in-WebView) so navigation is locked to known origins.
- **[low]** Misleading comment: webContentsDebuggingEnabled does not control cookie/localStorage persistence — `frontend/capacitor.config.ts L24`
  - The comment above android.webContentsDebuggingEnabled:false claims it 'lets the WebView keep cookies/localStorage across launches so the saved login token survives app restarts.' That is incorrect — webContentsDebuggingEnabled only toggles Chrome remote (chrome://inspect) debugging of the WebView; it has nothing to do with storage persistence. The misleading comment could lead a future maintainer to flip the flag (enabling remote inspection of a production auth WebView) believing it affects login persistence. Fix: correct the comment to describe what the flag actually does (disabling it is correct for production to prevent WebView inspection); storage persistence is automatic for a remote server.url WebView.
- **[low]** OAuth deep-link handler does not validate token format before persisting — `frontend/src/components/CapacitorDeepLink.tsx L42`
  - The appUrlOpen handler accepts any yozuv:// URL with #access=...&refresh=... and writes both values verbatim into localStorage, then navigates to /dashboard. Custom-scheme intent-filters on Android are not exclusive — any app (or a malicious link/QR) can fire yozuv://auth/callback#access=...&refresh=... and inject attacker-chosen token strings into the app's storage (login-CSRF / token fixation). There is no signature, nonce/state check, or even a basic JWT-shape sanity check on the incoming values. Fix: validate the tokens (e.g. confirm three-segment JWT structure and verify against a state/nonce generated before Browser.open) before storing, and prefer App Links (https deep links with assetlinks.json) over an unverified custom scheme.
  - ✅ Работает: capacitor.config.ts correctly gates HTTPS: cleartext:false and only emits a server block when CAP_SERVER_URL is set, so a missing URL safely falls back to the local mobile-shell splash instead of a broken/insecure load.; webContentsDebuggingEnabled:false is the right production setting — it prevents remote Chrome inspection of the auth-bearing WebView (only the comment explaining it is wrong).; Google OAuth is correctly run outside the embedded WebView via @capacitor/browser and returned through a yozuv:// deep link, which is the required pattern since Google blocks OAuth inside embedded WebViews.; The AndroidManifest declares only INTERNET permission and a single-task MainActivity with a properly scoped yozuv:// VIEW intent-filter (BROWSABLE/DEFAULT) for the OAuth return, plus a non-exported FileProvider.; The CI workflow bakes CAP_SERVER_URL into the app at the correct step (`cap sync` before assembleDebug), uses JDK 17 + temurin matching Capacitor requirements, and fails the build (if-no-files-found: error) when the APK artifact is missing.; platform.ts gives a single, well-reasoned source of truth for telegram/native/browser detection with correct precedence (signed Telegram initData > Capacitor native > browser) and SSR guards (typeof window checks).

### `migrations:001-013` — working (3 находок)
_A clean linear Alembic chain (001 base schema → 013 client_blocks) for the booking SaaS. New non-nullable columns are consistently added with server_default values so backfill on populated tables is safe, FK/constraint creation order is correct, and the trickier migrations (011 nullable booking_id + partial unique indexes, 012 client dedup before adding the unique constraint) are thoughtfully written and handle the Postgres-vs-SQLite split. Verdict: correct and production-safe; only minor edge-case gaps, no data-loss or ordering bugs._
- **[low]** Migration 012 dedup repoints only bookings+reviews; relies on those being the only client references at rev 012 — `backend/alembic/versions/012_client_telegram_id_unique.py L56-69`
  - The client-dedup only UPDATEs bookings and reviews to the canonical client row before DELETEing duplicate clients. This is correct as of rev 012 because only bookings (001) and reviews (003) carry a client_id FK at that point, and both use ON DELETE SET NULL/CASCADE so no FK violation occurs even for a missed table. The risk is purely maintenance: a copy of this pattern, or a future table with a client_id FK using ON DELETE RESTRICT, would silently lose data or break. Fix: add an inline comment enumerating the client-referencing tables this dedup must keep in sync (bookings, reviews) so future FK additions trigger an update here.
- **[low]** Partial unique index uq_reviews_standalone_per_client is bypassed when client_id is NULL — `backend/alembic/versions/011_review_standalone.py L33-39`
  - The standalone-review uniqueness index on (business_id, client_id) WHERE booking_id IS NULL does not prevent duplicates when client_id is NULL, because Postgres treats NULLs as distinct in unique indexes. Since reviews.client_id uses ON DELETE SET NULL (003 line 51), once a client is deleted their standalone review keeps booking_id NULL and client_id NULL, and any number of NULL/NULL standalone rows can coexist for the same business. So the 'one standalone review per client' guarantee is best-effort, not hard. Fix: if a hard guarantee is needed, enforce non-null client_id for standalone reviews in application logic; otherwise document the limitation. No mandatory schema change.
- **[low]** platform_settings created without a singleton guard while the model assumes id=1 — `backend/alembic/versions/002_card_payment.py L38-45`
  - platform_settings is modeled as a singleton (model default id=1) but the table has a plain integer PK with no CHECK or single-row constraint, so an application bug inserting a second row would not be caught at the DB level. This is a robustness gap, not a migration error (the single-column Integer PK is fine; SQLAlchemy emits SERIAL autoincrement on Postgres). Fix: optionally add CHECK (id = 1) or a one-row partial unique index if the singleton invariant matters; otherwise rely on application code always reading/writing id=1.
  - ✅ Работает: All non-nullable columns added to existing tables (002 screenshot_url/user_comment/reviewed_by, 004 username, 006 viloyat/tuman, 009/010 JSONB and counter columns) include server_default values, so backfilling on a populated table cannot fail or violate NOT NULL.; Downgrades are present and mirror upgrades in correct reverse order, dropping indexes before tables (001 downgrade) and constraints/columns in proper sequence (011 recreates reviews_booking_id_key and restores NOT NULL).; Migration 011 correctly drops the Postgres auto-named column-level unique constraint 'reviews_booking_id_key' (matching the unnamed UniqueConstraint('booking_id') in 003), relaxes booking_id to nullable, and replaces it with two partial unique indexes — a clean transition to standalone reviews.; Migration 012 deduplicates clients in Python (canonical/remap maps ordered by telegram_id, created_at, id so the oldest row wins) before adding the unique constraint, avoiding a constraint-creation failure on existing duplicate data, and branches Postgres (add unique constraint) vs SQLite (unique index) since SQLite can't ALTER TABLE ADD CONSTRAINT.; FK ondelete semantics are deliberate and consistent: CASCADE for owned child rows (schedules, services, bookings via business), SET NULL for bookings.client_id/service_id and reviews.client_id so historical bookings survive client/service deletion.; Linear revision chain with no branches or gaps (001->013, each down_revision pointing to the prior), and JSONB columns (009/010) use proper jsonb server defaults via sa.text("'{}'::jsonb").

### `models:booking` — working (5 находок)
_These four ORM models (Booking, Schedule/HolidayDate, Service, WaitlistEntry) define the core appointment schema for the SaaS. They are well-structured: tz-aware UTC defaults on all DateTime columns, sensible FK ondelete policies (CASCADE for owned rows, SET NULL for soft references on Booking), helpful unique constraints on Schedule and WaitlistEntry, and str-based enums that serialize cleanly into String columns. The schema appears to work end-to-end and is consistent with the booking service and migrations. The main real risks are time-of-day columns (start_time/end_time stored as naive Time with no date component) which break overlap math for any booking whose duration crosses midnight, plus a couple of integrity/validation gaps that are enabled by the model design._
- **[high]** Booking.end_time as bare Time breaks overlap detection for midnight-crossing bookings — `backend/app/models/booking.py L45-46`
  - start_time and end_time are stored as Time (no date). The service computes end_dt = start_dt + timedelta(minutes=duration) and persists end_dt.time() (booking_service.py:184-185, 208). For a booking starting 23:30 with a 60-min service, end_time wraps to 00:30. The conflict query (booking_service.py:118-119) then evaluates Booking.start_time < end_time AND Booking.end_time > start_time as 23:30 < 00:30 (FALSE), so the overlap predicate silently fails and a real conflict is not detected, allowing double-booking. The stored end_time < start_time also makes the row's own duration nonsensical for any consumer that subtracts the two. Fix: either forbid bookings whose computed end crosses midnight (validate in create_booking), or store start/end as full DateTime(timezone=True) and do interval math on timestamps rather than wall-clock Time.
- **[medium]** Conflict check filtered by staff_id misses NULL-staff (shared-calendar) bookings — `backend/app/models/booking.py L41-43`
  - staff_id is nullable to let single-resource (NULL) and multi-staff bookings coexist. But the conflict query only adds the staff filter when staff_id is set (booking_service.py:122-123). A staffed booking therefore never conflicts with an existing NULL-staff booking at the same time, and vice-versa is only one-directional. In a business that has legacy/shared NULL bookings AND has onboarded staff, a staff booking can be placed on top of a shared-calendar booking for the same physical resource. Fix: when staff_id is set, also treat NULL-staff bookings as conflicting (q.filter(or_(Booking.staff_id == staff_id, Booking.staff_id.is_(None)))), or migrate all bookings to an explicit resource model so NULL no longer means 'everyone'.
- **[low]** No DB/model validation that end_time > start_time or break_end > break_start — `backend/app/models/schedule.py L20-23`
  - Schedule.start_time/end_time and break_start/break_end have no CHECK constraint or model-level guard ensuring end > start, or that break_start/break_end are both set/unset together and fall within working hours. An inverted or half-populated schedule (e.g. break_start set, break_end NULL) will be accepted and can produce empty/negative working windows in slot generation. Same applies to Booking start/end. Fix: add CHECK constraints (end_time > start_time; (break_start IS NULL) = (break_end IS NULL); break window inside working window) or validate in the schema/service layer.
- **[low]** Booking.payment_amount Integer with no non-negative constraint; loyalty 100%-off relies on it being 0 — `backend/app/models/booking.py L52`
  - payment_amount (and Service.price / price_max / loyalty_after_visits) are plain Integer with default 0 and no CHECK (>= 0). The loyalty feature sets final_price (stored into payment_amount) and price comparisons assume non-negative money. Nothing at the model/DB level prevents a negative price or negative payment_amount from a bad caller, which would corrupt revenue analytics and any refund math. Fix: add CHECK (payment_amount >= 0), CHECK (price >= 0), CHECK (price_max IS NULL OR price_max >= price), CHECK (loyalty_after_visits >= 0).
- **[low]** Booking.status / payment_status stored as String(32) with no enum/DB constraint — `backend/app/models/booking.py L47-51`
  - status and payment_status are typed as Mapped[BookingStatus]/[PaymentStatus] but the column is String(32) with a Python default, not a SQLAlchemy Enum or a CHECK constraint. Because the enums subclass str the happy path works, but the DB will accept any arbitrary 32-char string written by raw SQL, a migration, or a future code path, and SQLAlchemy will hand that raw string back where code does Booking.status in [BookingStatus...] (comparison silently false). Fix: either use a real Enum/CHECK constraint, or keep String but normalize on write and rely on app-layer validation consistently. Low severity since current code paths only write valid values.
  - ✅ Работает: All DateTime columns use DateTime(timezone=True) with a tz-aware _utcnow default (datetime.now(timezone.utc)); the docstring on booking.py:12-19 correctly explains why naive utcnow is avoided, preventing offset-naive/aware comparison errors.; FK ondelete policies are deliberate and correct: business_id CASCADE (owned rows die with the business), while service_id/client_id/staff_id on Booking are SET NULL so historical bookings survive deletion of a service/client/staff.; WaitlistEntry has a well-chosen UniqueConstraint on (business_id, service_id, date, start_time, client_id) making re-tapping 'notify me' idempotent at the DB level, and notified_at is kept (not deleted) so turn-tracking survives.; Schedule has UniqueConstraint(business_id, day_of_week) preventing duplicate day rows; day_of_week convention (0=Mon..6=Sun) is documented.; reminder_sent_at / notified_at dedup columns are nullable and correctly designed to make minute-level Celery beat reminders idempotent.; recurrence_id is nullable + indexed, a clean way to group a recurring series without a separate table, and indexes on business_id/service_id/client_id/staff_id/date match the actual filter columns used by the booking service queries.

### `models:misc` — working (2 находок)
_Five small SQLAlchemy 2.0 declarative models: an admin audit log, a multi-provider auth-identity table, a broadcast-message log, a business photo gallery, and a per-business client block list. Schemas, FKs, cascades and uniqueness constraints are well-formed and match their Alembic migrations; the JSONB-with-SQLite-variant pattern is used correctly. Verdict: working. No data-integrity or correctness defects found in the model layer itself — the only issues are minor model/migration nullability drift and a redundant index, neither of which threatens integrity._
- **[low]** ORM nullability drifts from migration in admin_audit_log/broadcast_message — `backend/app/models/admin_audit_log.py L23-30`
  - In the ORM model admin_name, action's siblings target_type, target_id and created_at omit nullable=False, while migration 009 declares all of them NOT NULL with server_default. action is nullable=False in the model but target_type/target_id/created_at/admin_name are not. The DB still enforces NOT NULL, and Python-side default=/_utcnow always supplies a value, so inserts succeed; but the model is an inaccurate description of the table (e.g. a future autogenerate diff or a test on an SQLite schema built from metadata would allow NULLs the real Postgres table forbids). Same pattern in broadcast_message.py created_at (line 29-31): model lacks nullable=False but is functionally fine via default. Fix: add nullable=False to created_at, admin_name, target_type, target_id in the models to match the migrations.
- **[low]** Redundant standalone index on auth_identities.user_id — `backend/app/models/auth_identity.py L39-42`
  - UniqueConstraint("user_id","provider") already creates a btree whose leading column is user_id, which serves any user_id-prefix lookup (e.g. loading a user's identities). The extra Index("ix_auth_identities_user","user_id") in __table_args__ is therefore redundant — it only adds write/storage overhead with no query benefit. Fix: drop the standalone index and rely on the composite unique constraint (would require a follow-up migration).
  - ✅ Работает: AuthIdentity correctly encodes the documented invariants with two UNIQUE constraints: UNIQUE(provider, subject) prevents one external account mapping to two Yozuv accounts, and UNIQUE(user_id, provider) caps one identity per provider per account.; All FKs (auth_identities.user_id, business_photos.business_id, client_blocks.business_id, client_blocks.client_id) use ondelete=CASCADE, so deleting a user/business/client cleanly removes dependent rows; User.identities relationship adds ORM-side cascade='all, delete-orphan' that matches the DB cascade.; ClientBlock UNIQUE(business_id, client_id) correctly enforces the per-business (not platform-wide) block semantics described in the docstring, and booking_service.py queries exactly that pair, so the constraint and the read path agree.; JSONB().with_variant(JSON(), 'sqlite') is the right portability pattern for running the Postgres JSONB columns under the SQLite test DB; payload/filters/failed_recipients use server-side and client-side defaults consistently with migration 009/broadcast migration.; created_at uses timezone-aware datetime.now(timezone.utc) via _utcnow and DateTime(timezone=True), avoiding naive-UTC timezone bugs.; admin_audit_log indexes (admin_telegram_id, action, target_type, created_at) line up with the actual filter/order_by in admin.py's audit-log query, so the read path is index-backed.

### `models:payment` — working (5 находок)
_Three ORM models back billing: PaymentTransaction (one row per Payme/Click/Card payment attempt), Subscription (active billing window per business), and PromoCode (business-scoped discount codes). Money is stored as integer UZS amounts (no cents/tiyin), statuses use String-backed str-enums, and the promo code carries a (business_id, code) unique constraint. The area appears to function end-to-end: payment creation, admin approval, subscription activation (with row-level locking against webhook-retry races), and promo application (with SELECT FOR UPDATE) are all wired up and consistent. The defects below are integrity/robustness gaps rather than outright breakage._
- **[medium]** Promo uses_count never decremented on booking cancellation — `backend/app/services/booking_service.py L254 / 387`
  - _create_booking increments promo.uses_count by 1 (line 254) when a promo is applied, but cancel_booking (line 387) only flips status to CANCELLED and never decrements uses_count. For a limited promo (max_uses > 0), every cancelled booking permanently burns a use, so a promo can hit its cap and stop working even though no completed booking ever used it. Fix: when cancelling a booking that carried a promo, decrement uses_count (requires persisting which promo a booking used, e.g. a booking.promo_code_id FK), or only increment uses_count at booking completion rather than creation.
- **[medium]** PaymentTransaction.external_id is non-unique → no webhook idempotency at the data layer — `backend/app/models/payment.py L26`
  - external_id is a plain indexed String defaulting to '' (index unique=False per alembic 001_initial.py:100). The provider's transaction id is the natural idempotency key for webhook delivery, but nothing enforces one PaymentTransaction per (provider, external_id). Idempotency currently relies only on tx.id + a status==COMPLETED short-circuit in payment_service. If a provider retries a webhook before status reaches COMPLETED, or two webhooks for the same external payment arrive concurrently, a second row/activation can slip through. Fix: add a partial unique constraint on (provider, external_id) WHERE external_id <> '' and look transactions up by it in the webhook path. The default='' also pollutes the index with many empty-string rows.
- **[low]** Multiple ACTIVE subscriptions possible — no DB guard for single active row — `backend/app/models/subscription.py L20-24`
  - activate_subscription expires the prior ACTIVE sub and inserts a new one under a business row lock, which works for the normal path, but there is no DB-level guarantee (e.g. partial unique index on business_id WHERE status='ACTIVE') that a business has at most one ACTIVE subscription. Any code path that inserts a Subscription without going through activate_subscription, or a missed lock, can leave two ACTIVE rows; downstream 'is this business subscribed' checks that don't order by expires_at could then read the wrong one. Fix: add a unique partial index on (business_id) WHERE status = 'ACTIVE'.
- **[low]** Status/plan/provider columns are str-enum typed in Python but plain String in DB with no constraint — `backend/app/models/payment.py L25-31`
  - provider, status (payment.py) and plan/status (subscription.py) are declared Mapped[Enum] but mapped to bare String columns with no native enum, CHECK constraint, or TypeDecorator. Binding works because these are str subclasses, but values read back are plain str, not enum members, and the DB will accept ANY string — a typo or a code path writing a raw string (e.g. tx.plan stores plan.value directly at payment_service.py:67) cannot be caught. The asymmetry (status stores the enum member, plan stores .value) is also fragile. Fix: use SQLAlchemy Enum(..., native_enum=False) with a length, or a TypeDecorator, so the column round-trips to the enum and rejects invalid values.
- **[low]** No constraint that subscription expires_at > starts_at, and amount columns allow negatives — `backend/app/models/subscription.py L23-25`
  - Subscription has starts_at/expires_at with no CHECK that expires_at > starts_at, and amount_paid (subscription) / amount (payment) / discount_amount, discount_percent, max_uses, uses_count (promo) are plain Integers with no non-negative or 0..100 CHECK constraints at the DB level. Range validation for promos exists only in the Pydantic layer (promo.py PromoCreate, le=100), so a direct write or future endpoint could persist a 200% discount or negative amount, and _apply_promo would then compute a negative/over-large discount (max(0, ...) caps the floor but a >100% percent still over-discounts before the cap on the amount component). Fix: add CHECK constraints (discount_percent BETWEEN 0 AND 100, amounts >= 0, uses_count <= max_uses when max_uses>0, expires_at > starts_at).
  - ✅ Работает: Money is stored consistently as integer UZS across all three models and the service layer (MONTHLY_AMOUNT_UZS/YEARLY_AMOUNT_UZS), avoiding float rounding bugs; promo discount math uses integer floor division and clamps with max(0, ...) so the final price can never go negative.; PromoCode has a correct (business_id, code) unique constraint (uq_promo_biz_code) and codes are normalized to upper() on both create and lookup, so the uniqueness and matching are consistent and tenant-scoped.; Promo application (_apply_promo) uses SELECT ... FOR UPDATE on the promo row before checking max_uses and incrementing, correctly serializing concurrent redemptions against the usage cap.; Subscription activation locks the business row and the prior ACTIVE subscription with with_for_update() to serialize webhook-retry races before expiring the old sub and inserting the new one.; All timestamp columns use DateTime(timezone=True) and timezone-aware datetime.now(timezone.utc) defaults, so stored billing timestamps are tz-correct.; All three tables FK to businesses.id with ondelete=CASCADE and index business_id, giving clean tenant isolation and cleanup.

### `models:settings+enums` — working (0 находок)
_Three small, declarative model/enum modules: platform_settings.py (a singleton row holding platform-wide card/payment info), enums.py (all string-valued domain enums for categories, statuses, roles, providers), and review.py (client reviews of a business, optionally tied to a booking). All three are clean, internally consistent, and correctly integrated with their callers. Rating bounds, review uniqueness, and settings singleton behavior are enforced at the layers that own them (Pydantic in routers, input checks in the bot, partial unique indexes in migration 011). I found no real defects within these three files._
  - ✅ Работает: platform_settings.py: tz-aware UTC default/onupdate via _utcnow() with DateTime(timezone=True) is correct and avoids the naive/aware mixing bug; updated_at will be set on both insert and update.; platform_settings.py: singleton pattern (PK default=1) is matched by the only writer, payments.py:_get_or_create_platform_settings, which always filters/creates id==1, so the table stays a true singleton; column lengths (32/128/Text) align with the router's Pydantic max_length validators (32/128/2000).; enums.py: every enum subclasses (str, enum.Enum), so members serialize to their string .value when persisted into the String columns that back them (business.py, payment.py) and JSON-encode cleanly in responses; values are unique within each enum.; enums.py: enum value casing is self-consistent per enum and matches how each is used — e.g. AuthProvider/BusinessCategory use lowercase values (documented as stored lowercase), while status/role enums use uppercase; no duplicate or shadowed values.; review.py: created_at uses the same tz-aware _utcnow() default against DateTime(timezone=True), matching the in-code comment and avoiding timezone comparison bugs.; review.py: FK ondelete semantics are sensible — business_id/booking_id CASCADE (review is meaningless without its parent), client_id SET NULL with a nullable column (review survives client deletion). booking_id correctly nullable to support standalone reviews.

### `router:admin` — working (5 находок)
_Admin-only management router (summary stats, business CRUD, subscription extend/patch, broadcasts with retry, full DB backup export/import, audit log, payments list). Every endpoint is gated behind get_admin_user (telegram-id allowlist) and the logic is generally sound with consistent audit logging, input validation via Pydantic, and limit clamping. It appears to work end-to-end, but there are several real defects: a broadcast duplicate-send bug, an unreliable owner-already-has-business check, event-loop-blocking sync DB calls inside async endpoints (notably the destructive backup import), and a minor MRR rounding bias._
- **[high]** Broadcast can send duplicate messages and inflate counts when filtering by plan/status — `backend/app/routers/admin.py L621-639`
  - _select_broadcast_recipients joins Subscription (q.join(Subscription, Subscription.business_id == Business.id)) without any DISTINCT or one-per-business reduction. A business with multiple subscription rows (renewals, expired+active, history) produces multiple (Business, User) tuples. _send_broadcast_to then iterates rows and sends one Telegram message per row, so the owner receives the broadcast N times, and sent/total counts (returned to the admin and stored in BroadcastMessage) are inflated by the duplication. Fix: select distinct businesses, e.g. apply .distinct() on Business.id (or collect a unique set of owner telegram_ids) before fanning out, or use a subquery/EXISTS for the subscription filter instead of a join.
- **[medium]** create_business 'owner already has a business' check is unreliable (scalar relationship over a one-to-many situation) — `backend/app/routers/admin.py L297-298`
  - The guard uses owner.business (User.business is mapped uselist=False, back_populates='business' on Business.owner_id). But a user can in fact own several Business rows over time: delete_business only soft-deletes (sets deleted_at) and create_business then permits making a new one, so owner_id is not unique. With multiple owned rows the scalar relationship returns an arbitrary single Business, so 'owner.business.deleted_at is None' may inspect the wrong row — the guard can both incorrectly reject and incorrectly allow. Fix: query explicitly for an existing non-deleted business owned by that user: db.query(Business).filter(Business.owner_id==owner.id, Business.deleted_at.is_(None)).first().
- **[medium]** Destructive backup import runs blocking sync DB work on the event loop — `backend/app/routers/admin.py L836-944`
  - backup_import is `async def` but uses the synchronous Session (get_db -> sync create_engine/sessionmaker). The snapshot read (select every table, lines 889-896), the full delete loop (lines 907-908), and the bulk inserts (lines 911-917) all execute synchronously inside the coroutine, blocking the single FastAPI event-loop thread for the entire restore — potentially many seconds on a real dataset — during which the whole backend (all other requests) is frozen. The same pattern affects broadcast/retry_broadcast DB calls, but those are short; the import is the dangerous one because it is long and holds the loop. Fix: run the sync DB section in a threadpool (await run_in_threadpool(...)) or make the endpoint a normal `def` so Starlette runs it in a worker thread.
- **[low]** MRR for yearly plans truncates instead of rounding (downward money bias) — `backend/app/routers/admin.py L110`
  - mrr += int((s.amount_paid or 0) / 12) floor-truncates the monthly-equivalent of a yearly subscription, biasing reported MRR downward by up to ~11 UZS per yearly sub. Minor for a dashboard metric but it is a money/rounding inaccuracy. Fix: use round((s.amount_paid or 0)/12) or integer division with explicit intent; document the rounding.
- **[low]** Backup import reads entire upload into memory before size check — `backend/app/routers/admin.py L858-860`
  - contents = await file.read() loads the whole multipart body into memory first, then checks len(contents) > MAX_BACKUP_BYTES. A malicious/over-large upload (admin token required, so low exposure) is fully buffered before rejection, and the 50MB cap is not actually enforced against memory pressure. Fix: stream-read in chunks and abort once the cap is exceeded, or rely on an upstream body-size limit.
  - ✅ Работает: Every endpoint is consistently protected by Depends(get_admin_user), which enforces a telegram-id allowlist and returns 403 for non-admins; no endpoint is left unauthenticated.; Pydantic bodies validate input well: slug pattern/length, days range (ge=1,le=365), text length (max 4000), owner_telegram_id gt=0; category/plan/status are validated against enums with helpful 400 messages.; List endpoints clamp limit with min(max(1,limit),N), preventing unbounded result sets.; list_businesses and list_payments avoid N+1 by batch-loading owners/subscriptions/businesses with IN queries and dict lookups.; Backup import is well-guarded: requires the exact confirm phrase, validates version and rejects unknown tables, writes a best-effort pre-wipe snapshot, deletes in reversed FK-sorted order and inserts in forward order, and wraps the wipe/reload in try/except with db.rollback() on failure.; Audit logging is applied on every mutating action and is best-effort (never breaks the primary write).

### `router:analytics` — working (5 находок)
_A read-only analytics router (prefix /business/me/analytics) exposing summary, revenue, bookings-by-day, popular-services, top-revenue-services, heatmap, retention and funnel endpoints. Every endpoint is scoped to the caller's owned business via get_owned_business and filters by business_id, so there is no cross-tenant data leak. It uses the project's sync Session consistently (no async/await misuse). It works end-to-end, but several endpoints have correctness inconsistencies (which statuses count toward revenue/clients/popularity) and two endpoints issue one SQL query per day (N+1)._
- **[medium]** Revenue counts unpaid bookings (money correctness) — `backend/app/routers/analytics.py L48-58, 86-95, 155-173`
  - summary.revenue, revenue_chart and top_revenue_services sum Booking.payment_amount filtered only by status != CANCELLED. They never check payment_status. So a PENDING/CONFIRMED/NO_SHOW booking that has a payment_amount set but is UNPAID (or REFUNDED) is reported as earned revenue. A NO_SHOW with a recorded price especially inflates the owner's revenue number. Fix: decide the revenue definition explicitly — either filter status == COMPLETED (and/or payment_status == PAID), or exclude NO_SHOW and REFUNDED — and apply the same filter across all three revenue endpoints so they agree.
- **[medium]** Inconsistent status filtering across metrics (clients_count and popular_services include cancelled) — `backend/app/routers/analytics.py L59-68, 130-138`
  - summary.clients_count (lines 59-68) omits the status != CANCELLED filter that bookings_count and revenue use, so a client who only ever made a cancelled booking is counted as a client; the three summary numbers are computed over different row sets and won't reconcile. Likewise popular_services (lines 130-138) has no status filter at all, so cancelled bookings inflate 'popular' service counts, unlike every other endpoint which excludes CANCELLED. Fix: add Booking.status != BookingStatus.CANCELLED to both queries for consistency.
- **[low]** N+1: one SQL query per day in revenue_chart and bookings_by_day — `backend/app/routers/analytics.py L84-97, 108-121`
  - Both endpoints loop over the day range and run a separate aggregate query per day — up to 400 queries for /revenue?days=400 and 365 for /bookings-by-day?days=365. Fix: run a single grouped query (db.query(Booking.date, func.sum/count).filter(business_id, date between start and today, status != CANCELLED).group_by(Booking.date)), load results into a dict keyed by date, then fill the per-day output list (zero-filling missing days) in Python.
- **[low]** popular_services limit has no lower bound (LIMIT 0 / negative) — `backend/app/routers/analytics.py L128`
  - limit: int = Query(10, le=50) is missing ge, so a client can pass limit=0 (returns nothing) or a negative value. In Postgres LIMIT with a negative value is rejected (raises), and LIMIT 0 silently returns an empty list. Other endpoints (top_revenue_services line 147) correctly use ge=1. Fix: add ge=1 to the popular_services limit Query.
- **[low]** Period windows are off-by-one / overlapping (today included on both ends) — `backend/app/routers/analytics.py L16-26, 35-42`
  - _period_start('week') returns today-7 and the filters use date >= start_d AND date <= today, which is 8 calendar days, not 7 (month=31, year=366). top_revenue_services and funnel have the same inclusive-both-ends pattern (days+1 days of data). This is minor and may be intentional, but the labels ('week','7 days') don't match the actual window. Fix: use start_d = today - timedelta(days=period_len-1) (or document the window as inclusive) so the count of days matches the label.
  - ✅ Работает: Ownership scoping is solid: every query filters Booking.business_id == business.id, and get_owned_business enforces owner_id == user.id, so no cross-business leakage; Sync DB usage is consistent — all endpoints take Session = Depends(get_db) and use db.query(...).scalar()/.all(); no mixing of sync/async that would break the event loop; period and days/limit params are validated with Query patterns/bounds (e.g. pattern='^(today|week|month|year)$', ge/le ranges) preventing most malformed input; Timezone handling is correct: local_today() (Asia/Tashkent) is used everywhere instead of naive date.today(), matching how booking dates are stored; funnel status-key matching is correct because BookingStatus is persisted as a plain String(32) (no SQLEnum), so str(status) yields 'PENDING' etc., not 'BookingStatus.PENDING'; heatmap correctly guards against NULL date/start_time rows before indexing the grid, and date.weekday() (0=Mon) matches the documented Monday-first convention

### `router:auth` — working (3 находок)
_backend/app/routers/auth.py implements Telegram WebApp login, Google OAuth (login + link modes via signed PKCE cookie), username/phone+password login, set-password, refresh, identity listing/unlinking, and /me. It is sync SQLAlchemy with sync endpoints (no async/await misuse). Core flows are sound: CSRF state check, PKCE, email_verified gating, account-takeover guards in link mode, constant-time-ish password verify, and a lockout guard on Google unlink. A few edge-case defects exist around token-in-URL logging and unhandled username-uniqueness IntegrityErrors._
- **[high]** Access token passed in URL query string leaks into logs (/google/start?token=) — `backend/app/routers/auth.py L100-119`
  - google_start accepts a full JWT access token as the `token` query parameter for link mode. Query strings are routinely written to access/proxy logs (Render, nginx, CDN, browser history, Referer header on the subsequent 302 to Google). A leaked access token grants full account access for its lifetime. The code comment acknowledges 'the token rides the query' but does not mitigate the logging exposure. Fix: accept the token via a POST body or short-lived one-time link-nonce instead of GET query, or at minimum issue a dedicated narrowly-scoped, single-use link token (type='link', short exp) rather than a general access token, and ensure web server access-log query stripping for this path.
- **[medium]** Unhandled IntegrityError on username uniqueness in auth_telegram (create and update) — `backend/app/routers/auth.py L68-84`
  - User has a unique index on lower(username) where username<>''. In auth_telegram both the create branch (username=username) and update branch (user.username = username or user.username) write the incoming Telegram @handle without catching collisions. A password/Google account could have previously claimed that login string as its username via /set-password; if a Telegram user then logs in with the same (now matching) handle, db.commit() raises IntegrityError -> unhandled 500 and the Telegram login fails entirely. Fix: wrap the commit in try/except IntegrityError (rollback) and either skip the username update on clash or resolve it deterministically, mirroring the clash check already done in set_password.
- **[low]** Telegram identity stored only in legacy User column, not auth_identities — `backend/app/routers/auth.py L68-84`
  - Google login creates an AuthIdentity row, but Telegram login writes only User.telegram_id and never creates an AuthIdentity(provider='telegram'). list_identities compensates by reading User.telegram_id directly, so it works, but the auth_identities table is not the single source of truth it is documented to be, and the UNIQUE(provider,subject) protection that prevents one external account mapping to two Yozuv accounts is not enforced for Telegram. Low impact today (telegram_id is itself unique on users) but a latent inconsistency. Fix: also upsert a telegram AuthIdentity, or document that telegram intentionally stays on the legacy column.
  - ✅ Работает: Google OAuth callback verifies CSRF state from the signed cookie against the returned state and validates the JWT cookie type before trusting it (lines 167-177).; Refuses to create/login accounts on unverified Google emails (email_verified check, line 186) — anti-takeover.; Link mode guards against silently moving a Google identity already bound to a different account (identity.user_id != link_user_id -> google_taken, lines 207-215).; disconnect_google refuses to unlink if it would leave the account with no remaining login method (lines 405-412).; Password login runs verify_password even on user-miss to keep timing roughly constant, and uses a generic error message that does not reveal whether the login or the password was wrong (lines 301-306).; set_password checks for username/phone clashes against other accounts (case-insensitive) before claiming a login, returning 409 instead of risking ambiguous login resolution (lines 330-342).

### `router:bookings` — working (4 находок)
_This router handles the full booking lifecycle: public Telegram-WebApp booking creation, owner dashboard create/list/edit/confirm/complete/cancel, recurring series, waitlist join/list, and public slot lookup. It is consistently synchronous SQLAlchemy (matching get_db's sync Session and the sync booking_service), so the "async stack" description does not apply here and there is no async/await misuse. Authz is solid via get_owned_business on owner routes and verified Telegram initData on public routes; ownership scoping is applied throughout. The main defects are concurrency-correctness gaps in the recurring path and a staff-scoping inconsistency in the edit path._
- **[high]** create_recurring has no advisory lock and no SELECT FOR UPDATE — double-booking race — `backend/app/routers/bookings.py L572-586`
  - Unlike create_owner_booking (line 167 acquire_slot_lock + line 181 with_for_update) and update_booking (line 286/298), the recurring loop does its conflict check with a plain conflict_q.first() (line 586) and never calls acquire_slot_lock. The module's own docstring (acquire_slot_lock, booking_service.py:35) explains that SELECT FOR UPDATE cannot lock an empty slot, so two concurrent requests targeting the same destination slot (e.g. a recurring create racing a single owner-create, or two recurring creates) both pass the conflict check and both insert, producing overlapping bookings. Fix: call acquire_slot_lock(db, business.id, slot_date, body.start_time) before each iteration's conflict query and add .with_for_update() to conflict_q, mirroring create_owner_booking.
- **[medium]** update_booking conflict check ignores staff_id — wrong overlap semantics for multi-staff businesses — `backend/app/routers/bookings.py L288-300`
  - create_owner_booking and create_recurring filter the conflict query by Booking.staff_id when staff_id is set (lines 179-181, 584-585), implementing per-staff overlap (different masters can run parallel sessions). update_booking never reads or filters on staff_id, so its conflict query is always per-business. Consequence for a multi-staff business: editing booking A onto a slot already held by a DIFFERENT staff member is falsely rejected with 'Vaqt band' (line 302), even though that slot is free for A's staff. It also never reschedules/validates against the booking's own staff. Fix: load booking.staff_id (and any body override) and add a .filter(Booking.staff_id == staff_id) branch identical to the create path.
- **[low]** complete allows marking a PENDING (or already CANCELLED-adjacent) booking COMPLETED — `backend/app/routers/bookings.py L345-347`
  - The /complete endpoint only guards against CANCELLED (line 345) and then unconditionally sets status=COMPLETED. A booking that was never confirmed (PENDING) can be jumped straight to COMPLETED, skipping the confirm step the comment at lines 335-337 says complete is meant to follow. This can corrupt funnel/reporting metrics that assume COMPLETED implies prior CONFIRMED. Fix: require b.status == BookingStatus.CONFIRMED (or at minimid disallow PENDING) before completing.
- **[low]** create_public_booking dereferences business after reload without null-checking it for publish_event — `backend/app/routers/bookings.py L74-113`
  - After commit the booking is reloaded (line 74). The owner-notification block guards with `if business and ... and client` (line 84), but publish_event(business.id, 'booking_new') at line 113 is unconditional. If the reload query returned None (e.g. the row was deleted/rolled back by a concurrent process between commit and reload) or booking.business is None, line 81/113 raises AttributeError and the client gets a 500 even though the booking was already committed. Fix: guard the reload result and business before line 113, or skip publish/return a minimal response when reload fails.
  - ✅ Работает: Public booking creation correctly ignores client-supplied client_telegram_id and overwrites it from verified Telegram initData (lines 51-65), preventing identity spoofing.; All owner routes depend on get_owned_business and every owner query filters by business.id (e.g. lines 247, 340, 474, 636), so cross-tenant access is properly scoped.; create_owner_booking and update_booking take the advisory slot lock before the conflict check and use with_for_update (lines 167/181, 286/298), correctly serializing concurrent writes to an empty slot.; waitlist_join verifies the service belongs to the requested business before inserting (lines 428-438), blocking entries against a stranger's calendar.; list_bookings caps limit via Query(50, le=200) (line 222) and uses joinedload for service/client (line 226) to avoid N+1.; Recurring strict mode rolls back already-created bookings on first conflict (lines 588-595) so a partial series isn't left behind.

### `router:business` — working (5 находок)
_backend/app/routers/business.py implements the owner-facing business CRUD/dashboard plus the public catalog and per-slug public pages. Ownership scoping is consistent (owner endpoints all resolve the business via get_owned_business/owner_id, public endpoints filter is_active), the update schema is a strict allowlist that deliberately blocks privilege escalation, and timezone handling for "today" is correct. It appears to work end-to-end. The notable issues are non-correctness: a DB-connection-pool exhaustion risk on the long-lived SSE stream and an unbounded in-memory catalog query/pagination that will not scale and mis-paginates filtered/sorted results._
- **[high]** SSE stream pins a DB connection for the entire connection lifetime (pool exhaustion) — `backend/app/routers/business.py L381-425`
  - notifications_stream depends on get_owned_business_download, which Depends(get_db). FastAPI keeps the get_db generator (and thus the checked-out SQLAlchemy Session/connection) open until the StreamingResponse finishes. An SSE connection stays open for hours, so each open dashboard tab holds one connection from the pool (pool_size=20, max_overflow=10) even though the stream body never touches the DB again after auth. A few dozen concurrent dashboards exhaust the pool and block all other requests. Fix: resolve auth/business in a short-lived session that is closed before the stream starts (e.g. open a SessionLocal() inside the dependency, fetch the business, close it, and pass only the business id/object out), or make notifications_stream not depend on a request-scoped get_db at all — capture business.id and release the session before yielding.
- **[medium]** Catalog loads all active businesses into memory and paginates after filtering/sorting — `backend/app/routers/business.py L456-532`
  - catalog() runs query...order_by(name).all() with no SQL LIMIT/OFFSET, pulling every active business, then computes review stats, applies min_rating, sorts in Python, and finally slices enriched[offset:offset+limit]. This is O(all businesses) per request in both DB rows and memory and degrades linearly as the directory grows. It also means offset/limit cannot be pushed to the DB because min_rating/distance filtering happens in Python. Fix: push category/q/viloyat/tuman + pagination to SQL, join review aggregates (or a cached rating column) in the query, and only fall back to in-memory work for distance sort; bound the result set.
- **[low]** Owner endpoints don't exclude deactivated/soft-deleted businesses — `backend/app/routers/business.py L104-439`
  - get_owned_business (deps.py:29) filters only on owner_id, not deleted_at.is_(None) / is_active. After an admin soft-deletes/deactivates a business (admin.py:411-412 sets deleted_at and is_active=False), its owner can still call /business/me, /me/dashboard, /me/notifications, the SSE stream, and PUT /business/me and continue operating on the deactivated record. Whether that is intended is ambiguous, but a blocked business should generally be read-only or 404 for its owner too. Fix: decide the policy and, if deactivated businesses should be inaccessible, add `Business.deleted_at.is_(None)` (and optionally is_active) to get_owned_business / get_owned_business_download, or branch behavior for deactivated state.
- **[low]** latitude/longitude accept any float; out-of-range coords feed haversine — `backend/app/routers/business.py L58-59`
  - BusinessCreate/BusinessUpdate (schemas/business.py:32-33,49-50) and the catalog lat/lng query params have no -90..90 / -180..180 bounds. Bad coordinates are stored and later fed into _haversine in catalog (line 484-491); radians/sin/cos won't crash but produce meaningless distance_km, corrupting distance sort. Fix: add Field(ge=-90, le=90) for latitude and Field(ge=-180, le=180) for longitude in the schemas and on the catalog lat/lng Query params.
- **[low]** create_business slug pre-check races with unique constraint and ignores soft-deleted slugs — `backend/app/routers/business.py L40-42`
  - The slug uniqueness pre-check (db.query(Business).filter(slug==body.slug).first()) is a TOCTOU: two concurrent creates pass the check, then db.commit() raises IntegrityError on uq_businesses_slug, surfacing as an uncaught 500 instead of a clean 400. Additionally the unique constraint is global (no partial index excluding deleted_at), so a soft-deleted business permanently reserves its slug, making the 400 'Slug already taken' message correct but the slug unreusable. Fix: catch IntegrityError around the commit and translate to 400; if slug reuse after deletion is desired, switch to a partial unique index on slug WHERE deleted_at IS NULL.
  - ✅ Работает: BusinessUpdate is a strict field allowlist that deliberately omits is_active/slug/owner_id, with an explicit comment, so the setattr-based mass update in update_business cannot be used for privilege escalation (re-activating a blocked owner).; Dashboard date logic uses local_today() (Asia/Tashkent) instead of naive UTC, avoiding the day-boundary drift the clock module warns about.; Public endpoints (/{slug}, /{slug}/services, catalog) all filter Business.is_active.is_(True), and soft-delete sets is_active=False (admin.py:412), so soft-deleted businesses don't leak to public views or their menus.; The SSE event bus is scoped per business_id, so one owner's stream cannot receive another business's change events; publish is fire-and-forget and never breaks the booking write.; Aggregate dashboard queries use func.coalesce/func.count with `or 0` guards and int() casts, so empty result sets return 0 rather than None.; Notifications batch-loads clients via a single Client.id.in_(client_ids) query keyed into a dict, avoiding an N+1 over recent bookings.

### `router:files` — working (4 находок)
_This router handles business asset files: QR PNG, brochure PDF, logo upload/delete, and a photo gallery (list/upload/delete), plus public file-serving and a public per-slug gallery endpoint. Logic, ownership scoping, MIME/size validation, and path-traversal guards are largely correct and the endpoints work end-to-end. The main real issues are operational (uploads written to ephemeral /tmp on Render disappear on restart) and architectural (async endpoints doing blocking file/DB I/O on the event loop), plus a minor ordering-collision bug on gallery re-uploads._
- **[high]** Uploaded logos/photos stored on ephemeral filesystem (data loss on restart) — `backend/app/routers/files.py L34-37, 52-55, 130, 233`
  - _logos_dir()/_photos_dir() write under settings.uploads_dir, which defaults to /tmp/yozuv_uploads (backend/app/config.py:58). On Render the container filesystem is ephemeral, so every deploy/restart wipes all uploaded logos and gallery photos while the DB rows (Business.logo_url, business_photos) still point at /api/business/logos/... and /api/business/photos/.... get_logo/get_photo then return 404 for every previously uploaded image, and the bot/landing gallery silently breaks. Fix: persist blobs durably (object storage like S3/R2, or store bytes in Postgres as was done elsewhere in the project) instead of local disk, or mount a persistent volume.
- **[medium]** Async upload endpoints block the event loop with sync file + DB I/O — `backend/app/routers/files.py L114-142, 206-243`
  - upload_logo and upload_photo are declared `async def` but call path.write_bytes(contents) (synchronous disk I/O of up to 4-6 MB) and synchronous SQLAlchemy queries/commit (db is a sync Session from database.py). Inside an async endpoint these run directly on the event loop thread, stalling all other requests for the duration of each upload. Either make these endpoints plain `def` (so Starlette runs them in the threadpool) or offload the blocking work via run_in_threadpool / async DB. Note the rest of the router's blocking endpoints (qr_png, brochure_pdf, get_logo, etc.) are correctly plain def.
- **[low]** Gallery `order` collisions after deleting a middle photo — `backend/app/routers/files.py L220-239`
  - upload_photo sets order=count where count is the current row count. After deleting a non-last photo (orders 0,1,2 -> delete order 1 -> count becomes 2), the next upload gets order=2, colliding with the surviving order=2 row. There is no unique constraint (business_photo.py:45 explicitly allows this), so it's silent, and the list query's created_at tiebreaker keeps output deterministic. Impact is limited to confusing/duplicate order values that can desync any client-side reorder logic. Fix: compute next order as max(order)+1 for the business, or coalesce(max,-1)+1, instead of using count.
- **[low]** Non-atomic photo-count cap check allows exceeding MAX_PHOTOS under concurrency — `backend/app/routers/files.py L220-241`
  - The `count >= MAX_PHOTOS_PER_BUSINESS` check and the subsequent insert/commit are not in a single transaction with locking, so two concurrent uploads for the same business can both read count=9 and both insert, ending with 11 photos. Low real-world likelihood (a single owner uploading), and no security impact, but the documented cap can be violated. Fix: enforce with a SELECT ... FOR UPDATE on the business row before counting, or a DB-side constraint/trigger.
  - ✅ Работает: Path-traversal is correctly blocked in get_logo/get_photo: rejects when os.path.basename(filename) != filename or contains / or \ before touching the filesystem.; Ownership scoping is enforced via get_owned_business / get_owned_business_download deps, and delete_photo additionally filters by business_id so one owner cannot delete another's photo.; Upload validation is solid: content_type allow-list, max-byte cap, and empty-file rejection, with extension derived from a trusted MIME->ext map rather than user-supplied filename.; Filenames are generated as uuid4().hex + safe extension, so public file-serving endpoints (intentionally unauthenticated, used by bot/landing) are not enumerable.; Deletes commit the DB change first, then unlink the file and swallow OSError, so DB stays the source of truth and a missing/locked file won't 500 the request.; Literal public routes (/logos/{filename}, /photos/{filename}) are registered before /{slug}/photos, so Starlette ordered matching prevents the catch-all slug route from shadowing them.

### `router:geo` — working (0 находок)
_A tiny public reference-data router exposing Uzbekistan's administrative divisions: GET /api/geo/viloyats returns all regions, and GET /api/geo/tumans?viloyat=X returns districts for a region (404 if unknown). It is backed by a static in-memory dict in app/utils/uz_geo.py, with no DB, auth, or user-scoped data. Verdict: correct and working end-to-end; intentionally public lookup data, so the absence of authz/validation/scoping is appropriate. No defects found._
  - ✅ Работает: Router is registered in main.py at line 156 (app.include_router(geo.router, prefix="/api")), so endpoints are reachable at /api/geo/*.; /tumans correctly validates input: list_tumans returns [] for an unknown viloyat (dict.get default), and `if not items` raises a 404 'Unknown viloyat' rather than returning an empty list silently.; Data exposed is non-sensitive static geographic reference data (regions/districts), so no auth, ownership scoping, or rate-limited validation is required — the public design is appropriate.; No async/DB usage at all; sync handlers are fine for FastAPI (run in threadpool) and there is no I/O to await, so no async misuse risk.; Return types are correctly annotated as list[str] matching the actual returns from list_viloyats/list_tumans, giving accurate response schemas.

### `router:promo` — working (3 находок)
_Promo-code router providing owner-scoped CRUD (list/create/toggle/delete) plus two validate endpoints (one public-by-slug, one authenticated). It is consistently synchronous, matching the sync get_db session factory, so there is no async/await misuse. Ownership is correctly enforced everywhere via get_owned_business and explicit business_id == business.id filters, and the actual uses_count increment (the integrity-critical, race-prone part) lives in booking_service._apply_promo using with_for_update(), not in this file. Verdict: the area appears to work end-to-end and is largely solid; only minor validation/consistency nits, no serious defects._
- **[low]** min_length on code is bypassable via whitespace — `backend/app/routers/promo.py L49,97`
  - PromoCreate enforces code: Field(min_length=2) on the RAW input, but the handler then does body.code.strip().upper(). An input like " a" (2 chars) passes Pydantic validation yet becomes the 1-character code "A" after stripping. The empty-string guard on line 98 (`if not code`) only catches all-whitespace input, not short-after-strip. Result: codes shorter than the intended minimum can be created. Fix: normalize first (strip/upper) then validate length, e.g. a Pydantic field_validator that strips+uppercases and re-checks 2<=len<=32, or recheck len(code) after stripping in create_promo and raise 400.
- **[low]** validate_promo lacks (uses_count or 0) guard used elsewhere — `backend/app/routers/promo.py L168`
  - The authenticated validate_promo computes `p.uses_count >= p.max_uses` directly, whereas validate_promo_public (line 39) and booking_service defensively use `(p.uses_count or 0)`. The model column has default=0 and is not nullable, so in practice uses_count is never None, making this benign today; but it is an inconsistent invariant that would raise a TypeError if a row ever had a NULL uses_count (e.g. via raw SQL/migration backfill). Fix: use `(p.uses_count or 0)` for consistency with the rest of the codebase.
- **[low]** create_promo relies on app-level dup check instead of catching the unique constraint — `backend/app/routers/promo.py L102`
  - Duplicate detection does a SELECT (business_id+code) then INSERT. There is a DB UniqueConstraint uq_promo_biz_code (business_id, code) backing it, so data integrity is safe, but two concurrent create requests for the same code can both pass the SELECT and the second INSERT will raise an IntegrityError that surfaces as an unhandled 500 instead of the intended 400 "Code already exists". Low impact (same owner racing themselves) but the error handling is wrong. Fix: wrap db.commit() in try/except IntegrityError -> db.rollback() -> raise HTTPException(400, "Code already exists").
  - ✅ Работает: Ownership scoping is correct on every owner endpoint: list/toggle/delete/create all filter by business_id == business.id (from get_owned_business), so cross-tenant access of another business's promo codes is not possible.; Sync DB usage is consistent with the sync get_db/SessionLocal session factory (database.py uses create_engine + Session, not async), so the non-async handlers are correct, not a bug.; Public validate endpoint correctly filters Business.is_active and PromoCode.is_active and only returns code + discount fields (no internal data like uses_count/business_id leaked).; The race-prone uses_count increment is intentionally NOT in this router; it lives in booking_service._apply_promo with .with_for_update() row locking, so the validate endpoints being non-atomic read-only checks is acceptable by design.; Discount inputs are validated at the schema layer (discount_percent ge=0 le=100, discount_amount ge=0, max_uses ge=0) and create_promo rejects the zero/zero case.; Code normalization (strip().upper()) is applied consistently on both create and all validate paths, so stored and looked-up codes match.

### `router:reviews` — working (2 находок)
_backend/app/routers/reviews.py exposes four endpoints: a public POST /reviews that authenticates the author via Telegram WebApp initData and upserts a review for a booking the client owns; an owner-only GET /business/me/reviews list; an owner-only summary; and a public per-slug rating summary. Ownership scoping is sound (booking->client->telegram_id match for writes; get_owned_business for owner reads; slug+is_active for the public read), validation of rating is enforced via Pydantic, and timezone handling on created_at is correct. The flow works end-to-end. The main defects are a concurrency race on first-time review insert (unhandled IntegrityError -> 500) and a duplicate per-review N+1/extra query, both non-fatal._
- **[medium]** Race on first-time review insert raises unhandled IntegrityError (500) — `backend/app/routers/reviews.py L64-81`
  - submit_review does a check-then-insert: it queries for an existing Review by booking_id (line 64) and, if none, INSERTs a new row (lines 72-81). Migration 011 enforces a partial unique index uq_reviews_booking_id_when_set on booking_id WHERE booking_id IS NOT NULL. Two concurrent POSTs for the same booking (e.g. a double-tap in the WebApp) both see existing=None, both attempt INSERT, and the second commit raises sqlalchemy.exc.IntegrityError. There is no try/except around db.commit(), so the user gets an opaque 500 and the request fails instead of behaving like the intended idempotent upsert. Fix: wrap the insert commit in try/except IntegrityError, db.rollback(), then re-query the existing review and update it (or use PostgreSQL INSERT ... ON CONFLICT DO UPDATE on the partial unique index).
- **[low]** Redundant client re-query after upsert duplicates work already needed — `backend/app/routers/reviews.py L51-91`
  - The handler queries the booking's client once at line 51-55 to authorize the write, then for the response it issues a second identical query for the same client at lines 88-91 (db.query(Client).filter(Client.id == review.client_id)). Since review.client_id == booking.client_id, the already-loaded `client` object holds first_name/last_name. The second round-trip is unnecessary. Fix: reuse the `client` already fetched at line 52 to build client_name instead of re-querying.
  - ✅ Работает: Rating bounds enforced declaratively via Pydantic Field(ge=1, le=5).; Write authorization is properly scoped: the booking's client is loaded and its telegram_id is compared to the initData-derived author id (line 56), so a user cannot review another user's booking.; Owner read endpoints use get_owned_business which scopes by owner_id, and queries filter Review.business_id == business.id, so no cross-tenant leakage.; Public summary endpoint deliberately returns only average/count (no comment text or client names) and filters on is_active, matching its documented intent.; comment is trimmed and truncated to 2000 chars server-side before persistence, so the unbounded ReviewCreate.comment cannot bloat storage.; created_at default is tz-aware UTC and serialized via isoformat with a None guard; no naive/aware mixing.

### `router:schedule` — working (4 находок)
_A small, synchronous (sync SQLAlchemy Session) CRUD router under /business/me for weekly working-hours schedule and holiday dates. All five endpoints are correctly scoped to the caller's owned business via get_owned_business (owner_id == user.id), and the delete-holiday and put-schedule paths filter by business_id, so cross-tenant access/leakage is prevented. It appears to work end-to-end for the happy path. The defects are missing input validation that can surface as unhandled IntegrityErrors (500s) and a few data-integrity gaps._
- **[medium]** Duplicate day_of_week in PUT /schedule causes unhandled IntegrityError (500) — `backend/app/routers/schedule.py L61-81`
  - SchedulePut.days is a free list of ScheduleItem and there is no de-duplication or validation that day_of_week values are unique. The Schedule model has UniqueConstraint('business_id','day_of_week', name='uq_schedule_business_day') (backend/app/models/schedule.py:13). If a client sends two items with the same day_of_week, db.commit() raises sqlalchemy IntegrityError, which is not caught -> 500 with a DB error rather than a 400. Fix: validate uniqueness of day_of_week in SchedulePut (e.g. a pydantic model_validator rejecting duplicates) and return 400, or upsert per day.
- **[medium]** No validation that end_time > start_time / break ordering / break within hours — `backend/app/routers/schedule.py L15-21`
  - ScheduleItem accepts any start_time/end_time and any break_start/break_end with no cross-field checks. A schedule with end_time <= start_time, break_end <= break_start, or a break outside working hours is persisted as-is. Downstream slot/availability generation will then produce empty or nonsensical booking windows (e.g. negative interval), silently breaking customer booking for that day. Fix: add a pydantic model_validator enforcing start_time < end_time when is_working, and (break_start is None) == (break_end is None) with break_start < break_end and the break contained in [start_time, end_time].
- **[low]** reason has no max_length; long value can exceed String(255) and 500 — `backend/app/routers/schedule.py L28-30`
  - HolidayCreate.reason: str = '' has no length bound, but HolidayDate.reason is String(255) (backend/app/models/schedule.py:37). On Postgres a reason longer than 255 chars raises a DataError/StringDataRightTruncation at commit in add_holiday, surfacing as an uncaught 500. Fix: constrain with Field(max_length=255) (and ideally strip).
- **[low]** Duplicate holidays for the same date are silently allowed — `backend/app/routers/schedule.py L97-107`
  - HolidayDate has no unique constraint on (business_id, date) (see backend/app/models/schedule.py:29-39), and add_holiday performs an unconditional insert. Posting the same date twice creates two rows, so the holidays list and any availability logic that checks 'is this date a holiday' may double-count or show duplicate entries in the UI. Fix: add a UniqueConstraint('business_id','date') and/or check-existing-before-insert returning the existing row (idempotent upsert).
  - ✅ Работает: Every endpoint is ownership-scoped: get_owned_business resolves the business by owner_id == user.id, and all queries filter by business.id, so there is no cross-tenant read/write/delete.; DELETE /holidays/{id} correctly filters by both id AND business_id before deleting and returns 404 when not found, preventing IDOR/cross-tenant deletion and avoiding leaking existence of other tenants' holidays.; day_of_week is validated with Field(ge=0, le=6), rejecting out-of-range weekday values.; PUT /schedule's delete-then-insert runs inside a single transaction committed once, so a full replace is atomic (no partial state visible to other transactions).; list_holidays uses an explicit order_by(date.asc()) for stable output, and HolidayOut uses from_attributes so ORM rows serialize cleanly.; Sync SQLAlchemy usage (Session.query/.commit/.refresh) is internally consistent with get_db and the deps module — no mixed async/sync misuse in this file.

### `router:services` — working (3 находок)
_CRUD router for a business's services (list/create/update/delete/toggle-active) under /business/me/services. Every endpoint is gated by get_owned_business and consistently scopes queries by business_id, so ownership isolation is solid and the core flow works end-to-end. The main gaps are missing numeric input validation (price, price_max, duration_minutes) that can produce negative money values, inverted price ranges, and zero/negative durations that corrupt scheduling._
- **[medium]** duration_minutes accepts 0 / negative, corrupting scheduling — `backend/app/routers/services.py L19,32`
  - ServiceCreate.duration_minutes (default 30) and ServiceUpdate.duration_minutes have no bounds. The value flows directly into timedelta(minutes=service.duration_minutes) in booking_service.py:185 (end-time) and bookings.py:159/568 and into get_available_slots (slots.py:64). A 0 makes every booking zero-length so conflict detection never blocks overlaps (double-booking); a negative value makes booking end < start, producing nonsense windows. Fix: duration_minutes: int = Field(default=30, gt=0, le=1440) on create and Field(default=None, gt=0, le=1440) on update.
- **[medium]** price / price_max accept negative values and inverted ranges — `backend/app/routers/services.py L16,17,29,30`
  - price and price_max (both create and update) have no ge=0 constraint, so negative prices are persisted and shown to clients / used in loyalty discount math. There is also no check that price_max >= price, so a service can have a max lower than its base price, producing an inverted/garbage price range in the public listing. Fix: price: int = Field(default=0, ge=0); price_max: int | None = Field(default=None, ge=0); add a model_validator ensuring price_max is None or >= price (apply equivalently on ServiceUpdate).
- **[low]** Hard delete of a service silently nulls out historical bookings — `backend/app/routers/services.py L104-115`
  - delete_service performs a hard db.delete(s). The bookings.service_id FK is ondelete=SET NULL (booking.py:30), so deleting a service that has past/future bookings sets their service_id to NULL, losing the record of which service those appointments/history were for (reporting, loyalty counts, PDFs that read s.duration_minutes/name). The waitlist FK is CASCADE, so pending waitlist entries for that service are silently deleted too. Consider soft-delete (the model already has is_active / the toggle endpoint) or blocking deletion when bookings exist, instead of destroying historical linkage.
  - ✅ Работает: Every endpoint scopes the query by business_id AND filters via get_owned_business, so a user can never read or mutate another business's services (no IDOR) — update/delete/toggle all use .filter(Service.id==service_id, Service.business_id==business.id).; 404 is correctly raised before mutation when the service is not found or not owned (update/delete/toggle).; create_service hardcodes business_id=business.id from the authenticated dep rather than trusting client input, preventing cross-tenant writes.; update_service uses model_dump(exclude_unset=True) so PATCH-style partial updates only touch supplied fields and won't blank out omitted columns.; name length (1..255) and loyalty_after_visits (0..50) are validated with Field constraints.; DB layer is synchronous (sync Session, sync def endpoints, sync get_db) consistently throughout, so there is no async/await misuse here despite the stack description.

### `router:staff` — working (2 находок)
_Owner-side CRUD for staff plus a public listing for clients. It uses synchronous SQLAlchemy Session (consistent with get_db/get_owned_business deps, not async despite the project's async stack elsewhere). Ownership scoping is correct: every owner endpoint filters by business_id from get_owned_business, and assign_services validates that service ids belong to the same business. The router appears functional end-to-end; only minor data-leak/efficiency issues exist._
- **[low]** N+1 query loading staff.services in list endpoints — `backend/app/routers/staff.py L62, 77, 220`
  - _serialize() and public_list_staff iterate s.services for every staff row, but neither list_staff (line 71-77) nor public_list_staff (line 209-223) eager-loads the relationship. With the default lazy='select' relationship (models/staff.py line 84), each staff row triggers a separate SELECT against staff_services/services, i.e. N+1 queries per list call. Fix: add .options(selectinload(Staff.services)) to both list queries so services load in one extra query regardless of staff count.
- **[low]** Public staff list leaks ids of inactive services — `backend/app/routers/staff.py L220`
  - public_list_staff returns service_ids straight from s.services with no is_active filter (Service has is_active, models/service.py line 22). A service the owner deactivated still appears in a staff member's service_ids on the public/bot picker, so a client could attempt to book a disabled service. Unless the downstream booking flow independently rejects inactive services, this is an inconsistency. Fix: filter [str(svc.id) for svc in s.services if svc.is_active] in the public serializer (keep the owner serializer unfiltered so owners can still see/manage assignments).
  - ✅ Работает: Ownership scoping is correct on every owner endpoint: get/update/toggle/delete/assign all filter Staff.business_id == business.id, so one owner cannot read or mutate another business's staff (lines 73, 108, 128, 147, 177).; assign_services properly validates that every supplied service id belongs to the caller's business and rejects unknown/foreign ids via the len(services) != len(set(...)) check (lines 184-193), preventing cross-tenant service attachment; using set() also correctly handles duplicate ids in the request.; Pydantic input validation is reasonable: name min_length=1/max_length=255, phone/photo_url length caps, and StaffUpdate uses exclude_unset so PATCH-style partial updates only touch provided fields (lines 27-38, 113).; StaffUpdate intentionally omits is_active, so the PUT setattr loop cannot flip activation state arbitrarily; toggling is confined to the dedicated /toggle endpoint.; delete_staff's reliance on ondelete=SET NULL is accurate — Booking.staff_id is defined with ForeignKey(ondelete='SET NULL') (models/booking.py line 41-42), so deleting a staff member safely nulls existing bookings rather than cascading-deleting them.; Public list correctly restricts to active businesses (Business.is_active) and active staff (Staff.is_active), and returns a trimmed projection without phone/order, avoiding exposure of internal fields to clients (lines 200-223).

### `router:subscription` — working (2 находок)
_A small two-endpoint router for subscription billing: GET /subscription returns the caller's active subscription, POST /subscription/upgrade creates a PENDING payment transaction with payme/click and returns a payment URL. Authz and ownership scoping are correct (every query is bound to the owned business via get_owned_business), input validation via Pydantic enum + regex is solid, and sync Session/sync-service usage is consistent (no async/await misuse). It works end-to-end, but the status endpoint can report lapsed subscriptions as still active because it trusts the status column without checking expiry._
- **[medium]** GET /subscription reports expired subscriptions as ACTIVE (stale status, no expiry check) — `backend/app/routers/subscription.py L38-50`
  - The query filters only on status == SubscriptionStatus.ACTIVE and orders by expires_at desc, but never checks Subscription.expires_at > now. Nothing in the codebase flips a lapsed subscription's status from ACTIVE to EXPIRED on a schedule — the only place EXPIRED is set is activate_subscription (payment_service.py:45), which runs only when a NEW payment supersedes the old sub. So a subscription that has passed its expires_at but was never superseded stays status=ACTIVE in the DB, and this endpoint returns it as a live active subscription (with a past expires_at). Every other reader of 'active' subscriptions adds the expiry guard (booking_service.py:85, admin.py:98/166/444, and even refund_transaction at payment_service.py:255), so this endpoint is the inconsistent one and will mislead the dashboard/gating logic. Fix: add .filter(Subscription.expires_at > datetime.now(timezone.utc)) to the query (matching the other readers), and/or return 404/expired when expires_at has passed.
- **[low]** POST /upgrade has no dedup/idempotency — unlimited PENDING transactions — `backend/app/routers/subscription.py L53-69`
  - Each call to /upgrade unconditionally creates a new PaymentTransaction in PENDING state (create_payme_payment / create_click_payment always db.add a fresh row, then the router commits). Repeated clicks or retries from the WebApp generate an unbounded number of dangling PENDING transactions for the same business/plan, cluttering the table and complicating reconciliation. Fix: before creating, reuse or expire any recent PENDING transaction for the same business+provider+plan, or add a short-window dedup so a rapid retry returns the existing transaction/URL instead of minting a new one.
  - ✅ Работает: Ownership scoping is correct: both endpoints depend on get_owned_business, which scopes to Business.owner_id == user.id, so a caller can only see/upgrade their own business's subscription — no IDOR.; Auth is enforced through the get_current_user -> get_owned_business chain (bearer token, active-user check) before any handler runs.; Input validation is solid: plan is a SubscriptionPlan enum and provider is constrained by regex ^(payme|click)$ at the Pydantic layer, rejecting bad input with 422 before the handler.; Async usage is consistent — sync Session, sync deps, and sync service functions throughout; no blocking-in-async or missing-await bugs.; expires_at is stored as DateTime(timezone=True), so the .isoformat() serialization yields a correct offset-aware timestamp (no naive-datetime/timezone bug).; db.commit() is called after the service builds the transaction, and a missing payment URL (unconfigured credentials) is surfaced as a 500 rather than returning an empty URL to the client.

### `service:booking_service` — working (7 находок)
_Synchronous SQLAlchemy service backing the public booking flow: validates business/service/staff, checks subscription and client block list, serializes concurrent writers on a slot via a Postgres transaction-scoped advisory lock, detects overlap conflicts, applies promo codes and a loyalty stamp-card discount, and creates the Booking. Also handles cancel/confirm. Core logic is coherent and the advisory-lock approach to the empty-slot race is genuinely sound. Verdict: works end-to-end, but has several real defects around the loyalty/promo interaction, promo concurrency, and the loyalty boundary counting that can produce wrong prices or free-booking exploits._
- **[high]** Loyalty discount counts only COMPLETED visits, but free booking is granted at create time — exploitable / wrong cadence — `backend/app/services/booking_service.py L258-282`
  - _maybe_apply_loyalty computes next_visit = COMPLETED count + 1 and grants a 100% discount (price 0) at the moment of booking creation, before the visit is completed.
