Because only COMPLETED bookings are counted, a client can repeatedly create bookings on the boundary: e.g. with loyalty_after_visits=5 and 4 completed visits, EVERY new booking the client creates is priced 0 (each create sees completed=4 -> next_visit=5 -> free), since pending/confirmed creates never increment the completed count. A client can spam multiple free bookings simultaneously, and if any later visit is marked completed the cadence is also off. Fix: either grant the stamp based on the count of already-completed visits being an exact multiple at completion time (award the free visit when the Nth visit is completed, not when the (N)th is booked), or guard against multiple outstanding pending/confirmed free bookings by also counting PENDING/CONFIRMED toward next_visit when deciding the boundary.
- **[medium]** Promo uses_count incremented even when loyalty made the booking free — `backend/app/services/booking_service.py L227-254`
  - _apply_promo returns (final_price, promo) and increments promo.uses_count at line 253-254 whenever a valid promo was matched. But _maybe_apply_loyalty can override final_price to 0 (free) afterward, in which case the client paid nothing yet a limited-use promo is still burned. Worse, the discount stacking is order-dependent and the promo's monetary effect is silently discarded while still consuming a use against max_uses. Fix: only increment promo.uses_count when the promo actually changed the price (i.e. loyalty did not zero it out), or compute loyalty first and skip promo when the booking is already free.
- **[medium]** Promo redemption race: max_uses can be exceeded under concurrency despite FOR UPDATE — `backend/app/services/booking_service.py L312-327, 253-254`
  - _apply_promo selects the PromoCode with with_for_update() and checks uses_count >= max_uses, but the uses_count increment happens later in create_booking (line 253-254) on the same row. The FOR UPDATE row lock does serialize concurrent transactions on that promo row, so this is mostly safe — HOWEVER the increment reads promo.uses_count from the in-session ORM object ((promo.uses_count or 0) + 1) rather than an atomic SQL UPDATE ... SET uses_count = uses_count + 1. If the loaded value is stale relative to a committed concurrent change that occurred between load and this transaction's lock acquisition it is fine, but combined with the validate_promo_for_business read path (no lock, line 335-343) used by the bot UI there is a check-then-act gap from the user's perspective. Lower-risk than it looks because of FOR UPDATE, but prefer an atomic increment to remove any reliance on the loaded value. Fix: use db.execute(update(PromoCode).where(...).values(uses_count=PromoCode.uses_count+1)).
- **[medium]** Naive datetime overlap comparison mixes date+time without timezone; correct only if all bookings use the same wall-clock convention — `backend/app/services/booking_service.py L184-185, 207-209`
  - start_dt/end_dt are built with datetime.combine on naive local date/time and end_dt.time() is stored as end_time. The overlap check in _check_slot_available compares start_time/end_time as naive times within a single date. A booking that crosses midnight (start_time late, duration_minutes pushing end past 00:00) yields end_dt on the NEXT day, but only end_dt.time() is stored (the date rolls over and is lost), so end_time < start_time. The overlap predicate (Booking.start_time < end_time AND Booking.end_time > payload.start_time) then breaks for midnight-crossing bookings: such a booking will fail to register conflicts correctly and may be double-booked or wrongly considered free. Fix: reject or specially handle bookings whose end crosses midnight, or store full datetimes and compare on datetimes.
- **[low]** Money math floor-division can produce 0% discount surprise and order-dependent rounding — `backend/app/services/booking_service.py L326, 348`
  - discount = base_price * percent // 100 + amount uses integer floor division. This is acceptable for UZS (integer currency) but means percent discounts always round in the customer's favor downward; combined with discount_amount the two are summed then clamped with max(0, ...). Not a bug per se, but validate_promo_for_business (line 348) and _apply_promo (line 326) duplicate the exact formula — if one is ever changed the bot preview and the actual charge diverge silently. Fix: extract a single shared discount() helper so preview and charge can never drift.
- **[low]** get_or_create_client updates existing client fields but the block check runs against a separately fetched Client row — `backend/app/services/booking_service.py L164-211`
  - create_booking queries Client by telegram_id three separate times (blocking_client at 164, existing_client at 189, and again inside get_or_create_client at 56). These are redundant round-trips (minor N+1) and rely on identity-map dedup within the session. Functionally fine but wasteful; consolidate into one lookup reused across the block check, idempotency check, and get_or_create.
- **[low]** MD5-truncated advisory lock key risks rare cross-slot collisions — `backend/app/services/booking_service.py L25-27`
  - _slot_lock_key_for hashes (business, date, start) and truncates to 31 bits. Two different slots can collide on the same advisory key, causing unnecessary serialization (not incorrectness — collisions only over-lock, never under-lock). Acceptable, but worth noting the lock is keyed on start_time only; two overlapping bookings with DIFFERENT start_times (e.g. 10:00 90-min vs 11:00) hash to different keys and do NOT serialize via the advisory lock. They still rely on _check_slot_available's FOR UPDATE, which cannot lock a not-yet-existing row — so the empty-slot race the advisory lock was designed to close is only closed for identical start_times, not for overlapping-but-offset starts. Fix: key the advisory lock on business+date only (coarser but correct), or otherwise serialize all writers on the same business/day.
  - ✅ Работает: Advisory-lock approach (pg_advisory_xact_lock) correctly addresses the empty-slot insert race that SELECT FOR UPDATE cannot cover, with a clean SQLite no-op fallback for tests.; Idempotent re-creation: an identical (client, business, date, start_time) pending/confirmed booking is returned instead of erroring, handling double-clicks/retries.; Overlap conflict query uses correct half-open interval logic (start < end AND end > start) and properly scopes per-staff vs per-business.; Subscription expiry check uses timezone-aware UTC comparison (datetime.now(timezone.utc) vs expires_at).; Client block list is enforced with a generic non-revealing error message.; ConfirmationMode parsing is defensively wrapped with a fallback to AUTO on bad enum values.

### `service:pdf_service` — working (0 находок)
_backend/app/services/pdf_service.py renders a single-page A5 PDF brochure for a business (cover, QR card, services list, contacts, footer) using reportlab, and generates the QR code (deep link to the Telegram bot). It is pure presentation/rendering code: no DB transactions, no money arithmetic beyond integer thousands-formatting, no timezone math beyond formatting time objects, and no runtime external network calls. It is defensively coded (try/except around all image draws, ASCII sanitization, autosizing/truncation). It appears to work end-to-end and is exercised by build_brochure_pdf from the /brochure router. No real defects in correctness, concurrency, money, or error handling were found._
  - ✅ Работает: _logo_reader (lines 16-22) and every c.drawImage call (logo line 160, QR line 203) are wrapped in try/except so a corrupt/missing image degrades gracefully (text fallback for logo, white rect for QR) instead of 500-ing the brochure endpoint.; _format_price (lines 87-92) is robust: coerces None/bad values to 0 via try/except, and DB Service.price is Integer so no float-rounding concern; thousands grouping with space separator is locale-correct for UZ.; _ascii_safe (lines 54-67) maps Uzbek/typographic glyphs (ʻ ' ' " " — – …) to WinAnsi-safe equivalents, preventing Helvetica from rendering tofu/boxes for the Latin-Uzbek alphabet.; _format_schedule (lines 319-366) defensively validates day_of_week bounds (0-6) and skips rows with missing start/end times or is_working=False before indexing DAY_ABBR_UZ, so it cannot IndexError on malformed schedule rows.; Services list is capped at 6 rows (line 219) and names are truncated/clamped (max(name_max_w, 10*mm), line 266), so unbounded or extreme data cannot overflow the fixed A5 layout.; build_brochure_pdf filters to is_active services (line 384) and the schedules relationship is accessed via getattr on a synchronous Session in the router (files.py), so the lazy-load is safe (no async MissingGreenlet) and produces correct output.

### `service:qr_service` — working (0 находок)
_qr_service.py is a small, pure image-generation utility: it renders a deep-link QR code (https://t.me/{bot}?start={slug}) using a hand-rolled rounded-module PIL renderer with H-level error correction and an embedded brand logo, returning PNG bytes. There is no database access, money math, timezone handling, transactions, or external network I/O here, so most audit dimensions do not apply. End-to-end it works: callers in routers/files.py and pdf_service.py pass a slug and bot username and receive valid PNG bytes; the lru_cache layers correctly key on (slug, bot_username) and the fallback bot name resolves consistently. I found no real defects._
  - ✅ Работает: Cache key for _generate_qr_cached is (business_slug, bot_username), so renaming a slug yields a new key and a fresh QR rather than a stale image; the router also sets Cache-Control: no-store.; generate_qr normalizes a None/empty bot_username to the same default ('Yozuv_cl_bot') before reaching the cached function, so cache entries don't fragment between None and the literal default.; functools.lru_cache is thread-safe, and the QR endpoint is a sync (def) FastAPI route run in the threadpool, so concurrent calls into the cached generators are safe; no shared mutable state is mutated without protection.; _logo_plate handles a missing or unreadable logo file gracefully (returns None), and _render_qr correctly skips logo embedding when None, so QR generation never crashes on a missing asset.; Error correction is set to ERROR_CORRECT_H and the embedded logo area is ~22% of the QR side, within H-level (~30%) tolerance, so the code should remain scannable.; qr.make(fit=True) with version=None auto-sizes the matrix to the data length, so longer slugs won't overflow a fixed version.

### `service:waitlist_service` — working (3 находок)
_Two small synchronous-ORM write paths: `join` registers a client's interest in a full (business, service, date, start_time) slot, and `notify_first_for_slot` pulls the oldest non-notified waitlist entry for a slot after a cancellation and marks it notified. In normal single-request operation both work correctly end-to-end (verified callers in routers/bookings.py and bot/handlers/booking.py, plus the WaitlistEntry/Client models). Verdict: working for the happy path, but it relies on DB constraints rather than code for idempotency and has unguarded check-then-write races under concurrency that can cause 500s or double-notifications._
- **[high]** notify_first_for_slot has a read-modify-write race (double notification / skipped client) — `backend/app/services/waitlist_service.py L96-121`
  - The head-of-queue entry is selected with a plain SELECT (ORDER BY created_at LIMIT 1, notified_at IS NULL) and only later has notified_at set; there is no row lock (no `.with_for_update()`) and no atomic UPDATE...RETURNING. Two concurrent cancellations of the same slot (e.g. two staff cancelling overlapping bookings, or a retry) can both read the same head entry before either commits, both set notified_at on it, and the same client receives two '🔔 slot ochildi' Telegram messages while the second waiting client is never pinged. The router (bookings.py:369-388) commits then sends, so the duplicate send is fully exposed. Fix: lock the candidate row, e.g. `q.order_by(...).with_for_update(skip_locked=True).first()`, or replace the select+assign with a single atomic statement (UPDATE waitlist_entries SET notified_at=now() WHERE id = (SELECT id ... FOR UPDATE SKIP LOCKED) RETURNING ...). SKIP LOCKED also lets concurrent cancellations correctly hand the slot to distinct waiting clients.
- **[medium]** join is not idempotent in code — concurrent identical joins raise IntegrityError (500) — `backend/app/services/waitlist_service.py L58-81`
  - The docstring claims the operation is 'strictly idempotent thanks to the unique constraint', but the Python path is check-then-insert: it SELECTs an existing entry, and if none is found INSERTs a new one. The uq_waitlist_unique_entry constraint guarantees data integrity but NOT a clean idempotent response — two concurrent calls for the same (business, service, date, start_time, client) both find nothing and both insert; the second commit raises IntegrityError, surfacing as an unhandled 500 in /waitlist/join (bookings.py:440-451) rather than returning the existing entry. Fix: wrap the insert/flush in a try/except IntegrityError that rolls back to a savepoint and re-queries the existing row, returning it (true upsert semantics).
- **[medium]** First-time client creation in join races on the unique telegram_id constraint — `backend/app/services/waitlist_service.py L45-56`
  - Client is resolved with SELECT-by-telegram_id then INSERT if missing. clients.telegram_id is declared unique (app/models/client.py:24-26), so two concurrent first-time joins (or a join racing a first-time booking) both see no client and both INSERT, and the second flush/commit raises IntegrityError → unhandled 500. The bot batch caller (bot/handlers/booking.py:391-402) makes this more likely: it loops join() many times for one user, but only the first iteration matters here. Fix: catch IntegrityError on the client insert and re-select the row (or reuse booking_service.get_or_create_client which the model comments reference as the canonical path, so the same hardening lives in one place).
  - ✅ Работает: Slot-level idempotency is correctly backed by a real composite unique constraint (uq_waitlist_unique_entry on business_id, service_id, date, start_time, client_id) and the existing-entry SELECT returns the prior row in the common single-request case.; notify-once semantics are sound: notified_at is set (and committed by the caller before the Telegram send at bookings.py:377) so a subsequent cancellation of the same slot won't re-pick the same entry; a flaky send won't un-mark it.; Stale-row handling is defensive: if client/business/service rows are missing, the entry is marked notified and None returned instead of crashing or NPE-ing on .name (line 114-118).; Telegram side-effects are intentionally kept out of the service so the cancel transaction isn't coupled to a flaky HTTP call, and the router swallows post-commit notify failures so the cancel itself is never rolled back (bookings.py:389-393).; Timestamps are timezone-aware UTC (datetime.now(timezone.utc)) and the column is DateTime(timezone=True); no naive/aware mixing. No money math is involved in this module, so no rounding concerns.; The /waitlist/join router validates that the service actually belongs to the requested business before calling join (bookings.py:428-438), closing the cross-tenant 'park an entry on a stranger's calendar' gap noted in the comment.

### `task:backup` — working (3 находок)
_backend/app/tasks/backup.py is a Celery beat task that nightly dumps the entire DB to JSON (same shape as the admin /backup/export endpoint), uploads it to an S3-compatible bucket via boto3, and prunes objects older than the retention window. It is correctly gated to a no-op when BACKUP_S3_BUCKET is blank, uses a sync SQLAlchemy session consistent with the rest of the Celery worker, and handles upload/prune failures without crashing the task. It appears to work end-to-end for typical text/numeric data. The main weaknesses are around backup *fidelity/consistency* rather than the upload mechanics: the dump is not taken in a single consistent snapshot, and the bytes serialization is lossy (latent, since binary columns were removed in this WIP branch)._
- **[high]** DB dump is not a consistent snapshot (READ COMMITTED across many statements) — `backend/app/tasks/backup.py L61-70`
  - _build_dump() reads each table with a separate db.execute(select(table)) statement on a default-isolation (READ COMMITTED) Postgres session. Under READ COMMITTED, every statement sees a fresh snapshot, so tables read later can include rows that reference rows that did not exist when an earlier table was read (and vice-versa). The nightly task runs at 02:30 Tashkent, but any concurrent write (a booking, a client signup, a webhook) during the dump can yield a referentially-inconsistent backup that fails or silently corrupts on restore. For a tool whose entire purpose is restore safety this is a real defect. Fix: wrap the reads in a single REPEATABLE READ (or SERIALIZABLE) transaction, e.g. db.connection(execution_options={'isolation_level': 'REPEATABLE READ'}) before the first select, or use a SET TRANSACTION ISOLATION LEVEL REPEATABLE READ at the start so all selects share one consistent snapshot. (Same issue exists in admin.backup_export at admin.py:817-819, which shares this code shape.)
- **[medium]** Lossy/irreversible serialization of binary (bytes) columns — `backend/app/tasks/backup.py L51-52`
  - _json_default serializes bytes via o.decode('utf-8', errors='replace'). For real binary data (e.g. media blobs / bytea), this corrupts bytes (errors='replace' substitutes U+FFFD) and is not reversible — and the restore side (_coerce_row in admin.py:57-78) has no bytes/base64 decoding, so even valid UTF-8 bytes would be re-inserted as a str, not bytes. The memory notes indicate logos/photos were stored in a Postgres media_blobs (bytea) table; that model is absent in this WIP snapshot (no LargeBinary columns currently exist), so the branch is not triggered today — but it is a latent data-loss path the moment any binary column is reintroduced. Fix: encode bytes with base64 (e.g. {'__b64__': base64.b64encode(o).decode('ascii')}) and add matching base64 decoding to _coerce_row on restore.
- **[low]** Backup completeness depends on fragile transitive import ordering of models — `backend/app/tasks/backup.py L56-70`
  - The dump iterates Base.metadata.sorted_tables, which only contains tables whose model modules have been imported. backup.py imports Base from app.database but never imports app.models. Today it works only because celery_app.py imports app.tasks.reminders (line 48) before app.tasks.backup (line 49), and reminders.py does 'from app.models import ...' which loads app/models/__init__.py and registers every table. If that import order changes, or backup is loaded in a context that does not pull in reminders/models first, the task would silently produce a partial or empty backup (sorted_tables incomplete) with no error. Fix: add an explicit 'import app.models  # noqa: F401' (or 'from app import models') inside backup.py before reading Base.metadata.sorted_tables so completeness does not rely on side-effect ordering.
  - ✅ Работает: Correct no-op gating: returns early with a clear status payload when backup_s3_bucket is blank, so dev environments never touch a bucket (backup.py:98-100).; S3 client init, upload, and prune are each wrapped in try/except with logger.exception and a structured status return — a failure in any stage degrades to a skipped/failed status rather than crashing the beat worker (backup.py:102-121, 166-173).; Credentials and endpoint come from settings/env (no hardcoded secrets); endpoint_url is only set when provided, correctly supporting AWS S3 / B2 / R2 / MinIO (backup.py:81-89).; Prune logic is sound: normalizes naive LastModified to UTC before comparison (backup.py:157-158), and batches deletes in chunks of 1000 to respect the S3 delete_objects hard limit (backup.py:164-171).; Object key prefix handling is correct: lstrip('/') of the prefix while preserving the trailing slash yields keys like 'yozuv/backups/auto-<ts>.json' (backup.py:110-111).; Uses a sync SQLAlchemy SessionLocal (matching the rest of the Celery worker) and closes it in a finally block — no async/await misuse and no leaked session (backup.py:61-72).

### `util:auth` — working (0 находок)
_backend/app/utils/auth.py provides password hashing/verification (bcrypt) and JWT helpers (create access/refresh tokens, decode, and resolve a User from an access token). The logic is correct and internally consistent: token type is checked, expiry is verified by jose's defaults, bcrypt 72-byte truncation is handled symmetrically in hash and verify, and error handling degrades to None/False rather than 500s. No real defects found in this file. Note: the audit focus areas of ratelimit, slot math, HTML escaping, and timezone-clock math are not implemented in this file (they live elsewhere in the codebase), so they could not be assessed here._
  - ✅ Работает: create_access_token/create_refresh_token use timezone-aware datetime.now(timezone.utc) for exp, so JWT expiry is computed in UTC correctly with no naive-datetime ambiguity (lines 41, 49).; get_user_from_token enforces payload type == 'access' (line 61), so a refresh token cannot be used as an access token; the /refresh endpoint symmetrically enforces type == 'refresh' (auth.py:426).; Password bcrypt 72-byte truncation is handled identically in hash_password and verify_password via the shared _encode helper (lines 22-23, 27, 34), avoiding the bcrypt>=4.1 'password too long' exception and keeping hash/verify consistent on the same byte slice.; verify_password returns False for a None/empty stored hash and catches ValueError/TypeError from malformed DB hashes (lines 31-37), so it never raises a 500 on bad stored data and never treats a missing hash as a match.; get_user_from_token catches both JWTError (decode/signature/expiry failures) and ValueError (invalid UUID in sub, missing sub) and returns None (lines 64-68), giving clean 401 behavior at the dependency layer instead of unhandled exceptions.; decode_token relies on jose's default verification, which validates the HS256 signature and the exp claim, so expired tokens are rejected (line 55).

### `util:clock` — working (0 находок)
_A tiny module of timezone helpers for the business clock (Asia/Tashkent). `local_now()` returns a tz-aware current datetime and `local_today()` returns the local calendar date, so server-side UTC hosting (Render) doesn't drift the displayed "today/tomorrow" by 5 hours. The logic is correct and works end-to-end._
  - ✅ Работает: local_now() correctly uses datetime.now(TZ) which returns a timezone-aware datetime in Asia/Tashkent, avoiding the UTC drift described in the docstring (clock.py:18).; local_today() correctly derives the calendar date from the localized now via local_now().date(), so the day boundary follows Tashkent time rather than UTC (clock.py:23).; ZoneInfo('Asia/Tashkent') is created once at module import as a constant (TZ), which is the correct/cheap pattern (clock.py:13).; Asia/Tashkent is a fixed +05:00 offset with no DST, so there are no ambiguous/imaginary-time edge cases to mishandle.

### `util:google_oauth` — working (2 находок)
_backend/app/utils/google_oauth.py provides minimal Google OAuth 2.0 / OIDC Authorization-Code + PKCE helpers: enablement check, callback URL, base64url, PKCE verifier/challenge, random CSRF state, auth-URL builder, code exchange, and ID-token claim parsing. The crypto primitives (PKCE S256, CSRF state entropy) are correct, and exp/iss/aud/sub validation is sound and timezone-safe. The code is called only from synchronous FastAPI routes in auth.py, so the blocking httpx.Client is acceptable. The deliberate choice to skip JWT signature verification (relying on direct TLS fetch from Google's token endpoint) is consistent with Google's documented guidance. Verdict: working, with one defensible-but-fragile security tradeoff worth hardening._
- **[low]** ID token signature is never cryptographically verified — `backend/app/utils/google_oauth.py L84`
  - parse_id_token uses jwt.get_unverified_claims and only checks iss/aud/exp/sub manually; the JWT signature is never validated. The module docstring justifies this because the token is fetched directly from Google's token endpoint over TLS (exchange_code, line 75-78), which matches Google's own guidance and is a legitimate pattern. The residual risk: this trust is entirely implicit and depends on parse_id_token only ever being fed tokens that came straight from the TLS code exchange. If parse_id_token is ever reused on a token from a less-trusted path (e.g. an APK/native flow passing an id_token from the client), an attacker could forge arbitrary claims. Suggested hardening: verify the signature against Google's JWKS (jose.jwt.decode with the fetched public keys + cached keyset), or at minimum add a clear in-code assertion/comment that this function must only receive token-endpoint-fetched tokens. Severity kept low because the current sole caller (auth.py:181) feeds it a freshly-exchanged token.
- **[low]** exp validation has no clock-skew leeway — `backend/app/utils/google_oauth.py L90`
  - int(exp) < int(time.time()) rejects tokens with zero tolerance for clock drift between the server and Google. ID tokens are freshly minted during the code exchange so this rarely bites, but a server clock running slightly ahead can spuriously reject valid logins. Fix: allow a small skew, e.g. int(exp) + 60 < int(time.time()), mirroring standard OIDC leeway.
  - ✅ Работает: make_pkce uses secrets.token_bytes(32) -> 43-char base64url verifier (within RFC 7636's 43-128 range) and a correct S256 challenge (sha256 of verifier, base64url, no padding).; random_state uses 128 bits of secrets entropy, adequate CSRF protection; state is bound to a signed cookie and re-checked in the callback (auth.py:172).; _b64url correctly strips '=' padding and produces URL-safe output, matching PKCE/OAuth expectations.; exp check uses epoch seconds on both sides (int(time.time()) vs int(exp)), so it is timezone-safe and not affected by local TZ.; iss is validated against both accepted Google issuer forms, aud is matched against the configured client_id, and a non-empty sub is required before claims are trusted.; exchange_code sends client_secret + code_verifier and calls raise_for_status(), so a failed/invalid exchange surfaces as an exception that the caller converts into a safe failure redirect.

### `util:htmlsafe` — working (0 находок)
_A 28-line helper module exposing h() (alias escape) that runs html.escape with quote=False over any value (None becomes empty string, other types via str()) before interpolation into Telegram HTML-mode messages. Its job is to neutralize HTML injection of user-controlled strings (owner welcome_text, business name, client names, phone/address) so they cannot inject clickable <a href> phishing links. It works correctly end-to-end: callers consistently wrap user-controlled values in h() and place the output as tag content, never inside an HTML attribute._
  - ✅ Работает: h() escapes the dangerous metacharacters <, >, and & via html.escape, which is exactly what is needed to prevent tag injection in Telegram HTML parse mode (line 20).; None and non-string inputs are handled safely: None maps to empty string and everything else is coerced with str() before escaping, so the function never raises on unexpected types (line 20).; The quote=False choice is safe in this codebase: a Grep across backend confirms every call site interpolates h() output as tag *content* (e.g. <b>{h(b.name)}</b>), never inside an attribute value, and because < is escaped a user cannot break out into an attribute context where unescaped " or ' would matter.; Call sites are consistent: start.py, my_bookings.py, payments.py, bookings.py, and reminders.py all wrap user-controlled fields (welcome_text, name, first_name, phone, address) in h() before sending HTML messages.; The escape alias and explicit __all__ keep the public surface minimal and intentional (lines 24, 27).

### `util:slots` — working (3 находок)
_backend/app/utils/slots.py is a small set of synchronous-Session helpers that compute bookable time slots: it reads the weekday Schedule, skips holidays and non-working days, generates 30-minute-granularity start times within the working window, and removes any slot that overlaps the break or an existing PENDING/CONFIRMED booking. The core interval-overlap math is correct and the timezone-aware local_today() is used for next_working_dates. It works end-to-end for single-resource businesses, but the availability calculation is staff-unaware and ignores business activation state, so it can mis-report availability for multi-staff or deactivated businesses._
- **[high]** Slot availability is staff-unaware while booking conflicts are per-staff (over-restrictive / inconsistent) — `backend/app/utils/slots.py L35-44, 60, 84-89`
  - get_bookings_for_date() filters existing bookings only by business_id and date, and get_available_slots() blocks a slot if it overlaps ANY of those bookings. But the authoritative conflict check in booking_service._check_slot_available (backend/app/services/booking_service.py:122-123) filters by Booking.staff_id when a staff is targeted, i.e. conflicts are per-staff. Consequence for a multi-staff business: if staff A is booked 10:00-10:30, the public /slots endpoint hides 10:00 for EVERYONE, even though staff B is free — clients are told no slot exists when one does, and the data the UI shows disagrees with what create_booking will actually accept. Fix: add an optional staff_id param to get_bookings_for_date/get_available_slots and thread it from slots_for_date (bookings.py:671); when staff_id is set, filter existing_bookings to Booking.staff_id == staff_id (treating NULL as the shared/legacy calendar) to match _check_slot_available semantics.
- **[medium]** Slots served for deactivated / soft-deleted businesses — `backend/app/utils/slots.py L47-60`
  - get_available_slots derives availability purely from Schedule/HolidayDate/Booking keyed on business_id and never checks the Business is active. The public caller slots_for_date (backend/app/routers/bookings.py:665) looks up the business by slug with no is_active / deleted_at filter, then calls get_available_slots, so a deactivated (or unsubscribed) business still exposes bookable times via the public API. Note create_booking does run _check_active_subscription, so a client could be shown slots and then fail at submit — a confusing dead-end. Fix: filter the business lookup in slots_for_date by is_active (and deleted_at if present), and/or have the slots endpoint short-circuit to [] for inactive businesses.
- **[medium]** Past time slots are offered for the current day — `backend/app/utils/slots.py L67-96`
  - For d == local_today(), the generator starts at schedule.start_time and emits every step up to end_time regardless of the current wall-clock time. local_now() is available in app.utils.clock but is not used here, and neither caller (bookings.py:671, bot/handlers/booking.py:303) filters past times, nor does create_booking reject a past start_time. Result: at 15:00 a client is still offered 09:00, 09:30, ... and can actually create a booking in the past. Fix: when d == local_today(), skip slots whose current_dt (or current_dt + duration) is <= local_now(); ideally also reject past start times in create_booking as a defensive backstop.
  - ✅ Работает: Interval-overlap logic for both breaks (line 79) and existing bookings (line 87) uses the correct standard test `not (a_end <= b_start or a_start >= b_end)`, so a long service correctly skips slots that straddle a break or booking, not just ones whose start lands inside (matches the in-code comment and the test_break_slots_excluded / test_existing_booking_blocks_slot tests).; Loop guard `while current_dt + duration <= end_dt` correctly prevents emitting a slot that would run past closing time, and yields nothing for a misconfigured schedule where start_time >= end_time (safe, no crash).; Only PENDING/CONFIRMED bookings block slots (line 41); cancelled/completed bookings correctly free the slot.; next_working_dates uses timezone-aware local_today() (Asia/Tashkent) rather than naive date.today(), avoiding the UTC day-flip drift described in clock.py, and bounds its scan with MAX_WORKING_DATE_SCAN so it can't loop forever when a business never works.; Holiday and non-working-day short-circuits return [] before any slot generation (lines 54-58).

### `util:telegram_webapp` — working (0 находок)
_This module verifies Telegram WebApp initData signatures and extracts the user object. validate_telegram_init_data implements Telegram's documented HMAC-SHA256 scheme correctly (secret = HMAC("WebAppData", bot_token), data_check_string is the alphabetically-sorted "k=v" pairs joined by newline after removing hash, compared with hmac.compare_digest), then enforces a freshness window via auth_date with both an upper TTL bound and a future-date rejection to close the replay gap. parse_user_from_init safely JSON-parses the user payload and validates the id shape. It is used by auth, bookings, and reviews routers, all of which guard for an empty bot_token and wrap calls in try/except mapping to 401. The area appears correct and secure end-to-end._
  - ✅ Работает: HMAC verification follows Telegram's spec exactly: secret_key = HMAC(b'WebAppData', bot_token), then HMAC over the newline-joined sorted k=v pairs, compared with hmac.compare_digest (constant-time) at lines 33-35 — no timing leak and no algorithm error.; hash is popped from the parsed dict (line 26) before building data_check_string, so the signature input is correct and the returned dict excludes the hash.; Replay protection is well-designed: the upper TTL bound (age > 3600) plus the future-date rejection (age < -300) at lines 46-49 together prevent a forward-dated auth_date from bypassing expiry, which a one-sided check would miss. The reasoning is documented in the comments.; parse_user_from_init (lines 54-72) defends against signed-but-malformed payloads: it catches JSON errors, verifies the result is a dict containing 'id', and pre-validates int(user['id']) so callers' int(u['id']) cannot raise an unhandled 500 — malformed input yields a clean ValueError mapped to 401.; Callers (auth.py:58-64, bookings.py, reviews.py) guard against an unconfigured bot_token (500) and wrap validation in try/except -> 401, so exceptions raised here surface as proper auth failures rather than 500s.; Missing hash, missing auth_date, and non-integer auth_date are each explicitly rejected (lines 27-28, 39-44).

### `util:uz_geo` — working (0 находок)
_backend/app/utils/uz_geo.py is a static reference module: a dict mapping Uzbekistan viloyats (and Toshkent shahri / Qoraqalpog'iston) to lists of tumans/shaharlar, plus three trivial helpers (list_viloyats, list_tumans, is_valid). It backs the /geo router and the Telegram bot's location-filter keyboards. The helpers are defensive (use .get with default, copy lists via list(), handle missing keys and empty/None tuman), and the callers guard index-based access with try/except for ValueError/IndexError. It works end-to-end. None of the listed focus areas (auth/JWT/initData, ratelimit, slot math, html escaping, timezone) live in this file._
  - ✅ Работает: list_tumans uses UZ_VILOYAT_TUMAN.get(viloyat, []) so an unknown viloyat returns an empty list instead of raising KeyError.; Both list_viloyats and list_tumans return fresh list() copies, so callers cannot mutate the underlying module-level dict.; is_valid correctly handles empty/None viloyat, unknown viloyat, and the optional tuman (treating None and "" as "no tuman specified").; The /geo/tumans router converts an unknown viloyat (empty list) into a 404 rather than returning an empty 200.; Bot callers (start.py:218-223, 287-294) wrap index lookups into list_viloyats()/list_tumans() in try/except (ValueError, IndexError), so stale or malicious callback indices cannot crash the handler.
